Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Obligation of Witr: Proofs and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Arguing that witr is wajib using hadith and rational proofs, responding to Sahibayn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that witr is wajib, explain the three deductive arguments from the hadith, and respond to Sahibayn's objections.

Core Idea
Witr is wajib because its proof is a non-definitive sunnah attributed to Allah with an imperative that indicates obligation.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents the core evidence for the wajib status of witr, a debated topic within the Hanafi school itself. While Imam Abu Hanifa held that witr is wajib (obligatory), his two illustrious students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, considered it sunnah. The commentator here not only presents the proofs for Abu Hanifa's view but also addresses and refutes the objections of the Sahibayn, establishing the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
Determine what exactly is being contested: the legal status of witr prayer. Is it wajib (as per Imam Abu Hanifa) or sunnah (as per Sahibayn)?
2
Analyze the primary dalil
Examine the hadith 'Inna Allaha zada kum salatan...' and its three lines of reasoning: attribution to Allah, increase upon limited (faraid), and imperative form (amr). Understand why each leads to wujub.
Note the Hanafi principle that al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
3
Examine Sahibayn's objections
Identify the two main objections raised by Sahibayn: the hadith of Ibn Umar praying witr on a mount (implying it is nafl), and the hadith of the Bedouin who did not mention witr among the obligatory prayers.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
Learn how the commentator (following Tahawi) refutes these objections: the mount hadith is contradicted by another narration from Ibn Umar, so both are dropped; the Bedouin hadith is abrogated by later evidence. Also, the denier of witr is not a disbeliever because the proof is zanni.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: if witr is wajib, it must be made up (qada) if missed; if sunnah, makeup is not obligatory. This distinction has real implications for a person who misses witr.

باب صلوة الوتر
دوم یہ کہ حین میں ابن عمر سے مروی ہے ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم اوتر علی البعير یعنی نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے وتر کی نماز سواری پر پڑ گیا بات ظاہر ہے کہ سواری پرنفل نماز ادا کی جاسکتی ہے نہ کہ فرض اور واجب پس اگر وتر کی نماز واجب ہوتی تو آنحضرت سواری پر نہ فرماتے۔
امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل حضور کا یہ قول ہے ان الله تعالی زادكم صلوة الا وهي الوتر فصلوهات مالك العشاء الى طلوع الفجر صاحب عنایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ اس حدیث سے چند طریقوں پر استدلال کیا گیا ہے۔ اول یہ کہ زبان ترجمہ نسبت اللہ کی طرف کی گئی ہے اور سنتوں کی نسبت رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی طرف کی جاتی پس اگر وتر کی نماز سنت ہوتی تو حدیث میں بجا۔ طرف نسبت کرنے کے رسول کی طرف نسبت کی جاتی لیکن چونکہ رسول کی طرف نسبت نہیں کی گئی اس لئے وتر کی نماز سنت نہیں ہیں چاہتے ۔ ایک قول واجب ہوگی۔
دوم یہ کہ کسی چیز پر زیادتی اسی وقت ہوتی ہے جبکہ شی مزید عليه (جس پر زیادتی کی گئی ہو محدود العد واد به مسلم ہے کہ نوافل غیر محدود ہیں ان کی کوئی انتہا نہیں پس زیادتی فرائض پر ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ محدود العدد ہیں اور چونکہ مزید (جس کی زیاد گئی ) کا مزید علیہا کے ہم جنس ہونا ضروی ہے اس لئے اس کی مقتضی یہ ہے کہ فرائض پر جس چیز کی زیادت کی گئی یعنی وتر کی بھی ، اسلاموں مگر چونکہ حدیث خبر واحد ہونے کی وجہ دلیل غیر قطعی ہے اور دلیل غیر قطعی سے واجب تو ثابت ہو سکتا ہے لیکن فرض ثابت نہیں ہو تار اور میان وتر واجب ہوگا۔
سوم یہ کہ حدیث مذکور میں فصلوها امر کا صیغہ اور امر وجوب کے لئے آتا ہے لہذا اس سے بھی وتر کا وجوب ثابت ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ وتر چونکہ واجب ہے اس لئے اس کی قضاء واجب ہوتی ہے ورنہ سنتوں کی قضاء واجب نہیں ہوا المقال صاحب کی تائید اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے کہ سردار دو جہاں صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ الوتر حق واجب فمن لم يوتر فليس دا است و تر حق واجب ہے جس نے وتر کی نماز نہیں پڑھی وہ ہم میں سے نہیں ہے (ابو داؤد) مسلم شریف میں ابوسعید خدری کی حدیث - لئے پر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال او تــروا قبل ان تصبحوا یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ صبح ہونے سے پہلے پہلے وتر پڑھ لو۔ اس حدیث میں م" امر کا صیغہ ہے جو وجوب پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔ صاحبین کی طرف سے پیش کردہ عقلی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ وتر کا منکر کافر اس لئے نہیں ہوتا کہ وتر کا ثبوت سنت غیر متواتر ہے اور یہ جو امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ وتر سنت ہے اس کے معنی بھی یہی ہیں کہ وتر کا ثبوتو سنت سے ہے اور چونکہ وتر کی نماز وقت میں ادا کی جاتی ہے اس لئے عشاء کی اذان اور اقامت پر اکتفاء کیا گیا۔ وتر کے لئے علیحدہ اذان واقامت کی ضرورت نہیں صاحبین کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث اعرابی کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ حدیث وجوب و تر سے پہلے کی ہے۔ اور حدیث ابن عمر اونہ البعير کا جواب بقول طحاوی کے یہ ہے کہ حدیث ابن عمر ، حدیث حنظلہ بن ابی سفیان عن نافع عن ابن عمر کے معارض ہے۔ مدین کے الفاظ یہ ہیں انه كان يصلى على راحلته و يوتر بالارض و يزعم ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم فعل ذلک یعنی ابن عمرانی نماز پڑھتے تھے مگروتر زمین پر پڑھتے ۔ اور ابن عمر فرماتے تھے کہ نبی نے یہی کیا یعنی وتر کی نماز زمین پر ادا کی۔ پس جب ابن عمر روایتوں میں تعارض واقع ہو گیا تو دونوں ساقط ہو جائیں گی۔
Chapter of Salat al-Witr. Second, that it is narrated from Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed witr on a camel, meaning the Prophet performed witr prayer on a mount. It is evident that nafl prayers can be performed on a mount, not fard or wajib. So if witr were wajib, the Prophet would not have performed it on a mount. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Indeed Allah has increased for you a prayer, and it is witr, so pray it between Isha and the break of dawn.' The author of al-Inaya wrote that this hadith is used as evidence in several ways. First, the addition (ziyada) is attributed to Allah, while sunnah practices are attributed to the Messenger of Allah. So if witr were sunnah, it would be attributed to the Messenger in the hadith. But since it is attributed to Allah, witr is not sunnah; rather it is wajib. Second, something is only increased upon something that is limited in number. It is established that nafl prayers are unlimited, they have no end. So the increase is upon the faraid, because they are limited in number. And since the increased (mazid) must be of the same type as that upon which it is increased (mazid alayhi), this requires that what is increased upon the faraid, i.e., witr, is also of the same type. But because the hadith is khabar wahid (single narration), it is non-definitive (ghayr qat'i) evidence, and non-definitive evidence can prove wajib but not fard. Therefore witr is wajib. Third, in the aforementioned hadith, 'fajjiluha' is in the imperative form (amr), and the imperative indicates obligation (wujub). Thus this also proves the obligation of witr. The author of al-Hidaya said that because witr is wajib, its makeup (qada) is obligatory, whereas makeup of sunnah is not obligatory. This is supported by the hadith: 'Witr is a due right (haqq wajib); whoever does not pray witr is not of us' (Abu Dawud). In Sahih Muslim, from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Pray witr before you become morning.' In this hadith, 'awtiru' is imperative indicating obligation. The response to the rational proof presented by the two companions (Sahibayn) is that the denier of witr is not a disbeliever because witr is proven by non-mutawatir sunnah. And what is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that witr is sunnah means that its proof is from the sunnah. And since witr is performed in its time, the adhan and iqamah of Isha are sufficient; there is no need for a separate adhan and iqamah for witr. The response to the hadith of the Bedouin presented by the two companions is that this hadith is from before the obligation of witr. And the response to the hadith of Ibn Umar about the camel, according to Tahawi, is that the hadith of Ibn Umar conflicts with the hadith of Hanzala ibn Abi Sufyan from Nafi' from Ibn Umar. The wording of the latter is: 'He used to pray on his mount and pray witr on the ground, and he claimed that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did that.' That is, Ibn Umar used to pray witr on the ground. And Ibn Umar said that the Prophet did that, i.e., performed witr on the ground. So when conflicting narrations from Ibn Umar exist, both are dropped.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. It begins by stating the ruling that witr is wajib according to Imam Abu Hanifa, then presents objections from Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and responds to them. The primary proof is the hadith: 'Allah has increased for you a prayer, and it is witr, so pray it between Isha and dawn.' The commentary explains three deductive arguments: (1) the addition is attributed to Allah, not the Prophet, indicating it is not sunnah; (2) the increase implies limitation, so witr must be like faraid but since evidence is non-definitive, it is wajib; (3) the command (amr) indicates obligation. It also addresses the objection from the hadith of Ibn Umar about praying on a mount by showing contradiction in Ibn Umar's own narrations, thus dropping both. The passage concludes that witr is wajib, and its makeup is obligatory unlike sunnan.

Key Terms
وتر (witr): A prayer performed after Isha, consisting of three rak'ahs with one salam, considered wajib in the Hanafi school.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act that is proven by zanni evidence; omission is blameworthy but not disbelief.
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A hadith transmitted by a single or few narrators, providing zanni certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason witr is not considered sunnah?
A) The Prophet said it is fard.
B) The addition is attributed to Allah, not the Prophet.
C) The hadith is mutawatir.
D) Witr is always prayed in congregation.

Key Takeaway
Witr is wajib, and its makeup is obligatory, as established by Imam Abu Hanifa's deduction from the hadith and the refutation of Sahibayn's objections.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Witr is Three Rak'ahs with One Salam
Establishing the Hanafi ruling on witr against opposing views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on witr prayer and explain how the hadith of Aisha and the consensus of the Companions support the ruling of three rak'ahs with one salam.

Core Idea
Witr is three rak'ahs with one salam—upheld by Aisha's practice and unanimous consensus of the Salaf.

The witr prayer is a nightly obligation that has generated significant inter-madhhab discussion regarding its structure. This lesson examines the Hanafi position that witr consists of three rak'ahs concluded with a single salam, contrasting it with the Maliki and Shafi'i views. By analyzing the primary evidence—the hadith of Aisha and the reported consensus—you will understand why the Hanafi school adheres to this practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school holds witr to be three rak'ahs with one salam at the end, no separation with salam in between.
This is the zahir riwayah position.
2
Identify the opposing views
Note that Malik and one saying of al-Shafi'i hold that witr is prayed with two salams (either two plus one or two salams in three). Also some reports say one rak'ah suffices.
These are the views the Hanafis refute.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
Look at the hadith of Aisha: 'The Prophet used to pray witr with three.' Also the consensus (ijma) reported by Hasan al-Basri that the Companions agreed on three rak'ahs with one salam.
The dalil is fi'li (action) and qawli (statement) combined.
4
Analyze the opposing proof and Hanafi response
The opponents cite hadiths about praying 'two by two' and then one rak'ah, and the hadith 'Witr is one rak'ah at the end of the night.' The Hanafis respond that those refer to the witr of the night (after tahajjud), not the witr after Isha which is specifically three rak'ahs.
This distinction is key to resolving the conflict.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis pray three rak'ahs with one salam and qunut in the third; Malikis pray two rak'ahs and then a separate single rak'ah each with salam; Shafi'is have both options.
The mufta bihi in Hanafi school is three with one salam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة الوتر
وتر کی تین رکعتیں ایک سلام کے ساتھ پڑھی جائیں
قال الوتر ثلاث ركعات لا يفصل بينهن بسلام لما روت عائشة انه عليه السلام كان يوتر بثلاث وحكى الحسن اجماع المسلمين على الثلاث وهذا احد اقوال الشافعى وفى قول يوتر بتسليمتين وهو قول مالك والحجة عليهما ما رويناه
مہ وتر تین رکعات ہیں۔ ان میں سلام سے جدائی نہ کرے کیونکہ حضرت عائشہ نے روایت کیا کہ حضور وتر تین رکعات تے تھے۔ اور حسن بصری نے تین رکعات پر مسلمانوں کا اجماع نقل کیا ہے۔ اور یہی امام شافعی کے اقوال میں سے ایک قول ہے۔ اور بہ قول میں دوسلاموں کے ساتھ وتر پڑھے۔ اور یہی امام مالک کا قول ہے اور دونوں کے خلاف حجت وہ حدیث ہے جس کو ہم روایت
تفریح وتر کی رکعتوں کی تعداد کے بارے میں اختلاف ہے۔ اور اس بات میں اختلاف ہے کہ وتر ایک سلام کے ساتھ ہے یا دو راموں کے ساتھ ۔ علماء احناف کے نزدیک وتر کی تین رکعتیں ایک سلام کے ساتھ واجب ہیں۔ درمیان میں ایک اور سلام لا کر ان کے یان فصل نہ کرے۔ امام شافعی کے دو قول ہیں ایک قول تو احناف کے قول کے مطابق ہے۔ دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ وتر کی تین رکعتیں دو راموں کے ساتھ ادا کرے۔ یہی قول امام مالک کا ہے اور بعض نے کہا کہ وتر کی ایک رکعت ہے۔
ایک رکعت کے قائلین نے حدیث ابن عمر سے استدلال کیا ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے ان رجلا سأل النبي عن صلاة الليل لدل مثنى مثنى فاذا خشيت الصبح فصل ركعة توتر لك ما صلیت یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے کسی آدمی نے صلاۃ اللیل کے بارے میں دریافت کیا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ دو دورکعتیں ہیں۔ پس جب تجھ کو طلوع صبح کا اندیشہ ہو تو ایک رکعت پڑھ کہ وہ تیرے پہلے کی نماز کو وتر کردے گی۔ نیز مسلم شریف میں ابن عمرہؓ سے مرفوعا روایت ہے کہ الوتر ركعة من آخر الليل يعنى آخر رات وتر ایک رکعت ہے۔ نیز حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے روایت ہے قال من احب ان يوتر بخمس فايفعل و من احب ان يوتر بواحدة الفعل یعنی آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جس نے وتر کی پانچ رکعات کو پسند کیا تو اس کو کرے اور جس نے ایک رکعت کو پسند کیا تو وہ اس کو کرے۔ وتر کی سات نو اور گیارہ رکعت کی تعداد بھی مروی ہے۔ (عنایہ )
تارے دلائل یہ ہیں :-
حضرت عائشہ سے مروی ہے ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يوتر بثلاث ركعات
حسن بصری نے وتر کی ایک سلام کے ساتھ تین رکعات پر مسلمانوں کا اجماع نقل کیا ہے چنانچہ حسن بصری سے مروی ہے فال جمع المسلمون على ان الوتر ثلث لا يسلم الا فی آخر من یعنی کہا کہ مسلمانوں کا اس بات پر اجماع ہے کہ وتر کی تین رکھتیں ہیں صرف ان کے آخر میں سلام پھیرے۔ عن عائشة قالت كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يسلم في الركعتين الا وليين من الوتر یعنی حضرت عائشہ نے کہا کہ حضور ور کی پہلی دو رکعتوں میں سلام نہیں پھیرتے تھے۔
Chapter of Salat al-Witr. Witr is three rak'ahs, one should not separate them with salam, because Aisha narrated that he (peace be upon him) used to pray witr with three. And Hasan al-Basri reported the consensus of Muslims on three. This is one of the sayings of al-Shafi'i. In another saying, he prays witr with two salams, and that is the saying of Malik. The proof against them is what we narrated. Explanation: There is disagreement about the number of rak'ahs of witr and whether it is with one salam or two salams. According to Hanafi scholars, three rak'ahs of witr are wajib with one salam, one should not separate with a salam in between. Imam al-Shafi'i has two sayings: one agrees with the Hanafis, the other says to pray three rak'ahs with two salams. That is the saying of Imam Malik. Some said witr is one rak'ah. Those who say one rak'ah use the hadith of Ibn Umar: A man asked the Prophet about night prayer, he said: 'Two by two, and when you fear dawn, pray one rak'ah to make what you have prayed odd (witr).' Also in Sahih Muslim from Ibn Umar marfoo': 'Witr is one rak'ah at the end of the night.' Also the Prophet said: 'Whoever wishes to pray witr with five, let him do so; whoever wishes to pray witr with one, let him do so.' And seven, nine, and eleven rak'ahs are also narrated (from al-Inaya). The proofs (for the Hanafi position) are: From Aisha: 'The Prophet used to pray witr with three rak'ahs.' Hasan al-Basri narrated consensus on three rak'ahs of witr with one salam at the end. From Aisha: 'The Messenger of Allah did not say salam in the first two rak'ahs of witr.'
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the manner of performing witr. It begins by stating the Hanafi position: witr is three rak'ahs with one salam, without separating with a salam. The proof is the action of the Prophet as narrated by Aisha and the consensus reported by Hasan al-Basri. It then mentions that Imam al-Shafi'i has two sayings: one agrees, the other says two salams (similar to Malik). The passage also refutes the view that witr is one rak'ah, which is based on hadiths about night prayer, but these are interpreted differently. The Hanafis hold that the one-rak'ah report refers to the witr of the night (after tahajjud), while the witr after Isha is specifically three rak'ahs. The consensus on three rak'ahs with one salam is taken as decisive.

Key Terms
رکعت (rak'ah): A unit of prayer consisting of standing, bowing, prostrations, and sitting.
سلام (salam): The concluding salutation of prayer, saying 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' to the right and left.
اجماع (ijma): Consensus of the mujtahid scholars of the Muslim community on a ruling.

Checkpoint

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi Position on Witr: Three Rak'ahs, One Salam
Inter-madhhab dispute on Witr form.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of rak'ahs and salams in Witr prayer, explain the proofs from hadith and ijma, and distinguish the opposing views of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik.

Core Idea
Witr is three rak'ahs with one salam — explicit hadith and consensus settle the form.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: how many rak'ahs and salams constitute the Witr prayer? The Hanafi school firmly holds that Witr consists of three rak'ahs with a single salam, without separation. The author presents the proofs from the Sunnah and the consensus of the Companions, and then refutes the views that Witr should be performed with two salams (Shafi'i/Maliki) or as a single rak'ah. Understanding this disagreement is essential for correct practice and for appreciating how different schools derive rulings from the same sources.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling as given in the text: Witr is three rak'ahs performed with one salam, with no separation (fasl) between the rak'ahs.
The text explicitly says: 'الوتر ثلاث ركعات لا يفصل بينهن بسلام'.
2
Identify the opposing views
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i has two sayings: one agrees with the Hanafis, the other says Witr is with two salams. Imam Malik holds the two-salams view. Some early authorities held that Witr is a single rak'ah.
The text mentions: 'وهذا احد اقوال الشافعى وفى قول يوتر بتسليمتين وهو قول مالك'.
3
Examine the Hanafi proofs
List the proofs cited: (1) Hadith of Aisha that the Prophet prayed Witr as three. (2) Consensus (ijma) of Muslims transmitted by Hasan al-Basri. (3) Reports from Ibn Mas'ud and Abu al-Aliya that Witr is like Maghrib. (4) Prohibition of 'al-Batira' (praying a single rak'ah alone).
The hadith 'ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يوتر بثلاث' is the primary proof.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to opposing proofs
Understand how the Hanafis rebut the one-rak'ah view: the hadith 'فصل ركعة' is interpreted as 'pray one rak'ah along with two before it' (making three). The narrations of one, five, or seven rak'ahs are considered abrogated by the final determination on three.
Imam al-Tahawi's response is cited in the passage.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Recognize the practical difference: Hanafis pray three rak'ahs continuously with one salam at the end; Shafi'is/Malikis following the second view pray two rak'ahs, make salam, then pray one rak'ah individually.
This affects the recitation of tashahhud and the overall structure of the prayer.

باب صلوة الوتر
قال الوتر ثلاث ركعات لا يفصل بينهن بسلام لما روت عائشة انه عليه السلام كان يوتر بثلاث وحكى الحسن اجماع المسلمين على الثلاث وهذا احد اقوال الشافعى وفى قول يوتر بتسليمتين وهو قول مالك والحجة عليهما ما رويناه
تفريح وتر کی تین رکعات ہیں۔ ان میں سلام سے جدائی نہ کرے کیونکہ حضرت عائشہ نے روایت کیا کہ حضور وتر تین رکعات پڑھتے تھے۔ اور حسن بصری نے تین رکعات پر مسلمانوں کا اجماع نقل کیا ہے۔ اور یہی امام شافعی کے اقوال میں سے ایک قول ہے۔ اور بہ قول میں دوسلاموں کے ساتھ وتر پڑھے۔ اور یہی امام مالک کا قول ہے اور دونوں کے خلاف حجت وہ حدیث ہے جس کو ہم روایت
تفريح وتر کی رکعتوں کی تعداد کے بارے میں اختلاف ہے۔ اور اس بات میں اختلاف ہے کہ وتر ایک سلام کے ساتھ ہے یا دو سلاموں کے ساتھ ۔ علماء احناف کے نزدیک وتر کی تین رکعتیں ایک سلام کے ساتھ واجب ہیں۔ درمیان میں ایک اور سلام لا کر ان کے یان فصل نہ کرے۔ امام شافعی کے دو قول ہیں ایک قول تو احناف کے قول کے مطابق ہے۔ دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ وتر کی تین رکعتیں دو سلاموں کے ساتھ ادا کرے۔ یہی قول امام مالک کا ہے اور بعض نے کہا کہ وتر کی ایک رکعت ہے۔
ایک رکعت کے قائلین نے حدیث ابن عمر سے استدلال کیا ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے ان رجلا سأل النبي عن صلاة الليل لدل مثنى مثنى فاذا خشيت الصبح فصل ركعة توتر لك ما صلیت یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے کسی آدمی نے صلاۃ اللیل کے بارے میں دریافت کیا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ دو دو رکعتیں ہیں۔ پس جب تجھ کو طلوع صبح کا اندیشہ ہو تو ایک رکعت پڑھ کہ وہ تیرے بھی ہوئی نماز کو تر کردے گی نیز مسلم شریف میں ابن عمرہؓ سے مرفوعا روایت ہے کہ الوتر ركعة من آخر الليل يعنى آخر رات میں ایک رکعت ہے۔ نیز حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے روایت ہے قال من احب ان يوتر بخمس فايفعل و من احب ان يوتر بواحدة الفعل یعنی آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جس نے وتر کی پانچ رکعات کو پسند کیا تو اس کو کرے اور جس نے ایک رکعت کو پسند کیا تو وہ اس کو کرے۔ وتر کی سات نو اور گیارہ رکعت کی تعداد بھی مروی ہے۔ (عنایہ )
ہمارے دلائل یہ ہیں :-
حضرت عائشہ سے مروی ہے ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يوتر بثلاث ركعات
حسن بصری نے وتر کی ایک سلام کے ساتھ تین رکعات پر مسلمانوں کا اجماع نقل کیا ہے چنانچہ حسن بصری سے مروی ہے فقل جمع المسلمون على ان الوتر ثلث لا يسلم الا فی آخر من یعنی کہا کہ مسلمانوں کا اس بات پر اجماع ہے کہ وتر کی تین رکھتیں ہیں صرف ان کے آخر میں سلام پھیرے۔ عن عائشة قالت كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يسلم في الركعتين الا وليين من الوتر یعنی حضرت عائشہ نے کہا کہ حضور ور کی پہلی دو رکعتوں میں سلام نہیں پھیرتے تھے۔
ابن مسعودؓ سے مروی ہے وتر الليل ثلث كوتر النهار یعنی رات کا وتر تین رکعتیں ہیں جیسا کہ دن کا وتر تین رکھتیں اس کے وتر سے مراد مغرب کی نماز ہے۔ (فتح القدیر) ۵) ابو خالد نے بیان کیا کہ میں نے جلیل القدر تابعی ابو العالیہ سے وتر کے بارے میں سوال کیا تو فرمایا کہ علمنا اصحاب رسا شهر ط ان الوتر مثل صلوة المغرب هذا وتر الليل وهذا وتر النهار یعنی ہم کو اصحاب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے تعلیم کہ مغرب کی نماز کے مانند ہے۔ یہ رات کا وتر ہے اور یہ یعنی مغرب دن کا وتر ہے۔ اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ مغرب کی نماز کی کے بھی تین رکعتیں ہیں۔
عن عائشة ان النبي كان يوتر بثلاث يقرأ فى اول ركعة سبح اسم ربک و فى الثانية قل يابها الكامين في الثالثة قـل هـو الله والمعوذتین یعنی حضور تین رکعتیں وتر کی پڑھتے تھے، پہلی میں سبح اسم ربک ابدا رکعت میں قل یا ایها الکافرون اور تیسری رکعت میں قل ھو اللہ احد اور معوذتین پڑھتے تھے۔
نہی رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلمعن البتيراء يعنى حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے صلوة بتيراء یعنی ایک رکعت پڑھنے سے منع فرمایا جو حضرات وتر کی ایک رکعت کے قائل ہیں ان کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث ابن عمر کا جواب بقول امام طحاوی یہ ہے کہ
کے قول فصل ركعة کے معنی یہ ہیں ۔ صل ركعة مع ثنتين قبلها یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اس سے پہلی دور کھتوں کے کر ایک رکعت اور پڑھ لے۔ پس اب تین رکعتیں ہوئیں نہ کہ ایک۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ ایک رکعت یا پانچ رکعتیں یا سات انا مترجم کی روایت استقراروتر سے پہلے کی ہیں۔ لیکن جب تین رکعتوں پر استقرار ہو گیا اور ٹھہراؤ ہو گیا تو باقی روایتیں منسوخ ہو گئیں۔
Chapter of Witr Prayer. He said: Witr is three rak'ahs, not separating between them with a salam, because Aisha narrated that he (peace be upon him) prayed Witr as three, and Hasan (al-Basri) reported the consensus of Muslims on three. This is one of the sayings of al-Shafi'i, and in another saying he prays Witr with two salams, and that is the saying of Malik. The proof against them is what we narrated. Explanation: Witr is three rak'ahs. Do not separate them with salam because Aisha narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray Witr as three rak'ahs. Hasan al-Basri transmitted the consensus of Muslims on three rak'ahs. This is one of the sayings of Imam al-Shafi'i. In another saying, he prays Witr with two salams, and that is the saying of Imam Malik. The proof against both is the hadith we narrated. Detail: There is disagreement about the number of rak'ahs of Witr and whether it is with one salam or two. According to Hanafi scholars, three rak'ahs of Witr are wajib with one salam, not separating them with another salam. Imam al-Shafi'i has two sayings: one agrees with the Hanafis, the other says to perform three rak'ahs of Witr with two salams. That is also Imam Malik's saying. Some said Witr is one rak'ah. Those who say one rak'ah used the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'A man asked the Prophet about night prayer; he said: Two by two. When you fear dawn, pray one rak'ah, making what you have prayed odd.' Also in Sahih Muslim from Ibn Umar marfu'an: 'Witr is one rak'ah at the end of the night.' Also the Prophet said: 'Whoever likes to pray Witr as five, let him do so; whoever likes to pray Witr as one, let him do so.' Numbers of seven, nine, and eleven rak'ahs are also narrated. Our proofs are: From Aisha that the Prophet prayed Witr as three rak'ahs. Hasan al-Basri transmitted the consensus of Muslims on three rak'ahs with one salam: 'The Muslims agreed that Witr is three, and one does not make salam except at the end.' From Aisha: 'The Messenger of Allah did not make salam in the first two rak'ahs of Witr.' From Ibn Mas'ud: 'The Witr of the night is three like the Witr of the day' meaning Maghrib. Abu Khalid said: I asked Abu al-Aliya about Witr; he said: 'The companions of the Messenger taught us that Witr is like the Maghrib prayer; this is the Witr of the night, and this is the Witr of the day.' From Aisha: The Prophet prayed Witr with three, reciting in the first 'Sabbihisma rabbika', in the second 'Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun', and in the third 'Qul huwa Allahu ahad' and al-Mu'awwidhatayn. The Prophet prohibited 'al-Batira' prayer, meaning one rak'ah. The response to the hadith of Ibn Umar from those who say one rak'ah, according to Imam al-Tahawi, is that the saying 'pray one rak'ah' means 'pray one rak'ah along with two before it', so it becomes three, not one. The second response is that the narrations of one, five, or seven rak'ahs are from before the determination of Witr, and when the determination was settled on three, those narrations were abrogated.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the number of rak'ahs and salams in Witr prayer. The Hanafi position is that Witr consists of three rak'ahs with a single salam, without separating between them. This is based on the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet prayed Witr as three, and the consensus (ijma) transmitted by Hasan al-Basri. The Shafi'i school has two views: one agrees with the Hanafis, the other says Witr should be prayed with two salams (i.e., like Maghrib or with a tashahhud after two rak'ahs). The Maliki school holds the latter view. The Hanafis rebut these by citing the hadith of Aisha and the consensus. Additionally, the passage addresses the view that Witr is only one rak'ah, providing evidence from hadith and explaining that the one-rak'ah hadith is interpreted as combining with two previous rak'ahs, or that it predates the final determination. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah since this is from Al-Hidayah, and the relied-upon position is the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
وتر (witr): The prayer performed after the night prayer, consisting of an odd number of rak'ahs.
فصل (fasl): Separation between rak'ahs by making salam.
بتيراء (batira): A prayer consisting of a single rak'ah, which the Prophet prohibited.
استقرار (istiqrar): Final determination or settled practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) One rak'ah with one salam

Key Takeaway
According to the Hanafi school, Witr prayer is three rak'ahs with one salam, based on the Sunnah and consensus.

Salah — Prayer

The Placement of Qunut in Witr: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Resolving a fiqh dispute on qunut placement via hadith and linguistic reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the placement of qunut in Witr, explain the Shafi'i objection, and evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal using hadith and linguistic reasoning.

Core Idea
Qunut in Witr is before ruku in the third rak'ah – the Hanafi proof is explicit, outweighing general interpretations of 'akhir'.

This passage addresses a well-known difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: where exactly in Witr prayer should the qunut supplication be recited? The Hanafi school holds it is before ruku in the third rak'ah, while the Shafi'i school places it after ruku. The dispute hinges on the interpretation of the phrase 'akhir al-witr' (end of Witr) and the strength of specific hadith narrations. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies the Hanafi methodology of prioritizing explicit textual evidence over general linguistic interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the Hanafi position (before ruku in the third rak'ah) and the Shafi'i position (after ruku). Note that both agree qunut is recited in the third rak'ah, but differ on the precise moment.
The Hanafi position is summarized in the opening phrase: 'wa yaqnitu fi al-thalithah qabla al-ruku'.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'is cite the general hadith that the Prophet recited qunut 'at the end of Witr' (akhir al-witr). They interpret 'akhir' as the very end of the prayer, i.e., after ruku and before the taslim.
This interpretation relies on the common understanding of 'akhir' as the final part.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafis present two proofs: (1) an explicit hadith from Ubayy ibn Ka'b that the Prophet recited qunut before ruku, and (2) a linguistic argument that anything exceeding half of something is considered its 'akhir'. Since the third rak'ah constitutes more than half of Witr (three rak'ahs), the portion before ruku is also part of the end.
The specific hadith is given as: 'an Rasul allah sallallahu alayhi wasallam kana yutiru fa-yaqnitu qabla al-ruku'.
4
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafis argue that the explicit hadith specifying 'before ruku' takes precedence over the general 'akhir al-witr' hadith. The linguistic argument reinforces that 'akhir' can include the portion after the halfway point.
The rebuttal uses the principle of takhsis (specification) of a general text by a more specific one.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference affects the actual performance of Witr: Hanafis recite qunut before ruku, raising hands and making the supplication silently; Shafi'is recite it after ruku, often aloud, and may repeat it during the last half of Ramadan.
This is a clear example of how a seemingly minor interpretative difference leads to a different ritual practice.

Source Text

و يقنت في الثالثة قبل الركوع وقال الشافعى بعده لما روى انه عليه السلام قنت في آخر الوقت و الركوع ولنا ماروى انه عليه السلام قنت قبل الركوع ومازاد على نصف الشيء آخره. ترجمہ اور تیسری رکعت میں رکوع سے پہلے قنوت پڑھے اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ رکوع کے بعد ( قنوت پڑھے) کیونکہ مودی آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے آخر وتر میں قنوت پڑھا اور آخر وتر رکوع کے بعد ہوگا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ روایت کیا گیا کہ حضور یعنی 1 سے پہلے قنوت پڑھا۔ اور کسی چیز کے آدھے پر جومتجاوز ہو وہ اس کا آخر ہے۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں دعا قنوت کے محل کا ذکر ہے ہمارے نزدیک دعاء قنوت کا محل رکوع سے پہلے ہے اور شوافع کے ماہ رمضا کے بعد ہے۔ شوافع کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ انہ علیہ السلام قنت فی آخر الوتر یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے آخر وتر میں قنوت پڑھا اور آخرون نہیں بعد ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا قنوت رکوع کے بعد پڑھا جائے گا۔ ہماری دلیل ابی بن کعب کی روایت ہے ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كـان يـوتـر فيقنت قبل الرکوع یعنی حضور گیا۔ قنوت رکوع سے پہلے پڑھتے ، جو الفاظ صاحب ہدایہ نے بیان فرمائے ہیں وہ عبداللہ بن مسعود سے مروی ہیں۔ نیز ہمارے مذاہب
And he recites qunut in the third rak'ah before ruku. Al-Shafi'i said after ruku, because it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) recited qunut at the end of Witr, and the end of Witr is after ruku. Our proof is that it is narrated that he recited qunut before ruku, and anything that exceeds half of a thing is its end. Translation: And in the third rak'ah, recite qunut before ruku. Imam al-Shafi'i said that qunut is recited after ruku, because it is narrated that the Prophet recited qunut at the end of Witr, and the end of Witr would be after ruku. Our proof is that it is narrated that the Prophet recited qunut before ruku. And what exceeds half of a thing is its end. Explanation: This passage mentions the place of the qunut supplication. According to us, the place of qunut is before ruku, and according to the Shafi'is, it is after ruku. The Shafi'i proof is that the Prophet recited qunut at the end of Witr, and 'end' means after. Therefore, qunut should be recited after ruku. Our proof is the narration of Ubayy ibn Ka'b that the Messenger of Allah prayed Witr and recited qunut before ruku. The words that the author of Hidayah stated are narrated from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. And our madhhab...
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the placement of qunut in Witr prayer. The Hanafi position is that qunut (the supplication) should be recited in the third rak'ah before bowing (ruku). The Shafi'i school holds that it should be recited after ruku. The Shafi'is argue that the Prophet recited qunut 'at the end of Witr' (akhir al-witr), and that the end of Witr is after ruku. The Hanafis respond with two points: first, there is a narration that the Prophet recited qunut before ruku (specifically from Ubayy ibn Ka'b and Abdullah ibn Mas'ud). Second, they provide a linguistic/rational argument: anything that exceeds half of a thing is considered its end. Since the third rak'ah is more than half of Witr (which is three rak'ahs), the part after ruku is not the only 'akhir'; before ruku in the third rak'ah is also part of the end. Thus, qunut can be before ruku. The reliance on the hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b is stronger. This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunut): A specific supplication recited in the Witr prayer.
آخر الوتر (akhir al-witr): The end of Witr prayer; Hanafis define it as the part after the halfway point of the third rak'ah.

Key Takeaway

Witr Prayer: Three Rak'ahs Proved
Establishes Hanafi position that witr is three rak'ahs with hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on witr rak'ahs and evaluate the opposing proof from Ibn 'Umar's hadith.

Core Idea
Witr is three rak'ahs, not one — the established practice of the Prophet and explicit prohibition of a single rak'ah settle the matter.

You may have heard that witr can be prayed as a single rak'ah. But the Hanafi school, drawing on the practice of the Prophet and the Companions, holds firmly that witr is three rak'ahs. This lesson unpacks the evidence and shows how Hanafi scholars interpret conflicting narrations using principles of abrogation and contextual interpretation.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that Hanafis hold witr to be three rak'ahs, equivalent to Maghrib (day witr).
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
Recognize that some scholars permit one rak'ah based on the hadith of Ibn 'Umar where the Prophet said 'salli rak'atan' (pray one rak'ah).
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
Two responses: (1) Contextual interpretation: 'pray one rak'ah along with two before it' makes three; (2) Abrogation: the one-rak'ah narration predates the established (istiqrar) practice of three rak'ahs.
The second response relies on the usul principle that later settled practice abrogates earlier conflicting reports.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafis pray three rak'ahs; those who accept one rak'ah may pray a single one. In a Hanafi congregation, witr must be three.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is considered stronger due to multiple corroborating proofs (Ibn Mas'ud, Aisha, prohibition of batira) and the principle of istiqrar.
Imam Tahawi's analysis is cited as authoritative in resolving the conflict.

Chapter of Witr Prayer. (4) Narrated from Ibn Mas'ud: 'Witr of the night is three like the witr of the day' meaning the night witr is three rak'ahs just as the day witr is three rak'ahs; by 'witr of the day' is meant Maghrib prayer. (5) Abu Khalid said: I asked the great Tabi'i Abu al-Aliyah about witr, and he said: 'The Companions of the Messenger of Allah taught us that witr is like Maghrib prayer; this is the witr of the night and this (Maghrib) is the witr of the day.' From this it is also understood that Maghrib prayer also has three rak'ahs. Narrated from Aisha: The Prophet used to perform witr with three rak'ahs, reciting in the first rak'ah 'Sabbih isma rabbika', in the second 'Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun', and in the third 'Qul huwa Allahu ahad' and al-Mu'awwidhatayn. There is a well-known narration: The Messenger of Allah forbade al-batira', meaning he forbade praying one rak'ah. The answer to the hadith of Ibn 'Umar presented by those who believe in one rak'ah for witr, according to Imam Tahawi, is that the meaning of his saying 'salli rak'atan' is: 'Pray one rak'ah along with two before it', so it becomes three rak'ahs, not one. The second answer is that the narration of one rak'ah, or five, or seven, are from before the settlement on witr; but when the settlement (istiqrar) occurred upon three rak'ahs, the other narrations became abrogated.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute establishing that witr prayer consists of three rak'ahs, not one. The Hanafi school relies on several proofs: the statement of Ibn Mas'ud equating night witr to day witr (Maghrib), the teaching of the Companions via Abu al-Aliyah, and the explicit practice of the Prophet as narrated by Aisha. Additionally, the Prophet forbade 'al-batira' (one-rak'ah prayer). The Hadith of Ibn 'Umar (which seems to permit one rak'ah) is interpreted by Imam Tahawi to mean 'pray one rak'ah in addition to two', making three total, or is considered abrogated after the established practice settled on three. Thus, the Hanafi position is that witr is three rak'ahs and the one-rak'ah view is invalid.

Key Terms
البتيراء (al-batira'): A prayer consisting of a single rak'ah, considered deficient and prohibited.
استقرار (istiqrar): The settled, established practice of the Prophet after which earlier practices are abrogated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One rak'ah
B) Three rak'ahs
C) Five rak'ahs
D) Seven rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
Witr is three rak'ahs, established by multiple hadith and the prohibition of a single-rak'ah prayer.

Placement of Qunoot in Witr: Before Ruku
Argues that qunoot should be recited before ruku, not after.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the placement of qunoot in witr and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the linguistic reconciliation.

Core Idea
Qunoot in witr is before ruku; the 'end of witr' begins after the halfway point.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute: whether qunoot in witr should be recited before or after ruku. The Hanafi school holds that it is before ruku, based on explicit hadith and a linguistic interpretation of the phrase 'end of witr'. We will analyze the evidence from both sides and the Hanafi response that reconciles conflicting narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The core disagreement is about the position of qunoot in the witr prayer: is it recited before ruku (the Hanafi position) or after ruku (the Shafi'i position)?
2
State the Hanafi position and its dalil
The Hanafi school relies on the hadith of Anas ibn Malik (رضي الله عنه) who explicitly said qunoot is before ruku. Also, the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) is reported to have recited qunoot before ruku.
The hadith is cited with the chain: 'Asim al-Ahwal asked Anas.'
3
State the Shafi'i position and its dalil
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that qunoot is after ruku, citing a hadith that the Prophet recited qunoot 'at the end of witr' (آخر الوتر), which he interprets as after ruku.
The Shafi'i position also has support from some narrations.
4
Explain the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response uses a linguistic argument: anything beyond half of a thing is called its 'end'. Since the third rak'ah's ruku occurs after the halfway point of the prayer, reciting qunoot before ruku can still be considered 'at the end of witr'. Thus, both hadiths are reconciled without contradiction.
Additionally, Anas explicitly denied that the Prophet regularly recited qunoot after ruku, except for one month.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is that Hanafis recite qunoot before ruku and then bow, while Shafi'is bow first, rise, and then recite qunoot. This affects the sequence and the takbirs for the qunoot.
This difference is observed in every witr prayer.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ اور تیسری ركعت میں ركوع سے پہلے قنوت پڑھے اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ ركوع کے بعد ( قنوت پڑھے) کیونکہ مودی آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے آخر وتر میں قنوت پڑھا اور آخر وتر ركوع کے بعد ہوگا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے كہ روایت کی گئی كہ حضور نے ركوع سے پہلے قنوت پڑھا۔ اور کسی چیز کے آدھے پر جومتجاوز ہو وہ اس کا آخر ہے۔

And he recites qunoot in the third (rak'ah) before ruku, and al-Shafi'i said after ruku, because it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) recited qunoot at the end of witr, and the end of witr is after ruku. Our proof is what is narrated that he (peace be upon him) recited qunoot before ruku, and what exceeds half of a thing is its end. Narrated from 'Asim al-Ahwal: I asked Anas about qunoot in prayer; he said yes. I said: Was it before ruku or after? He said: Before. I said: So-and-so informed me from you that you said after. He said: He lied; the Messenger of Allah only recited qunoot after ruku for one month. From these ahadith it is learned that qunoot is before ruku, not after. As for the response to the narration presented by Imam al-Shafi'i, it is that the hadith says 'qanata fi akhiri al-witr', and what exceeds half of a thing is called its end; therefore, even before ruku in the third rak'ah qualifies as 'end of witr', so this hadith is not against us.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the placement of qunoot in the witr prayer: before or after ruku. The Hanafi position, supported by the practice of the Prophet and the testimony of Anas ibn Malik, is that qunoot is recited before ruku. Imam al-Shafi'i argues it is after ruku, citing a hadith that the Prophet recited qunoot at the 'end of witr'. The Hanafi response employs a linguistic argument: anything beyond half of something is considered its 'end'; thus, before ruku in the third rak'ah is after the halfway point and can be called the end. Additionally, Anas explicitly denies that the Prophet regularly recited qunoot after ruku, except for one month. Therefore, the established practice is before ruku.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunoot): A specific supplication recited in the witr prayer, typically including words of devotion and supplication.
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha, consisting of three rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) In every rak'ah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school places qunoot before ruku based on explicit hadith and a linguistic reinterpretation of the phrase 'end of witr'.

Qunoot in Witr: Year-Round Obligation or Ramadan Only?
Establishes that qunoot is recited every night of the year, not just in Ramadan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that qunoot is wajib year-round and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the athar of 'Umar.

Core Idea
The Prophet's general command for qunoot in witr takes precedence over a Companion's practice.

In this passage, al-Marghinani defends the Hanafi position that qunoot in witr is recited every night of the year. Imam al-Shafi'i restricts it to the last half of Ramadan, citing the practice of 'Umar. The Hanafi response demonstrates how a general command (amm) from the Prophet outweighs a Companion's practice, especially when another Companion dissents.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: qunoot is recited every night of the year in witr, and it is wajib.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that qunoot is only in the last half of Ramadan, based on the action of 'Umar who ordered Ubayy ibn Ka'b to lead Tarawih and recite qunoot only in the last half.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i dalil: the athar (Companion's practice) of 'Umar, which they consider akin to consensus because no Companion objected at the time.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Two rebuttals: (1) 'Qunoot' in 'Umar's order means lengthy recitation (tul al-qira'ah), not the supplication. (2) Even if it means the supplication, Ibn 'Umar dissented, so no consensus. The explicit hadith of the Prophet remains binding.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis recite qunoot every night; Shafi'is only in the last half of Ramadan.

ترجمہ اور پورے سال قنوت پڑھے۔ رمضان کے نصف اخیر کے علاوہ میں امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حسن بن علي ناہ دی کہ سن کو دعاء قنوت سکھلائی کہ اس کو اپنے وتر میں داخل کر، بغیر کسی تفصیل کے۔
رنا ہمارے نزدیک وتر میں پورے سال دعائے قنوت کا پڑھنا واجب ہے حضرت امام شافعی کے نزدیک فقط رمضان المبارک ادف خیر میں دعاء قنوت پڑھنا مستحب ہے اور جو از بلا کراہت پورے سال ہے۔ (معین الہدایہ )

گر ہم جواب میں کہتے ہیں کہ ابن عمر کا اختلاف ثابت ہے۔ کیونکہ ابن عمر کہتے ہیں کہ لا اعرف القنوت الاطول القيام معنی میرے
He recites qunoot throughout the entire year, contrary to al-Shafi'i except for the last half of Ramadan, because of his (peace be upon him) saying to al-Hasan ibn 'Ali when he taught him the qunoot supplication: 'Place this in your witr' without specification. (Urdu explanation) And according to us, reciting the qunoot supplication in witr is obligatory throughout the entire year. According to Imam Shafi'i, it is only mustahabb in the last half of Ramadan. And it is permissible without dislike throughout the year. (Mu'in al-Hidayah) The proof of Imam Shafi'i is the narration that 'Umar appointed Ubayy ibn Ka'b as imam during the nights of Ramadan and ordered qunoot in the last half.' Our proof is the hadith that the Prophet taught al-Hasan ibn 'Ali the qunoot supplication and said 'Place this in your witr.' There is no specification of Ramadan or non-Ramadan, so qunoot is established throughout the year. The answer to the effect of 'Umar presented by Shafi'i is that 'qunoot' here means lengthy recitation (tul al-qira'ah) in prayer, i.e., 'Umar ordered Ubayy to lengthen the recitation in the last half. With this answer, this effect cannot be used as evidence. If we concede that it means the qunoot supplication, we respond that it is the effect of a Companion, and Imam Shafi'i considers a Companion's effect as evidence. But from Shafi'i's side it may be said that this effect is like consensus because Ubayy led a large group in the presence of other Companions and no one objected, so it stands in place of consensus. Then we respond: Ibn 'Umar's disagreement is established, because Ibn 'Umar says: 'I do not know qunoot except for lengthy standing.'
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about whether qunoot is recited throughout the year or only in the last half of Ramadan. The Hanafi school holds that qunoot is recited every night of the year, based on the general command of the Prophet to al-Hasan ibn 'Ali to include qunoot in his witr without seasonal restriction. Imam al-Shafi'i restricts it to the last half of Ramadan, citing the practice of 'Umar who ordered Ubayy ibn Ka'b to lead Tarawih and recite qunoot only in the last half. The Hanafi response first reinterprets 'Umar's order as referring to lengthy recitation (tul al-qira'ah), not the qunoot supplication. Even if it were qunoot, it is a Companion's action, which Shafi'is accept as evidence, but Hanafis argue that Ibn 'Umar himself disagreed with that practice, stating that qunoot is only prolonged standing. Therefore, there is no consensus, and the explicit hadith of the Prophet takes precedence. According to Mu'in al-Hidayah, reciting qunoot throughout the year is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school, while Shafi'is consider it mustahabb only in the last half of Ramadan.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunoot): A specific supplication recited in witr; in this context, disputed whether it is obligatory year-round or only in Ramadan.
طول القيام (tul al-qiyam): Lengthening the standing in prayer, i.e., reciting longer portions of the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is qunoot recited in witr?
A) Only in the last half of Ramadan
B) Throughout the entire year
C) Only on Fridays
D) Only when leading congregational prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds qunoot in witr as wajib every night of the year, based on the Prophet's general command, overruling the limited practice of 'Umar.

Timing of Qunoot in Witr: Before or After Ruku'?
Hadith of Anas proving Qunoot before ruku', with response to Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on Qunoot timing, explain the proof from the hadith of Anas, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the interpretation of 'akhir al-witr'.

Core Idea
Qunoot before ruku' is the established Sunnah; after ruku' was only one month.

The timing of Qunoot in Witr prayer is a classic point of ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. This lesson examines the primary Hanafi proof—the explicit hadith of Anas ibn Malik—and shows how the Shafi'i reliance on 'akhir al-witr' is reconciled with the Hanafi position. By understanding the linguistic argument over the word 'akhir', you will see how the Hanafi school harmonizes all evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on Qunoot timing
State clearly that the Hanafi school holds Qunoot is recited before ruku' in the last rak'ah of Witr. Know that this is the mufta bihi position.
The passage explicitly says 'Qunoot is before ruku'.'
2
Examine the primary Hanafi dalil
Read the hadith of Anas (from 'Asim al-Ahwal) where Anas affirms Qunoot before ruku' and denies the contrary report. Understand that this hadith is the core evidence.
The narrator uses strong denial ('He lied') for the report of after ruku'.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i proof and its wording
The Shafi'i school cites a hadith with the phrase 'qanata fi akhir al-witr'. Identify that the dispute hinges on the meaning of 'akhir'.
'Akhir' is often understood as 'the latter part', but its precise scope is debated.
4
Apply the Hanafi interpretation of 'akhir'
Hanafi scholars argue that 'akhir' applies to anything beyond half of something. Since the third rak'ah before ruku' is beyond half of Witr, it qualifies as 'akhir al-witr'. Thus the Shafi'i proof actually supports the Hanafi position.
This is a linguistic argument that resolves the apparent conflict.
5
Conclude with the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis recite Qunoot before ruku'; Shafi'is recite after ruku' in the last half of Ramadan. Recognize that both are valid within their own schools.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate; each school has strong evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن عاصم الاحول سألت انسا عن القنوت في الصلوة قال نعم فقلت اكان قبل الركوع او بعده قال قبله قلت فان فلانا اخبرنی عنک انک قلت بعده قال كذب انما قنت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بعد الركوع ہوا یعنی عام احوال سے مروی ہے کہ میں نے حضرت انس سے قنوت فی الصلوۃ کے بارے میں دریافت کیا تو کہا کہ ہاں، میں نے کہا کہ ان سے پہلے یا بعد میں فرمایا کہ رکوع سے پہلے، میں نے کہا کہ فلاں نے مجھ کو آپ کی طرف سے یہ خبر دی کہ آپ نے کہا کہ رکوع کے بعد ہے۔ اس نے کہا کہ و شخص جھوٹا ہے ۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے صرف ایک ماہ رکوع کے بعد قنوت پڑھا۔ ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قنوت رکوع سے پہلے ہے نہ کہ بعد میں۔ رہا امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ روایت کا جواب تو اس کے بارے نا ہے کہ حدیث میں قنت فی آخر الوتر کے الفاظ ہیں اور شئی کے آدھے سے جوزائد ہو اس پر آخر کا اطلاق کیا جاتا ہے کی تیسری رکعت میں رکوع سے پہلے پر بھی آخر وتر کا اطلاق ہو جائے گا۔ پس یہ حدیث بھی ہمارے خلاف نہ ہوگی۔
From 'Asim al-Ahwal: I asked Anas about Qunoot in prayer. He said, 'Yes.' I said, 'Was it before ruku' or after it?' He said, 'Before it.' I said, 'So-and-so narrated from you that you said after it.' He said, 'He lied. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) only recited Qunoot after ruku' for one month.' That is, from general circumstances it is narrated that I asked Hadrat Anas about Qunoot in prayer, so he said yes. I asked whether it was before or after, he said before ruku'. I said, 'So-and-so informed me from you that you said after ruku'.' He said, 'That person is a liar. The Prophet (peace be upon him) only recited Qunoot after ruku' for one month.' From these hadiths it is known that Qunoot is before ruku', not after. As for the answer to the narration presented by Imam Shafi'i, regarding it, it is that the hadith has the words 'qanata fi akhir al-witr' and the word 'akhir' is applied to what is more than half of something. So before ruku' in the third rak'ah also applies to 'akhir al-witr'. So this hadith will not be against us.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the timing of Qunoot in Witr prayer. The Hanafi school holds that Qunoot is recited before ruku', based on the explicit hadith of Anas ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him). In this hadith, Anas affirms that Qunoot was before ruku' and denies any report suggesting it was after. The author notes that the Prophet (peace be upon him) only recited Qunoot after ruku' for one month, implying it was an exception. Addressing the proof of Imam al-Shafi'i, who cites a hadith with the phrase 'qanata fi akhir al-witr' (he recited Qunoot in the latter part of Witr), the author explains that 'akhir' (latter part) applies to anything beyond half. Since the third rak'ah before ruku' is beyond half of Witr, it qualifies as 'akhir'. Thus, even this hadith supports the Hanafi position. The passage emphasizes that the correct practice, based on the primary evidence, is Qunoot before ruku'.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunoot): A specific supplication recited in Witr prayer.
وتر (witr): An odd-numbered prayer performed after the 'Isha prayer, consisting of an odd number of rak'ahs (typically three in the Hanafi school).
آخر الوتر (akhir al-witr): The latter part of Witr; interpreted as the third rak'ah before ruku' in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Qunoot in Witr is recited before ruku' according to the Hanafi school, based on the explicit hadith of Anas and a reasoned interpretation of the opposing proof.

Qunoot Throughout the Year: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Dispute with Shafi'i over whether Qunoot is prescribed for the whole year or only last half of Ramadan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that Qunoot in Witr is wajib throughout the year, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the practice of 'Umar.

Core Idea
The Prophet's unqualified command makes Qunoot wajib all year; 'Umar's practice is either about lengthening qiyam or not ijma'.

In this lesson, we examine a well-known dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the duration of Qunoot in Witr. The Hanafi school holds that reciting the Qunoot supplication in Witr is wajib every night of the year. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, restricts it to the last half of Ramadan. We will analyse the proofs on both sides and see how the Hanafi school refutes the Shafi'i reliance on the action of Caliph 'Umar.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What exactly does the Hanafi school rule regarding Qunoot in Witr? It is wajib and recited every night.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i restricts Qunoot to the last half of Ramadan and considers it mustahabb, not wajib.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
What is the Shafi'i main proof? The practice of 'Umar commanding Ubayy ibn Ka'b to recite Qunoot only in the last half, with no companion objecting, implying consensus (ijma').
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is twofold: First, 'Umar's command might refer to lengthening qiyam (qiyam), not the supplication. Second, even if it refers to the supplication, it is a companion's action, not binding, and there is no ijma' because Ibn 'Umar understood qunoot as lengthening qiyam.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence? Hanafis recite Qunoot every night; Shafi'is only in the last half of Ramadan.

Qunoot will be recited throughout the whole year, contrary to al-Shafi'i except for the last half of Ramadan, because of his (peace be upon him) statement to al-Hasan when he taught him the qunoot supplication: 'Place this in your witr' without specifying any time. The majority recite qunoot the whole year. His (Imam Shafi'i) difference is limited to the last half of Ramadan because the Prophet (peace be upon him) taught al-Hasan ibn 'Ali the qunoot supplication and said: 'Include this in your witr' without any detail. According to us, it is wajib to recite qunoot in witr throughout the year. According to Imam Shafi'i, it is only mustahabb to recite qunoot in the last half of Ramadan, and someone reciting it the whole year does so without dislike (as per certain transmission). The proof of Imam Shafi'i is the narration that 'Umar commanded Ubayy ibn Ka'b to lead in the nights of Ramadan and commanded qunoot in the last half of it. Our proof is the hadith that the Prophet taught the qunoot supplication to al-Hasan and then said: 'Place this in your witr.' There is no specification of Ramadan or other times, so it is established to recite qunoot all year. The answer to 'Umar's effect presented by Shafi'i is that by qunoot is meant lengthening qiyam (standing) in prayer; that is, 'Umar commanded Ubayy to lengthen qiyam in the last half. With this answer, this effect cannot be a proof for Shafi'i. And even if we accept that it means the qunoot supplication and not lengthening qiyam, we will respond that this is a companion's effect, and Imam Shafi'i considers companion's effects as proof. But from Shafi'i's side it can be said that this effect is proof because it is in the sense of ijma', since Ubayy led a large group of companions and no one objected, so it stands in place of ijma'. Then we respond that the difference of Ibn 'Umar is established because Ibn 'Umar says: 'I do not know qunoot except as lengthening qiyam'; meaning, in my view, qunoot has no meaning other than lengthening qiyam. So with the difference of Ibn 'Umar, how can there be consensus?
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the duration of Qunoot in Witr. The Hanafi school holds that reciting Qunoot in Witr is wajib throughout the entire year. The primary proof is the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) taught the supplication to al-Hasan ibn 'Ali and said 'Place this in your witr' without any temporal restriction. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, restricts Qunoot to the last half of Ramadan, citing the practice of 'Umar (radiAllahu 'anhu) who commanded Ubayy ibn Ka'b to recite Qunoot only in the last half of Ramadan. The Hanafi response to this proof is twofold: first, 'Umar's command might refer to lengthening qiyam (qiyam) rather than the Qunoot supplication; second, even if it refers to the supplication, it is a companion's saying (qawl al-sahabi) which is not binding, and there is no consensus due to the differing view of Ibn 'Umar who understood Qunoot as simply lengthening qiyam. The passage concludes that since Ibn 'Umar disputed the meaning, 'Umar's action cannot constitute ijma'. Therefore, the general command of the Prophet remains, requiring Qunoot throughout the year.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunoot): A specific supplication in Witr; in this passage, it is also argued to mean lengthening qiyam in prayer.
اجماع (ijma'): Consensus of the companions; here, the Shafi'i argument claims that 'Umar's action with no objection constitutes ijma'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires Qunoot in Witr every night of the year because the Prophet's command is unrestricted, and the Shafi'i reliance on 'Umar's practice is rebutted by alternative interpretation and lack of consensus.

Recitation in Each Rak'ah of Witr
Ruling that Fatihah and a Surah must be recited in each rak'ah of Witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on recitation in Witr prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain why it is classified as wajib.

Core Idea
Reciting Fatihah and a Surah in every Witr rak'ah is wajib—a cautious obligation due to the nature of Witr's evidence.

Witr prayer, though itself wajib in the Hanafi school, carries a recitation requirement that is also classified as wajib, not fard. This distinction arises from the epistemological weight of the evidence establishing Witr's obligation. In this lesson, we examine the ruling, its textual proof, and the reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting Surah al-Fatihah and an additional surah in each rak'ah of Witr. The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory, but not at the level of fard).
Wajib means omission requires sajdah al-sahw but does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary textual evidence is the Quranic verse: 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran' (So recite what is easy of the Quran).
This verse is from Surah al-Muzzammil (73:20).
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'faqra'u' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul. However, the verse only proves the obligation of recitation in general, not the specific requirement of Fatihah and an additional surah. The specification comes from other evidence (sunnah).
The verse is qat'i in transmission but zanni in indicating the specific recitation.
4
Understand the reason for wajib classification
Imam Abu Hanifah reasoned that since Witr's obligation is based on zanni evidence (qiyas), it resembles sunnah prayers in evidentiary strength. Therefore, out of caution (ihtiyat), the recitation in each rak'ah is made wajib, just as recitation in every rak'ah of sunnah and nafl prayers is wajib.
This is a precautionary measure to ensure the prayer is complete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقرأ في كل ركعة من الوتر فاتحة الكتاب وسورة لقوله تعالى فَاقْرَوا ما بد ترجمہ اور وتر کی ہر رکعت میں فاتحہ اور کوئی سورت پڑھے۔ کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرمایا کہ قرآن میں سے جو آسان ہورہا تشریح وتر کی ہر رکعت میں سورہ فاتحہ اور دوسری کسی سورت کا پڑھنا بالاتفاق واجب ہے صاحبین اور امام شافعی کے زر کا کہ وتر سنت ہے اور سنن و نوافل کی ہر رکعت میں قرآت ہے۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک وتر اگر چہ واجب ہے لیکن چونکہ کے شہوت سنت سے ہے اور سنت مفید یقین نہیں ہوتی اس لئے وتر کے واجب ہونے میں ایک گونہ شبہ رہا۔ پس احتیاں ان کے برکعت میں قرآت کو واجب قرار دیا، جیسا کہ سنتوں اور نوافل کی ہر رکعت میں قرآت واجب ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کا باری تعالیٰ کے قول فاقرؤا ما تيسر من القرآن سے استدلال کرنا مطلق قرآت کے وجوب پر ہوئی فاتحہ کی تعیین اور ضم سورت کی تعیین پر نہیں ہوسکتا۔
And he recites in every rak'ah of Witr Fatihah and a Surah, due to the statement of the Exalted: 'So recite what is easy [of the Quran].' Translation: And in every rak'ah of Witr, recite Fatihah and a Surah. Because Almighty said: 'So recite what is easy of the Quran.' Explanation: Reciting Surah Fatihah and another Surah in every rak'ah of Witr is wajib by consensus. Sahibayn and Imam Shafi'i opine that Witr is sunnah, and in sunnah and nafl prayers, recitation is required in every rak'ah. Imam Abu Hanifah holds that although Witr is wajib, since it resembles sunnah in weakness, and sunnah does not give certainty, there remains some doubt about its obligation. So out of caution, he made recitation in each rak'ah wajib, just as recitation in every rak'ah of sunan and nawafil is wajib. The author of Hidayah deducing from the verse 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' is for the obligation of absolute recitation, not for the specification of Fatihah and the addition of a surah.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about the recitation in Witr prayer. It states that it is wajib to recite Surah al-Fatihah and another Surah in each rak'ah of Witr, and this is agreed upon (bil-ittifaq) among the Hanafi school and others. The proof cited is the Quranic verse 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran' (So recite what is easy of the Quran). However, the commentary clarifies that this verse only establishes the obligation of recitation in general, not the specific requirement of Fatihah and an additional surah. The reason for making it wajib in each rak'ah, according to Imam Abu Hanifah, is that although Witr is wajib, it resembles sunnah in its level of evidence (ghayr qat'i), so out of caution, the recitation requirement is elevated to wajib in each rak'ah, similar to sunnah and nafl prayers where recitation is wajib in every rak'ah. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam Shafi'i hold Witr to be sunnah, but the ruling on recitation remains the same.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): A legal obligation established by zanni evidence; omission requires compensatory sajdah (sajdah al-sahw) but does not invalidate the prayer.
فاتحة الكتاب (Fatihah al-Kitab): Surah al-Fatihah, the opening chapter of the Quran.
قرآت (qira'at): Recitation of the Quran in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on reciting Surah al-Fatihah in each rak'ah of Witr according to the Hanafi school?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Mustahabb

Key Takeaway
Reciting Fatihah and a surah in each Witr rak'ah is wajib, not fard, due to the precautionary principle applied to Witr's zanni obligation.

Method of Qunoot: Takbir and Raising Hands
Ruling on Takbir and hand-raising for Qunoot in Witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Takbir and raising hands when beginning Qunoot in Witr, explain the evidence from the hadith of seven places, and respond to the objection regarding transitions between statements vs actions.

Core Idea
When starting Qunoot in Witr, saying Takbir and raising hands is wajib because the change of state requires it, as indicated by the hadith of seven hand-raisings.

This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the method of Qunoot in the Witr prayer. While the general rule is that transitions in prayer require Takbir, an objection arises: some claim that Takbir is only for action transitions, not for changes between statements like from Quran recitation to supplication. The Hanafi response clarifies that the hadith about raising hands in seven places, combined with the principle that hand-raising in prayer always accompanies Takbir, establishes the wajib nature of Takbir for Qunoot.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is saying Takbir and raising hands when starting Qunoot in Witr. According to the Hanafi school, this is wajib.
Wajib means obligatory; omission requires sajdah al-sahw.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'Hands are not raised except in seven places,' which includes Qunoot.
This is a hadith ahad, so its thubut is zanni, but it is accepted in practice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Raising hands in prayer is always accompanied by Takbir (as in iftitah and 'Eid). Therefore, the hadith commanding hand-raising for Qunoot also implies the Takbir.
The underlying principle is that a change of state in prayer requires Takbir, and Qunoot represents a change from Quran recitation to supplication.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars object: Takbir is only for transitions between actions (e.g., bowing), not between statements (e.g., from thana' to recitation). They argue the transition to Qunoot is a statement change, so no Takbir is needed.
This objection is answered by the Hanafi response.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: The hadith specifically commands raising hands for Qunoot, and since raising hands in prayer never occurs without Takbir (as seen in iftitah and 'Eid), the Takbir is necessarily included. Additionally, Qunoot is a 'semblance of recitation,' but the state change still warrants the Takbir.
Thus, the Hanafi position is solidly based on textual evidence and consistent practice.

Saying takbir is wajib. The proof is that the state of the person praying has changed; he was engaged in the reality of recitation (Quran) and will now engage in a semblance of recitation (qunoot supplication). Since takbirat are prescribed at times of transition, therefore saying takbir at this occasion is wajib. However, some scholars have objected to this proof. They say: Takbir is prescribed when a change occurs in actions, i.e., when moving from one action to another, like bowing. Takbir is not prescribed when there is a change in statements. Consider: when the person praying starts, there is no takbir at the transition from thana' to recitation, even though the state changes from thana' to recitation. So it is understood that takbir is not prescribed at the time of statements, but at the time of change of actions. The answer to this is that raising the hands at this state is based on the Prophet's statement: 'Do not raise the hands except in seven places' - and raising hands in prayer without takbir is not prescribed, like takbir al-iftitah and takbirat of 'Eid. Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the method of performing Qunoot in Witr. It states that when one intends to recite Qunoot, he should say Takbir (Allahu Akbar) and raise his hands, then recite the Qunoot supplication. The proof is a hadith that lists seven places in prayer where hands are raised, and Qunoot is among them. The author then discusses the reason: the change of state from Quran recitation to Qunoot (which resembles recitation) necessitates a Takbir, as transitions in actions generally require Takbir. An objection is raised: Takbir is only for transitions between actions (e.g., from standing to bowing), not between statements (e.g., from thana' to recitation). The response is that raising hands without Takbir is not prescribed in prayer (e.g., in Takbir al-Iftitah and 'Eid Takbirs, raising hands accompanies the Takbir). Therefore, since the hadith commands raising hands for Qunoot, it implies the Takbir as well.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunoot): A specific supplication in Witr; the act of reciting it includes raising hands and saying takbir.
تكبير (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar'; here it is wajib when starting qunoot due to change of state.

Recitation in Each Rak'ah of Witr Prayer
States the ruling on reciting Fatihah and a surah in Witr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation in Witr prayer and explain why it is classified as wajib rather than fard.

Core Idea
In every rak'ah of Witr, reciting al-Fatihah plus a surah is wajib, not fard—due to doubt in Witr's own obligation.

This lesson addresses a specific ruling within the Witr prayer: the recitation of al-Fatihah and an additional surah in each rak'ah. While in fard prayers, al-Fatihah and a surah are only required in the first two rak'ahs, Witr requires them in every rak'ah. The Hanafi school attaches a wajib status to this act, and the passage explains the reasoning behind this, including the intra-school difference on the nature of Witr itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that in every rak'ah of Witr, one recites Surah al-Fatihah and another surah. Determine the hukm (ruling) assigned to this recitation: is it fard, wajib, or sunnah?
The ruling is explicitly stated as 'wajib'.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the Quranic verse: 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran' (recite what is easy of the Quran). Identify the type of dalil and its authority.
The dalil is a Quranic verse (Surah al-Muzzammil 73:20), which is qati al-thubut.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the verse is used to prove the obligation of recitation. The commentary notes that the imperative implies obligation, but the verse is general and does not specify Witr or the requirement of al-Fatihah and an additional surah. Understand the limitations of this proof.
The verse only establishes the obligation of absolute recitation; specification comes from other evidence.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage mentions an intra-Hanafi difference: Imam Abu Hanifah considers Witr wajib, while the Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi'i consider it sunnah. Yet all agree that recitation in each rak'ah is wajib. Distinguish the theoretical difference from the practical ruling.
The ikhtilaf is about the nature of Witr, not the recitation rule itself.
5
Understand the tarjih and mufta bihi
The passage states that the ruling is 'bil-ittifaq' (by agreement) and that the mufta bihi is wujub. Appreciate how the doubt (shubha) in Witr's obligation leads to the wajib status, similar to sunnah prayers.
The mufta bihi position is clear: recitation in each rak'ah of Witr is wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة الوتر ويقرأ في كل ركعة من الوتر فاتحة الكتاب وسورة لقوله تعالى فَاقْرَوا ما بد ترجمہ اور وتر کی ہر رکعت میں فاتحہ اور کوئی سورت پڑھے۔ کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرمایا کہ قرآن میں سے جو آسان ہورہا تشریح وتر کی ہر رکعت میں سورہ فاتحہ اور دوسری کسی سورت کا پڑھنا بالاتفاق واجب ہے صاحبین اور امام شافعی کے زر کا کہ وتر سنت ہے اور سنن و نوافل کی ہر رکعت میں قرآت ہے۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک وتر اگر چہ واجب ہے لیکن چونکہ کے شہوت سنت سے ہے اور سنت مفید یقین نہیں ہوتی اس لئے وتر کے واجب ہونے میں ایک گونہ شبہ رہا۔ پس احتیاں ان کے برکعت میں قرآت کو واجب قرار دیا، جیسا کہ سنتوں اور نوافل کی ہر رکعت میں قرآت واجب ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کا باری تعالیٰ کے قول فاقرؤا ما تيسر من القرآن سے استدلال کرنا مطلق قرآت کے وجوب پر ہوئی فاتحہ کی تعیین اور ضم سورت کی تعیین پر نہیں ہوسکتا۔
Chapter of Witr Prayer. And he recites in every rak'ah of Witr Surah al-Fatihah and a surah, due to the Almighty's saying: 'So recite what is easy [of the Quran]'. Translation: And in every rak'ah of Witr, recite Fatihah and a surah. Because the Almighty said: 'From the Quran, whatever is easy.' Commentary: Reciting Surah al-Fatihah and another surah in every rak'ah of Witr is wajib by consensus. The Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi'i [say] that Witr is sunnah and in sunan and nawafil, recitation is [required] in every rak'ah. And according to Imam Abu Hanifah, although Witr is wajib, because it is from the sunnah of the Prophet and sunnah does not produce certainty, therefore there is some doubt in the obligation of Witr. So as a precaution, they made recitation in every rak'ah wajib, just as in sunnah and nafl prayers, recitation in every rak'ah is wajib. The author of al-Hidayah's deduction from the Almighty's saying 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran' is about the obligation of absolute recitation, not the specification of Fatihah and inclusion of a surah.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran regarding the recitation in Witr prayer. The text begins with the chapter heading 'Bāb Ṣalāt al-Witr' and immediately states the ruling: 'He recites in every rak'ah of Witr Surah al-Fatihah and a surah' with the proof from the Quranic verse 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran' (recite what is easy of the Quran). The commentary explains that this ruling is agreed upon (bil-ittifāq) as wājib. The passage then clarifies a key intra-Hanafi difference: while Imam Abu Hanifah considers Witr to be wājib, the two companions (Abū Yūsuf and Muhammad) along with Imam al-Shāfi‘ī consider it sunnah. Despite this difference, they all agree that recitation in every rak'ah of Witr is wājib. The reason for this, as explained, is that Imam Abu Hanifah views Witr as wājib but with some doubt due to its basis in sunnah (which is zannī), so precaution dictates making recitation wājib, similar to sunnah and nafl prayers where recitation is wājib in every rak'ah. The commentary further notes that the proof from the Quran (faqra'u ma tayassara) only establishes the obligation of absolute recitation in prayer, not the specific requirement of al-Fātihah and an additional sūrah; that specification comes from other evidence. Thus, the passage emphasizes the ruling and the reasoning behind it.

Key Terms
وتر (witr): A specific prayer performed after the night prayer, consisting of an odd number of rak'ahs (usually 1, 3, 5, etc.). In the Hanafi school, it is considered wajib according to Imam Abu Hanifah, but sunnah according to the Sahibayn and the majority of other schools.
سنن (sunan): Plural of sunnah; in this context, refers to the sunnah prayers (rawatib) and additional recommended prayers.
واجب (wajib): A legal obligation that is established by a zanni (non-definitive) proof. In Hanafi fiqh, it is a distinct category between fard (absolute obligation) and sunnah. Failure to perform a wajib without excuse incurs sin but does not invalidate the prayer if omitted unintentionally (requires sajdah sahw).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is wajib (obligatory with non-definitive proof).
C) It is sunnah (recommended).
D) It is mubah (permissible).

Key Takeaway
Recitation of al-Fatihah and an additional surah in every rak'ah of Witr is wajib, agreed upon by all Hanafi imams, with omission requiring sajdah sahw.
