The Obligatory Takbir for Qunut in Witr
Describes the method of qunut in Witr: raising hands, saying takbir, and reciting the supplication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on saying takbir and raising hands when beginning qunut in Witr, explain the proof from the hadith of the seven places, and evaluate the response to the objection that takbir is only for actions.

Core Idea
Takbir and raising hands for qunut in Witr are wajib, proven by the hadith of seven places.

This passage examines the Hanafi ruling on the method of performing qunut in Witr prayer. It establishes that when the worshipper intends to recite the qunut supplication in the third rak'ah, they must say takbir and raise their hands. The text provides both a rational proof based on the change of state and a textual proof from a hadith, and it addresses an objection that takbir is only for changes in actions, not words. By the end of this lesson, you will understand the basis for this ruling and how the Hanafi school defends it.

Guided Path
1
State the act and its ruling
Identify that the act under discussion is saying takbir and raising hands when beginning qunut in Witr prayer. The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory).
The passage explicitly says 'takbir kahnā wājib hai'.
2
Locate the primary proof (dalil)
Find the textual evidence: the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) saying 'Do not raise the hands except in seven places,' and qunut is mentioned among them.
This hadith is ahad (single-chain) but accepted by Hanafi scholars.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof yields the ruling)
Since the hadith commands raising hands in qunut, and raising hands in prayer is never done without takbir (e.g., takbir al-iftitah), the takbir is implied. Also, the change of state from recitation to supplication necessitates a takbir as a transition marker.
The text uses both textual and rational reasoning.
4
Note the objection and its basis
Some object that takbir is legislated only for changes in actions, not changes in words. They point out that moving from thana' to qira'ah (both words) does not require takbir.
This objection is a hypothetical challenge, not from another school.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The response is that in this case, the hands are raised (an action), and since raising hands without takbir is not legislated (as seen in other instances), the hadith indirectly proves the takbir. Therefore, the ruling stands.
The response distinguishes this transition from others by the presence of hand-raising.

قنوت پڑھنے کا طریقہ و ان اراد ان يقنت كبر لان الحالة قد اختلفت ورفع يديه وقنت لقوله عليه السلام لا ترفع الابر سبع مواطن وذكر منها القنوت ترجمہ اور اگر قنوت پڑھنا چاہئے تو تکبیر کہے کیونکہ حالت بدل گئی اور دونوں ہاتھ اٹھائے اور قنوت پڑھے کیونکہ نہ تو ہاتھ نہ اٹھائے جائیں مگر سات جگہوں میں اور انہیں سات میں قنوت کا ذکر کیا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ تیسری رکعت میں قرآت فاتحہ اور ضم سورت کے بعد جب دعاء قنوت پڑھنے کا ارادہ کرے تواب لیے ای الا کانوں تک اٹھائے اور تکبیر کہے پھر دعائے قنوت پڑھے۔ تکبیر کہنا واجب ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ مصلی کی حالت بدل گیا ایک حقیقت قرآۃ میں مشغول تھا اور اب شبیہ قرآت یعنی دعاء قنوت میں مشغول ہوگا اور چونکہ تکبیرات مشروع کی گئی ہیں جانا کے وقت ، اس لئے اس موقع پر بھی تکبیر کہنا واجب ہے۔ لیکن اس دلیل پر بعض حضرات نے اعتراض کیا ہے۔ وہ یہ کہ ایرانی کی گئی ہے جبکہ افعال کے اندر تبدیلی واقع ہو۔ یعنی ایک فعل سے دوسرے فعل کی طرف منتقل ہوتے وقت۔ جیسے جھکنے ان کے تکبیر مشروع ہے، اقوال کے اندر اختلاف کے وقت تکبیر مشروع نہیں ہوئی ہے۔ چنانچہ آپ غور کریں کہ مصلی جب کہ جو شروع کرتا ہے تو اس وقت تکبیر نہیں ہے۔ حالانکہ ثناء سے قرآت کی طرف حالت تبدیل ہو گئی ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ ان صا اقوال کے وقت تکبیر مشروع نہیں، بلکہ اختلاف افعال کے وقت مشروع ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس حالت میں ہاتھوں کا اٹھانا حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول لا ترفع الا يدى الا في سبع مواطن - اور نماز کے اندر ہاتھوں کا اٹھانا بغیر تکبیر کے غیر مشروع ہے۔ جیسے تکبیر افتتاح اور تکبیرات عیدین میں پس اس حدیث سے ثابت ہو جائے گا۔
Method of Reciting Qunut: And if he intends to recite qunut, he says takbir because the state has changed, and he raises his hands and recites qunut, due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Do not raise the hands except in seven places,' and he mentioned qunut among them. Translation: And if he wants to recite qunut, he should say takbir because the state has changed, and he raises both hands and recites qunut, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Hands are not raised except in seven places,' and he mentioned qunut among them. Commentary: The issue is that in the third rak'ah, after reciting al-Fatihah and an additional surah, when he intends to recite the qunut supplication, he should raise his hands to the ears and say takbir, then recite the qunut supplication. Saying takbir is wajib. The proof is that the state of the worshipper has changed: he was engaged in recitation (qira'ah), and now he will be engaged in something resembling recitation, i.e., the qunut supplication. And since takbirs are legislated at times of transition, therefore saying takbir at this occasion is wajib. But some have objected to this proof. They said: [Takbir] is legislated when there is a change in actions, i.e., when moving from one action to another, like at bowing, takbir is legislated; at times of change in words, takbir is not legislated. For example, when the worshipper begins [the prayer] and goes from thana' (glorification) to qira'ah, he does not say takbir. So it is known that takbir is not legislated at times of words, but rather at times of actions. The answer to this is: In this situation, raising the hands according to the Prophet's saying 'Do not raise the hands except in seven places' — and raising the hands in prayer without takbir is not legislated, like the takbir of iftitah and the takbirs of the two 'Ids. Thus, this hadith proves [the takbir].
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about the method of performing qunut in Witr prayer. It begins by presenting the ruling: when one intends to recite qunut in the third rak'ah, he should say takbir, raise his hands, and then recite the qunut supplication. The proof is a hadith that mentions raising hands in seven places, including qunut. The commentary then explains the reasoning: the worshipper's state changes from recitation (qira'ah) to supplication (which resembles recitation), so a takbir is performed to mark the transition, similar to other transitions in prayer like bowing. However, an objection is raised: takbir is legislated for changes in actions, not for changes in words; for example, when moving from thana' to qira'ah, no takbir is said. The response distinguishes that in this case, the hands are raised (as per the hadith), and raising the hands in prayer without takbir is not legislated (as in takbir al-iftitah and 'Id takbirs), so the hadith establishes that both actions (raising hands and saying takbir) are required. The passage thus confirms that saying takbir and raising hands are wajib when performing qunut in Witr.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunut): A special supplication recited in the last rak'ah of Witr prayer after the recitation of al-Fatihah and a surah, before bowing or after bowing according to some views. In this context, it is the supplication itself.
تکبیر (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar'. In this context, it refers to the takbir said when transitioning from recitation to qunut, which the text stipulates as wajib.
رفع الیدین (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands to the ears or shoulders. In this context, it is part of the qunut ritual, done when saying takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is sunnah (recommended).
B) It is wajib (obligatory).
C) It is mustahab (preferred).
D) It is makruh (disliked).

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, saying takbir and raising hands when performing qunut in Witr is wajib, based on the hadith of seven places and the principle that raising hands necessitates takbir.

Qunut Only in Witr and Following the Imam in Qunut
Inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi dispute on qunut and follower's action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qunut in Fajr, explain the inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school, and apply the intra-Hanafi rule for a follower when the imam recites qunut in Fajr.

Core Idea
Qunut is only for Witr; in Fajr it is abrogated, and a Hanafi follower should not recite it with the imam.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a classic inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is: whether qunut is performed in Fajr prayer. The Hanafi position, based on the practice of the Prophet and the caliphs, restricts qunut to Witr. The text then goes further, discussing what a Hanafi follower should do when praying behind a Shafi'i imam who recites qunut in Fajr, revealing an intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Hanifah, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf. We will walk through the proofs, the ikhtilaf, and the relied-upon position for the follower's action.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Recognize that the Hanafi school holds qunut is only for Witr, while Imam al-Shafi'i considers it sunnah in Fajr. This is the main inter-madhhab issue.
The text labels this as 'contrary to al-Shafi'i regarding Fajr.'
2
Analyze the Hanafi and Shafi'i proofs
Compare the two primary dalils: Ibn Mas'ud's hadith (Prophet did qunut for a month then left it) vs. Anas's hadith (Prophet continued qunut until death). Understand how the Hanafi school reconciles Anas's narration as referring to qunut nazilah (calamity) that was time-bound.
Also note the practice of Abu Bakr and Umar (no qunut in Fajr) as additional Hanafi evidence.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the follower's action
Identify the three positions: (1) Abu Hanifah and Muhammad: the follower remains silent (does not recite qunut); (2) Abu Yusuf: the follower follows the imam because it's a matter of ijtihad; (3) Two sub-views: stand silently or sit down to manifest opposition. The text says 'the first is more apparent' (al-awwal azhar).
The core principle: qunut in Fajr is mansukh (abrogated), so there is no following in an abrogated act.
4
Understand the broader principle of following a different-madhhab imam
The passage also states that it is permissible (ja'iz) to pray behind a Shafi'i imam generally, and that in Witr one should follow the imam in qunut. This shows the Hanafi tolerance for ikhtilaf in practice.
If the imam does something that the follower believes invalidates the prayer (like cupping/bleeding), following is not valid – but qunut in Fajr does not invalidate.
5
Conclude with the chosen view on recitation mode
The text ends with 'al-mukhtar fi al-qunut al-ikhfa'' – the chosen view is to recite qunut silently, because it is a supplication. This applies to Witr qunut as well.
This is a separate fiqh point that complements the discussion.

فيما نجب متابعة وقيل يقعد تحقيقا للمخالفة لان الساكت شریک الداعی والاول اظهر ودلت المسألة على جواز الاقتداء بالشفعوية وعلى المتابعة فى قراءة القنوت فى الوتر واذا علم المقتدى منه ما يزعم به فساد صلاته And he should not recite qunut in any prayer other than it (Witr), contrary to al-Shafi'i regarding Fajr, because Ibn Mas'ud narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited qunut in Fajr for a month and then left it. Translation: And do not recite qunut in any prayer other than Witr. There is a difference with Imam al-Shafi'i in Fajr. Because Ibn Mas'ud narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited qunut in Fajr for a month and then left it. Commentary: According to Hanafi scholars, there is no qunut in any prayer except Witr. Imam al-Shafi'i said that qunut in Fajr is sunnah. ... (section on Abu Bakr and Umar) ... And the ruling for the follower (muqtadi) regarding qunut: [If the imam recites qunut in Fajr prayer], according to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, those behind him remain silent. Abu Yusuf said: They follow him, because the follower is subject to his imam, and qunut in Fajr is a matter of ijtihad. The [view of the] two is that it is abrogated (mansukh) and there is no following in it. Then it is said: He should remain standing to follow him in what is required to follow; and it is said: He should sit to manifest opposition, because the silent one is a partner of the supplicator. And the first is more apparent. This issue indicates the permissibility of following a Shafi'i imam and following in reciting qunut in Witr. And if the follower knows from him (the imam) something that would corrupt his prayer, like cupping and the like, then following him is not sufficient. The chosen view regarding qunut is to recite it silently, because it is a supplication.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding qunut in prayers other than Witr. It addresses two main issues: (1) whether qunut is performed in any prayer besides Witr, and (2) what the follower should do if the imam performs qunut in Fajr. The Hanafi position is that qunut is only for Witr, not for Fajr or any other prayer. The text provides the Hanafi proof from Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet only did qunut in Fajr for a month and then left it, and from the practice of Abu Bakr and Umar who did not do it. Imam al-Shafi'i argues from a hadith of Anas that the Prophet did qunut in Fajr until he died. The Hanafi response is that the qunut in Fajr was only for a specific reason (a calamity) and was later abrogated. Then the text discusses the ruling for a muqtadi (follower) when the imam (who may be Shafi'i) performs qunut in Fajr: According to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, the follower should remain silent (not follow the imam in qunut), while Abu Yusuf says he should follow because it is a matter of ijtihad. The text states that the more apparent view (al-awwal azhar) is to remain standing but not recite qunut, or to sit to show opposition. However, it also mentions that it is permissible to follow a Shafi'i imam, and that in Witr one should follow the imam in qunut. The passage concludes that the chosen view (al-mukhtar) is to recite qunut silently (ikhfa'), because it is a supplication.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunut): A supplication recited in prayer, typically in Witr. In this passage, the focus is on qunut in Fajr, which the Hanafi school restricts to exceptional circumstances (qunut nazilah).
مقتدی (muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer. The passage discusses the muqtadi's action when the imam performs qunut in Fajr.
اخفاء (ikhfa'): Reciting silently, i.e., with the lips moving but not audible. The chosen view for qunut is ikhfa' because it is a supplication (du'a).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Recite qunut with the imam.
B) Remain silent and not recite qunut.
C) Leave the congregation.
D) Recite a different supplication.

Key Takeaway
Qunut is only for Witr in the Hanafi school; in Fajr it is abrogated, and a Hanafi follower should not recite it behind an imam, though the prayer remains valid regardless.

Qunut in Fajr and Following a Shafi'i Imam
States Hanafi ruling on Qunut in Fajr and intra-Hanafi dispute on following a Shafi'i imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Qunut in Fajr, explain the evidence for abrogation, and apply the mufta bihi rule for a Hanafi follower behind a Shafi'i imam.

Core Idea
Qunut in Fajr is abrogated; a Hanafi follower stands silently when the Shafi'i imam recites it.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position that Qunut is only prescribed in Witr, and the evidence from the Prophet's practice that Qunut in Fajr was a temporary measure. It then addresses the practical scenario when a Hanafi follower prays behind a Shafi'i imam who recites Qunut in Fajr, detailing the intra-Hanafi disagreement and the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general Hanafi position
State that Qunut is only performed in Witr, not in any other prayer, contrary to the Shafi'i school which considers it sunnah in Fajr.
2
Examine the Hanafi evidence (dalil)
Analyze the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (qunut for one month then abandoned) and the practice of Abu Bakr and Umar (no qunut in Fajr). Understand why these indicate abrogation.
The hadith of Anas is interpreted as referring to a specific period, not a continuous sunnah.
3
Understand the Shafi'i evidence and Hanafi response
Note the Shafi'i reliance on the hadith of Anas that the Prophet performed qunut in Fajr until his death. The Hanafi response distinguishes between qunut al-nazilah (temporary) and a permanent sunnah.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different interpretations of the same actions.
4
Apply the intra-Hanafi dispute on following
When a Shafi'i imam recites qunut in Fajr, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say the Hanafi follower remains silent (sukut); Abu Yusuf says follow the imam. Identify the mufta bihi: silence.
The follower stands silently – he does not sit or leave the prayer early.
5
Determine the practical application
The follower follows the imam in standing (the prescribed part) and remains silent during the qunut (the non-prescribed part). This shows the permissibility of praying behind a Shafi'i imam in general, unless the follower knows the imam's prayer is invalid.
Qunut itself (in Witr) should be recited silently as it is a supplication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة الوتر
والولايقت في صلوة غيرها خلافا للشافعى فى الفجر لما روى ابن مسعود انه عليه السلام قنت في صلوة الفجر شهرا ثم تركه
تشریح علماء احناف کے نزدیک سوائے وتر کے کسی نماز میں قنوت نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی نے کہا کہ فجر کی نماز میں قنوت مسنون ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل حدیث انس ہے کان النبی يقنت في صلوة الفجر الى ان فارق الدنیا یعنی حضور فجر کی نماز میں قنوت پڑھتے تھے۔ یہاں تک کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم دنیا سے تشریف لے گئے۔ احناف کی دلیل ابن مسعود کی حدیث ہے ان النبي قنت فى صلوة الفجر شهرا يدعو على حي من أحياء العرب حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایک ماہ فجر کی نماز میں قنوت پڑھا عرب کے کسی قبیلہ کے لئے بددعا فرماتے تھے۔ خود حضرت انسؓ سے مروی ہے کہ قال قت رسول الله في صلاة الفجر شهرا او قال اربعين يوما على اهل ذكوان و عصبة حين قلتوا اهراء و هم سبعون رجلا او ثمانون یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایک ماہ یا چالیس یوم قنوت پڑھا، مقصد ان لوگوں پر بددعا کرنا تھا جنہوں نے ستر یا اسی قراء کوشہید کر دیا تھا اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فجر کی نماز میں چند یوم کے علاوہ دعاء قنوت نہیں پڑھی۔ ابو عثمان نبندی نے با صليت خلف ابی بکر سنتين و صليت خلف عمر کذلک فلم ار واحدا منهما يقنت في صلوة الفجر

مان قنت الامام في الصلوة الفجر يسكت من خلفه عند ابی حنیفه و محمد و قال ابويوسف يتبعة لانه تبع الإمامه والقنوت في الفجر مجتهد فيه ولهما انه منسوخ ولا متابعة فيه ثم قيل يقف قائما ليتابعه فيما نجب متابعة وقيل يقعد تحقيقا للمخالفة لان الساكت شریک الداعی والاول اظهر ودلت المسألة على جواز الاقتداء بالشفعوية وعلى المتابعة فى قراءة القنوت فى الوتر واذا علم المقتدى منه ما يزعم به فساد صلاته كـالـفـصـد وغيره لايجزيه الاقتداء به والمختار فى القنوت الاخفاء لانه دعاء

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر امام شافعی المسلک نے فجر کی نماز میں دعاء قنوت پڑھی اور مقتدی حنفی المذہب ہوتا میں میں طرفین کے نزدیک حنفی المسلک مقتدی سکوت کرے، قنوت نہ پڑھے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقتدی بالیقین امام کا ہے۔ اور اصل یہ ہے کہ مقتدی امام کی متابعت کرے۔ اور فجر کی نماز میں قنوت پڑھنا مختلف فیہ ہے کیونکہ بعض مجتہدین کے نزدیک و نماز میں قنوت پڑھنا مسنون ہے اور بعض کے نزدیک فجر کی نماز میں قنوت تھا مگر منسوخ ہو گیا۔ پس اس اختلاف کی وجہ سے فجر کی نماز قنوت کا پڑھنا نہ پڑھنانہ مشکوک اور محتمل ہے۔ اور یہ اصول ثابت شدہ ہے کہ اصل اور یقینی چیز کو شک کی وجہ سے ترک نہیں کیا جاتا ال۔ متابعت امام کو ترک نہ کیا جائے بلکہ امام کی متابعت کرتے ہوئے حنفی المسلک مقتدی بھی قنوت پڑھے۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ فجر کی نماز میں قنوت پڑھنا منسوخ ہو چکا کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فجر میں ایک ماہ قنوت پڑھا اور پھر اس کو پی دیا۔ اور منسوخ میں متابعت نہیں کی جاتی اس لئے حنفی المسلک مقتدی قنوت پڑھنے میں امام کی متابعت نہ کرے بلکہ خاموش کھڑار ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ مقتدی جب متابعت نہیں کرے گا تو کیا کرے تو اس بارے میں بعض حضرات کی رائے تو یہ ہے کہ مقتدی خاموشی رہے تا کہ جس چیز میں متابعت واجب ہے اس میں متابعت ہو جائے یعنی قیام اور قنوت دو چیزیں ہیں۔ پس حنفی المسلک مقتدی قیری اپنے امام کی متابعت کرے۔ اور قنوت میں متابعت نہ کرے۔ اور بعض کا قول ہے کہ جب شافعی المسلک امام قنوت پڑھنا شروع کرے تو خفی المسلک مقتدی بیٹھ جائے۔ تا کہ امام کی مکمل مجان و ظاہر ہو۔ کیونکہ خاموش رہنے والا دعاء کرنے والے کا شریک شمار ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے مقتدی قرآت نہیں کرتا بلکہ خاموش رہتا ہے لیکن الرسا با وجود قرات میں امام کا شریک ہوتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ قول اول اظہر ہے۔ یعنی ساکت کھڑا رہنا یہی اظہر ہے۔ صاحب عنایہ نے اظہر ہونے کی وجہ یہ ذکر کی ہے امام کا فعل مشروع اور غیر مشروع دونوں پر مشتمل ہے پس قیام جو مشروع ہے اس میں امام کی اتباع کرے اور قنوت جو غیر مشروع ہے نہ میں اتباع نہ کرے بلکہ خاموش کھڑار ہے۔ عین الہدایہ میں لکھا ہے کہ قول اول اس لئے اظہر ہے کہ نماز میں امام کی مخالفت پیدا کرنا اگر ا کسیر کن یا شرط میں نہ ہو دو وجہ سے برا ہے۔ اول تو یہ شان اقتداء کے خلاف ہے کیونکہ حدیث میں ہے انـمـا جـعـل الامام ليزنه یعنی امام تو اسی لئے ہوتا ہے کہ اس کی متابعت کی جائے۔ دوم یہ کہ یہ فعل اگر چہ کثیر نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے مفسد نہیں لیکن قلیل مکروہ ہے۔ بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ جب امام قنوت پڑھے تو حنفی المسلک مقتدی بیٹھ کر التحیات وغیرہ پڑھ کر امام سے پہلے ہی سلام پھیر ۔ کیونکہ امام حنفی المسلک مقتدی کے نزدیک بدعت میں مشغول ہوگیا لہذا اس کے انتظار کے کوئی معنی نہیں ہیں۔ مصنف ہدایہ نے اس قول کو ذکر نہیں کیا کیونکہ اس صورت میں سلام جو امر مشروع ہے اس میں امام کی مخالفت کرنا لازم آتا ہے اور
Chapter of Salat al-Witr. And he does not perform qunut in any prayer other than it, contrary to al-Shafi'i regarding Fajr, because Ibn Mas'ud narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed qunut in Fajr prayer for a month then left it. Explanation: According to Hanafi scholars, there is no qunut in any prayer except Witr. Imam al-Shafi'i said that qunut in Fajr prayer is sunnah. Al-Shafi'i's evidence is the hadith of Anas: 'The Prophet would perform qunut in Fajr prayer until he departed this world.' The Hanafi evidence is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet performed qunut in Fajr for a month, supplicating against a tribe of Arabs. Also from Anas himself: 'The Messenger of God performed qunut in Fajr for a month, or forty days, against the people of Dhakwan and their group when they killed the reciters, seventy or eighty men.' This hadith shows that the Prophet only recited qunut for a few days. Abu Uthman al-Nahdi said: 'I prayed behind Abu Bakr for two years and behind Umar similarly, and I did not see either of them performing qunut in Fajr.' Then if the imam performs qunut in Fajr prayer, those behind him remain silent according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf said they follow him because the follower is subordinate to the imam, and qunut in Fajr is a matter of ijtihad. Their (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's) evidence is that it is abrogated, and there is no following in abrogated matters. Then it is said: he stands silently to follow him in what requires following, and it is said: he sits to actualize opposition, because the silent one is a partner in the supplication. The first is more apparent. And this issue indicates the permissibility of following a Shafi'i, and indicates following the imam in reciting qunut in Witr. And if the follower knows from him (the imam) something that would invalidate his prayer, like cupping etc., it is not permissible for him to follow him. And the preferred method in qunut is to recite it silently because it is a supplication. Explanation: The scenario is that if a Shafi'i imam recites qunut in Fajr and a Hanafi follower (is behind him), according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) the Hanafi follower remains silent, does not recite qunut. Imam Abu Yusuf's evidence is that the follower is definitely subordinate to the imam, and the principle is that the follower follows the imam. And performing qunut in Fajr is disputed because some mujtahids consider it sunnah and others consider it abrogated. Due to this difference, reciting qunut in Fajr or not is doubtful and probable. And the established principle is that the certain and definite thing is not abandoned due to doubt. Therefore, following the imam should not be abandoned; rather, while following the imam, the Hanafi follower should also recite qunut. The evidence of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that qunut in Fajr is abrogated because the Prophet performed it for one month and then left it. And there is no following in abrogated matters. So the Hanafi follower does not follow the imam in reciting qunut but stands silent. As for what the follower should do when not following, some scholars say the follower remains silent so that he follows the imam in what is obligatory to follow, i.e., standing and qunut are two things. So the Hanafi follower follows the imam in standing and does not follow in qunut. Others say when the Shafi'i imam starts qunut, the Hanafi follower sits down to show complete opposition, because the silent one is considered a partner in supplication, just as the follower does not recite but remains silent yet becomes a partner in recitation. The author of Hidayah said the first view is more apparent: standing silently. The author of Inayah mentioned the reason: the imam's action consists of both prescribed and non-prescribed elements, so he follows in the prescribed (standing) and does not follow in the non-prescribed (qunut) but stands silent. In 'Ayn al-Hidayah it is written that the first view is more apparent because opposing the imam in prayer, if not in the number of rak'ahs or conditions, is bad for two reasons: first, it opposes the dignity of following, because the hadith says 'The imam is appointed only to be followed'; second, this action, though not invalidating due to being not excessive, is nevertheless disliked (makruh). Some said that when the imam recites qunut, the Hanafi follower should sit and recite tashahhud etc. and finish the prayer with salam before the imam, because the imam has engaged in an innovation according to the Hanafi, so there is no point in waiting. The author of Hidayah did not mention this view because in that case opposing the imam in salam, which is prescribed, becomes necessary, and...
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on Salat al-Witr. It addresses two main issues: the general Hanafi position that Qunut is not recited in any prayer other than Witr, and the specific situation when a Hanafi follower prays behind a Shafi'i imam who recites Qunut in Fajr. The Hanafi school holds that Qunut in Fajr was a temporary practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) for about a month, and was then abrogated. This is supported by the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. In contrast, the Shafi'i school considers it a sunnah based on the hadith of Anas that the Prophet continued Qunut in Fajr until his death. The Hanafi response explains that the Prophet's Qunut in Fajr was for a specific reason (supplication against a tribe) and was not continuous. The passage then discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the follower's action. According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, the follower remains silent and does not recite Qunut, because the practice is abrogated. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that the follower should follow the imam in Qunut because following the imam is the default, and the matter is ikhtilafi (subject to ijtihad). The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as stated by al-Marghinani, that the follower stands silently. The follower should not sit or exit the prayer, because that would create unnecessary opposition. The passage also notes that this shows the permissibility of praying behind a Shafi'i imam, except when the follower knows that the imam's prayer is invalid due to something like cupping (i.e., a nullifier). Finally, the preferred method for Qunut (in Witr) is to recite it silently, as it is a supplication.

Key Terms
قنوت (Qunut): A supplication recited in a standing position during prayer, specifically in Witr according to Hanafis
سکوت (Sukut): The follower remains silent and does not recite Qunut when the imam recites it
منسوخ (Mansukh): Abrogated—the ruling of Qunut in Fajr was abrogated by the Prophet's leaving it

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should a Hanafi follower do when praying behind a Shafi'i imam who recites Qunut in Fajr?
A) Recite Qunut silently along with the imam
B) Remain silent and stand still
C) Sit down until the imam finishes Qunut
D) Leave the prayer immediately

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds Qunut in Fajr is abrogated; a follower behind a Shafi'i imam should stand silently during Qunut.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Hanafi Follower's Qunut Behind Shafi'i Imam in Fajr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on follower reciting qunut with Shafi'i imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a follower reciting qunut behind a Shafi'i imam in Fajr and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and the majority.

Core Idea
A Hanafi follower stands silent during qunut – abrogation overrides the general obligation to follow the imam.

When a Hanafi prays behind a Shafi'i imam who recites qunut in Fajr, a conflict arises between the duty to follow the imam and the Hanafi position that qunut in Fajr is abrogated. This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi disagreement on how to resolve this, tracing the arguments of Imam Abu Yusuf and the majority, and the preferred ruling (mufta bihi) given by al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal question
What is the specific fiqh issue being debated? State it clearly: whether a Hanafi follower should recite qunut behind a Shafi'i imam in Fajr.
The ikhtilaf is intra-Hanafi – both sides are Hanafi, but they differ on which principle takes precedence.
2
Examine Imam Abu Yusuf's position and proof
Imam Abu Yusuf argues that the follower should recite qunut because following the imam is a certain obligation. He uses the usul principle: certainty is not abandoned for doubt – since abrogation of qunut is disputed, the certain rule (mutaba'ah) prevails.
This position prioritizes the general principle of following over the specific evidence of abrogation.
3
Examine the majority position and proof
The majority (including Muhammad al-Shaybani and later Hanafis) hold that the follower should stand silent. Their proof is that qunut in Fajr was abrogated by the Prophet's practice (he recited for one month then stopped), and one does not follow in abrogated acts. They prioritize the specific evidence of abrogation over the general principle of mutaba'ah.
This position relies on hadith evidence (dalil naqli) to establish abrogation.
4
Analyze the alternative of sitting down
Some scholars suggested the follower should sit during qunut to clearly avoid participating. But al-Marghinani rejects this because it involves moving (a potentially invalidating action) and contradicts the essence of following the imam.
The preferred solution is to remain standing while refraining from reciting – this follows the imam in standing (which is legitimate) but not in qunut (which is abrogated).
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi ruling
Al-Marghinani declares the view of standing silent as 'azhar' (more apparent). This is the operative ruling for fatwa: the Hanafi follower stands silently during qunut in Fajr without reciting or sitting.
This ruling balances the duty to follow with the duty to avoid abrogated practices.

رہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ مقتدی جب متابعت نہیں کرے گا تو کیا کرے تو اس بارے میں بعض حضرات کی رائے تو یہ ہے کہ مقتدی خاموش رہے تا کہ جس چیز میں متابعت واجب ہے اس میں متابعت ہو جائے یعنی قیام اور قنوت دو چیزیں مخالفت ظاہر ہو۔ کیونکہ خاموش رہنے والا دعاء کرنے والے کا شریک شمار ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے مقتدی قرآت نہیں کرتا بلکہ خاموش رہتا ہے لیکن [الرسا] با وجود قرات میں امام کا شریک ہوتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ قول اول اظہر ہے۔ یعنی ساکت کھڑا رہنا یہی اظہر ہے۔ صاحب عنایہ نے اظہر ہونے کی وجہ یہ ذکر کی ہے امام کا فعل مشروع اور غیر مشروع دونوں پر مشتمل ہے پس قیام جو مشروع ہے اس میں امام کی اتباع کرے اور قنوت جو غیر مشروع ہے اس میں اتباع نہ کرے بلکہ خاموش کھڑا رہے۔ عین الہدایہ میں لکھا ہے کہ قول اول اس لئے اظہر ہے کہ نماز میں امام کی مخالفت پیدا کرنا اگر کثیر نہ ہو تو دو وجہ سے برا ہے۔ اول تو یہ شان اقتداء کے خلاف ہے کیونکہ حدیث میں ہے انما جعل الامام لیزونہ یعنی امام تو اسی لئے ہوتا ہے کہ اس کی متابعت کی جائے۔ دوم یہ کہ یہ فعل اگر چہ کثیر نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے مفسد نہیں لیکن قلیل مکروہ ہے۔ بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ جب امام قنوت پڑھے تو حنفی المسلک مقتدی بیٹھ کر التحیات وغیرہ پڑھ کر امام سے پہلے ہی سلام پھیر دے۔ کیونکہ امام حنفی المسلک مقتدی کے نزدیک بدعت میں مشغول ہوگیا لہذا اس کے انتظار کے کوئی معنی نہیں ہیں۔ مصنف ہدایہ نے اس قول کو ذکر نہیں کیا کیونکہ اس صورت میں سلام جو امر مشروع ہے اس میں امام کی مخالفت کرنا لازم آتا ہے اور کسی طرح مناسب نہیں۔
Chapter of Witr Prayer. (Commentary) ... and it is abrogated, and one does not follow in what is abrogated. Then it was said: (the follower) should remain standing so that he follows the imam in that where following is (required). And some said: the follower should sit so that opposition becomes evident, because the silent one is a partner of the supplicant. And the first is more apparent. The issue indicates the permissibility of following a Shafi'i imam, and indicates that in witr qunut he should follow (the imam). And when the Hanafi follower knows for certain that the Shafi'i imam has done something that invalidates his prayer, like cupping etc., then it is not permissible for that Hanafi to follow him. And in qunut, the preferred (method) is concealment because it is a supplication. Explanation of the issue: If a Shafi'i imam recites qunut in Fajr prayer and the follower is Hanafi, according to the two sides (Abu Yusuf and others), the Hanafi follower should remain silent and not recite qunut. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is that the follower is definitely following the imam, and the principle is that the follower follows the imam. And reciting qunut in Fajr is disputed because according to some mujtahids, qunut in Fajr is sunnah, and according to others, qunut in Fajr was (prescribed) but abrogated. So due to this dispute, reciting or not reciting qunut in Fajr is doubtful and probable. And it is an established principle that a certain and definite matter is not abandoned due to doubt. So following the imam should not be abandoned; rather, while following the imam, the Hanafi follower should also recite qunut. The proof of the other side is that qunut in Fajr has been abrogated because the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited qunut for one month in Fajr and then left it. And one does not follow in what is abrogated. Therefore the Hanafi follower should not follow the imam in reciting qunut, but should stand silently. As for what the follower should do when he does not follow, regarding this, some scholars opine that the follower should remain silent so that he follows in that where following is obligatory, i.e., standing and qunut are two separate things. So the Hanafi follower should follow his imam in standing, and not follow in qunut. And others say that when the Shafi'i imam starts reciting qunut, the Hanafi follower should sit, so that complete opposition to the imam becomes evident, because the silent one is considered a partner of the supplicant, just as a follower does not recite (Quran) but remains silent, yet [the man?] is a partner of the imam in recitation despite that. The author of Hidayah said: the first opinion is more apparent, i.e., remaining silent while standing is more apparent. The author of 'Inayah mentioned the reason for it being more apparent: the imam's action includes both legitimate and illegitimate; so he follows the imam in standing which is legitimate, and does not follow in qunut which is illegitimate, but stands silent. In 'Ayn al-Hidayah it is written: the first opinion is more apparent because creating opposition to the imam in prayer, if not excessive, is bad for two reasons: first, it is against the essence of following, because the hadith says 'the imam is only appointed to be followed'; second, this action, even if it does not invalidate due to being not excessive, is disliked if insignificantly small. Some scholars said: when the imam recites qunut, the Hanafi follower should sit and recite al-Tahiyyat etc. and then give salam before the imam, because the imam has engaged in a bid'ah according to the Hanafi follower, so there is no sense in waiting for him. The author of Hidayah did not mention this saying because in that case opposing the imam in salam, which is legitimate, becomes necessary, and that is not appropriate.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the conduct of a Hanafi follower (muqtadi) praying behind a Shafi'i imam who recites qunut in Fajr prayer. The central issue is whether the follower should also recite qunut, remain silent while standing, or sit down. The text presents two main views: the first (attributed to the majority of Hanafi scholars including Imam Abu Yusuf initially?) holds that the follower should remain silent and standing, following the imam in the permissible part (standing) but not in the qunut which is considered abrogated. The second view (attributed to some) says the follower should sit to show complete opposition. The author of Hidayah, al-Marghinani, declares the first view as 'aẓhar' (more apparent), and the commentary from 'Inayah and 'Ayn al-Hidayah supports this, citing the hadith that the imam is to be followed. The passage also discusses a third extreme view (not mentioned by al-Marghinani) that the follower should give salam early, but this is rejected because it involves opposition in a legitimate act. The discussion highlights the principle that doubt does not override certainty, but here the Hanafi certainty of abrogation takes precedence over the general principle of following the imam. The practical ruling (mufta bihi) is that the Hanafi follower stands silently during qunut, without reciting or sitting.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunūt): A supplication (dua) recited in prayer, specifically in witr and according to some in Fajr.
متابعت (mutāba‘at): Following the imam in actions of prayer.
اخفاء (ikhfā’): Reciting quietly, such that one hears oneself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in Al-Hidayah, what should a Hanafi follower do when a Shafi'i imam recites qunut in Fajr?
A) Recite qunut with the imam
B) Stand silently without reciting
C) Sit down until the imam finishes
D) Recite the Quran loudly

Key Takeaway
When a Hanafi follower encounters a Shafi'i imam reciting qunut in Fajr, the mufta bihi ruling is to stand silently – following the imam in the permissible action (standing) but not in the abrogated qunut.

Following a Non-Hanafi Imam: General Permissibility and Its Exception
Derived ruling: Hanafi may follow Shafi'i imam in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on following a non-Hanafi imam and identify the condition that prohibits it.

Core Idea
A Hanafi may follow a non-Hanafi imam unless he knows the imam's prayer is invalid by Hanafi standards.

The passage extracts two key rulings from an earlier discussion on qunut: first, that it is generally permissible for a Hanafi to pray behind a Shafi'i, Maliki, or Hanbali imam; second, that this permissibility has a critical exception—if the Hanafi knows the imam has done something that invalidates prayer according to Hanafi fiqh (e.g., broken wudu), following becomes impermissible. This ruling highlights the practical interaction between madhahib and the importance of certainty in ritual purity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
What does the passage say about the permissibility of a Hanafi following a Shafi'i, Maliki, or Hanbali imam? It states it is permissible (ja'iz).
2
Identify the exception
Under what condition does the permissibility cease? When the Hanafi knows for certain that the imam has committed an act that invalidates prayer according to Hanafi fiqh.
3
Understand the basis of the general ruling
Why is the general ruling permissibility? Because the differences in qunut (Fajr vs Witr) do not affect the validity of the prayer; they are subsidiary issues.
The passage mentions that in Witr, where qunut is wajib, the follower should recite qunut.
4
Understand the basis of the exception
Why does the permissibility become invalid when the imam's state is known? Because the Hanafi follower considers the imam to be in hadath (ritual impurity), and following an imam in hadath is invalid in the Hanafi school.
The imam may be valid according to his own madhhab but invalid according to the follower's madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودلت المسألة على جواز الاقتداء اس عبارت سے یہ بیان کرنا مقصود ہے کہ یہ مسئلہ دو باتوں پر دلالت کرتا ہے اول یہ کہ حنفی المذہب کا شافعی المذہب کی اقتداء کرنا جائز ہے۔ اسی طرح مالکی اور حنبلی کی اقتداء کرنا بھی جائز ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ مقتدی قنوت وتر میں اپنے امام کی متابعت کرے گا۔ کیونکہ اختلاف قنوت فجر میں متابعت کرنے کے سلسلہ میں ہے نہ کہ قنوت وتر میں۔ پس جہاں قنوت مسنون بلکہ واجب ہے وہاں مقتدی خاموش نہ رہے گا بلکہ قنوت پڑھے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اگر حنفی المسلک مقتدی کو اپنے شافعی المسلک امام کی طرف سے یقینی طور پر کوئی ایسی بات معلوم ہو جائے کہ احناف کے مذہب کے مطابق اس کی نماز فاسد ہو جاتی ہے تو اس حنفی کے لئے اس کی اقتداء کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ مثلا شافعی المسلک امام نے وضو کیا پھر فصد وغیرہ لگوائی یا غیر سبیلین سے خروج نجاست پایا گیا۔ اور وضو کا اعادہ نہیں کیا تو حنفی کے لئے اس کی اقتداء کرنا جائز نہیں ہو گا کیونکہ یہ چیزیں شوافع کے نزدیک اگر چہ ناقض وضو نہیں لیکن احناف کے نزدیک ناقض ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ حنفی المذہب مقتدی کے گمان کے مطابق اس کا امام محدث ہے اور محدث کے پیچھے اقتداء کرنا جائز نہیں۔
And the issue indicates the permissibility of following. By this expression it is intended to state that this issue indicates two things: First, that a Hanafi following a Shafi'i is permissible. Similarly, following a Maliki or Hanbali is also permissible. Second, that the follower will follow his imam in witr qunut, because the dispute is about following in Fajr qunut, not witr qunut. So where qunut is sunnah, rather wajib, the follower will not remain silent but will recite qunut. The author of Hidayah says: if the Hanafi follower knows for certain from his Shafi'i imam something that, according to the Hanafi school, invalidates his prayer, then it is not permissible for that Hanafi to follow him. For example, the Shafi'i imam performed wudu, then underwent cupping etc., or excretion from other than the two passages was found, and he did not repeat wudu. Then it is not permissible for the Hanafi to follow him, because these things, although not invalidators of wudu according to Shafi'is, are invalidators according to Hanafis. Therefore, according to the assumption of the Hanafi follower, his imam is in a state of ritual impurity (hadath), and following one in hadath is not permissible.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is a derived ruling (istinbat) from the previous maṣ'alah. The author of Hidayah explicitly states that the previous discussion about qunut in Fajr yields two conclusions: first, that it is generally permissible for a Hanafi to follow a non-Hanafi imam (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) in prayer. This is based on the fact that the difference in qunut does not affect the validity of the prayer; it is a subsidiary issue. Second, in witr prayer, where qunut is wajib, the Hanafi follower should recite qunut behind the imam because there is no dispute about its abrogation. However, there is an important exception: if the Hanafi follower knows with certainty that the imam has done something that invalidates prayer according to Hanafi fiqh (like breaking wudu through cupping or other non-standard exits), then it becomes unlawful to follow that imam, because the imam is considered in a state of hadath. This is a practical application of the principle that one cannot pray behind an imam whose ritual purity is doubtful in a way that contradicts one's own madhhab.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtidā’): Following an imam in prayer.
محدث (muḥdith): One who is in a state of ritual impurity requiring wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it prohibited for a Hanafi to follow a Shafi'i imam in prayer?
A) When the imam is Shafi'i
B) When the Hanafi knows the imam's prayer is invalid by Hanafi fiqh
C) When it is not Fajr or Witr
D) When the Hanafi is unsure about the imam's wudu

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi may follow a non-Hanafi imam unless he has certain knowledge that the imam's prayer is invalid by Hanafi standards.

Preferred Method of Reciting Qunut: Ikhfa
Ruling that qunut should be recited silently

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that qunut should be recited silently (ikhfa), explain the Quranic proof, and summarize the opposing view and its rebuttal.

Core Idea
Qunut is a supplication, and supplication is best done silently.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the manner of reciting qunut during witr prayer. The author affirms that the preferred method is ikhfa (silent recitation), reasoning that qunut is essentially a supplication (du'a), and Allah commands His servants to call upon Him in humility and secrecy. An alternative view advocating aloud recitation is examined and rejected on the basis that qunut is not Quran. Understanding this ruling helps avoid confusion about proper practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting the qunut supplication. The ruling is that it is preferred to recite silently (ikhfa).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Quranic verse about supplicating in humility inwardly (Quran 7:55).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse commands humility and inwardness, which applies to all du'a, thus qunut as a du'a should be recited silently.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars hold that qunut should be recited aloud because it resembles Quran; some Companions considered it Quranic.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The majority of scholars hold it is not Quran, and caution dictates that it is a du'a, so ikhfa is preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دعائے قنوت میں اختفار مختار ہے فرمایا کہ قنوت میں اخفا مختار ہے دعاء قنوت پڑھنے والا خواہ مقتدی ہو خواہ منفرد ہو، کیونکہ قنوت ایک دعا ہے اور دعا میں اخفاء اولی ہے۔ بعض حضرات کا خیال یہ ہے کہ قنوت بالجہر پڑھے۔ کیونکہ قنوت قرآن کے مشابہ ہے یہی ہ ہے کہ اللهم انا نستعینک کے بارے میں صحابہ نے اختلاف کیا ہے کہ آیا یہ قرآن ہے یا قرآن نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ حضرت ابن مسعود کا قول یہ ہے کہ قنوت قرآن کی سورت ہے اور حضرت ابی بن کعب کہتے ہیں کہ یہ قرآن نہیں ہے عامتہ العلماء بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں لیکن احتیاط کا تقاضا یہی ہے کہ حائضہ ، نفساء اور جنبی اس کی قرآت سے اجتناب کریں۔ (کفایہ) لوان صاحب کفایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ سب سے طویل دعا قنوت وہ ہے جو حضرت عمرؓ سے مروی ہے اللهم اغفر لنا وللمؤمنين والمؤمنات والمسلمين والمسلمات و الف بين قلوبهم و اصلح ذات بينهم وانصرهم على عدوک و عدوهم اللهم العن كفرة اهل الكتاب الذين يصدون عن سبیلک و یکذبون رسلك و يقاتلون اوليانك اللهم خالف بین کلمتهم و زلزل اقدامهم و انزل بهم بأسك الذى لا يرد عن القوم المجرمين بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم اللهم انا نستعینك و نستغفرک و نؤمن بک و نتوکل علیک و نثنی علیک الخیر و نشکرک ولا نکفرک و نخلع و نترك من يفجرک ، بسم الله الرحمن الحيم اللهم ایاک نعبد و لک نصلی و نسجد و الیک نسعی و نحفد و نرجو رحمتک و نخشی عذابک ان عذابك بالكفار ملحق - بعض روایات میں اللهم انا نستعینک سے آغاز کیا گیا ہے۔ جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
In the supplication of qunut, concealment (ikhfā') is chosen. He said: in qunut, ikhfa is chosen, whether the reciter is a follower or alone, because qunut is a supplication and in supplication, concealment is better. Some scholars opine that qunut should be recited aloud (jahr), because qunut resembles Quran. This is because regarding 'Allahumma inna nasta‘īnuka', the Companions differed whether it is Quran or not. Ibn Mas‘ud said it is a sura of Quran, while Ubayy ibn Ka‘b said it is not Quran; the majority of scholars also hold this view. But caution requires that menstruating women, women in post-natal bleeding, and those in major impurity avoid reciting it. (Kifayah) The author of Kifayah wrote: the longest qunut supplication is that narrated from ‘Umar (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Allahumma ighfir lana wa lilmu’minīna walmu’mināt...' (the text continues). In some narrations, it begins with 'Allahumma inna nasta‘īnuka'. Jamil Ahmad, forgiven.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on the method of reciting qunut (whether aloud or silently). The author states the preferred (mukhtār) position is ikhfā' (silent recitation). The reasoning is that qunut is a dua (supplication), and Allah says 'Call upon your Lord in humility and privately' (Quran 7:55). Therefore, silent recitation is better. An opposing view holds that qunut should be recited aloud because it resembles Quran, as some Companions considered parts of it as Quranic. However, the majority held it is not Quran, and the Hanafi position is that it should be silent. The passage then mentions a caution: to avoid confusion, those in a state of major impurity should not recite these words as a precaution. Finally, it cites the longest form of qunut, narrated from ‘Umar (ra), which includes various supplications. This passage serves as a practical guide for the recitation of qunut, particularly in witr prayer.

Key Terms
اخفاء (ikhfā’): Reciting in a low voice such that only the reciter can hear.
جہر (jahr): Reciting aloud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, how should qunut be recited?
A) Aloud (jahr)
B) Silently (ikhfa)
C) Only by the imam aloud
D) Only by the follower silently

Key Takeaway
Reciting qunut silently (ikhfa) is the preferred Hanafi practice because qunut is a supplication, and Allah commands supplication in humility and secrecy.

The Meaning of Nafl in Hanafi Fiqh
Chapter heading and definition of nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define nafl and distinguish it from fard, wajib, and sunnah mu'akkadah.

Core Idea
Nafl is the extra — every voluntary act of worship beyond what Allah made obligatory.

This brief passage opens the chapter on Nawafil in Al-Hidayah. Having completed the rulings on fard and wajib acts, the author now turns to the supererogatory prayers. Understanding the term nafl is essential: it sets the stage for the detailed rules of sunnah and nafl prayers. Let's break down the meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the chapter's subject
The chapter is about nawafil, supererogatory prayers. The text begins with 'Bāb al-Nawāfil'.
2
Learn the literal meaning of nafl
Nafl means 'additional' or 'extra.' It is something above and beyond the obligatory.
3
Understand the relationship to fard
The text states: 'Nafl means that which is additional to fard.' So fard is obligatory, and any extra worship is nafl or sunnah.
4
Distinguish between sunnah and nafl
The text mentions both 'sunan' and 'nawafil'. In Hanafi, sunnah mu'akkadah is a higher category than nafl, though both are voluntary.
Sunnah mu'akkadah is emphasized, while nafl is general voluntary prayer.

Source Text

بــــاب الــــنــــوافــــل 
 ترجمہ ( یہ ) باب نوافل کے بیان میں) ہے۔ 
 تشریح سابق میں فرض اور واجب کا بیان تھا اس باب کے تحت سفن اور نوافل کا بیان ہے نفل کے معنی ( جو فرض پر زائد ہو ) چونکہ سن کو
Chapter of Nawafil. Translation: This is a chapter explaining nawafil. Explanation: Previously, the discussion was about fard and wajib. In this chapter, the discussion is about sunan and nawafil. The meaning of nafl is that which is additional to fard. Since sunan...
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This is the beginning of a new chapter in Al-Hidayah titled 'Bāb al-Nawāfil' (Chapter of Supererogatory Prayers). The commentary explains that the previous chapter dealt with obligatory acts (fard and wajib), and now the author turns to voluntary prayers (nawafil) and emphasized sunnah acts. The term 'nafl' literally means 'extra' or 'additional,' and in fiqh, it refers to any voluntary act of worship beyond the obligatory. This passage sets the stage for detailed rulings on sunnah and nafl prayers, including their number, times, and virtues. The text cuts off mid-sentence, but the intention is clear.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer or worship beyond the obligatory.
نوافل (nawāfil): Plural of nafl; supererogatory prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the word 'nafl' linguistically mean?
A) Sunnah
B) Extra or additional
C) Recommended
D) Obligatory

Key Takeaway
Nafl means any voluntary act of worship beyond the obligatory, and it is distinct from sunnah mu'akkadah and wajib in the Hanafi school.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Following a Non-Hanafi Imam
Commentary on inter-madhhab following

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on following a non-Hanafi imam and identify the condition that makes it impermissible.

Core Idea
Following a non-Hanafi imam is generally allowed unless you are certain his wudu is invalid by Hanafi standards.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on a Hanafi follower praying behind a non-Hanafi imam (e.g., Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali). The passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains that such following is permissible in principle, but with a critical condition related to the imam's state of ritual purity. Understanding this ruling helps avoid invalid prayers in inter-madhhab settings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and general ruling
The passage states that the very mention of this issue indicates that following a non-Hanafi imam is permissible. Identify the act (iqtida' behind a non-Hanafi) and the default ruling (jawaaz / permissible).
2
Extract the condition for impermissibility
The text adds a condition: if the Hanafi follower knows with certainty that the imam has done something that invalidates wudu according to the Hanafi school, then following becomes impermissible. Identify what those actions are (e.g., cupping, bleeding, impurity exiting from other than the two passages).
3
Understand the reason (ta'lil)
The commentary explains the reasoning: because the Hanafi follower believes the imam is in a state of minor impurity (hadath), and following an imam with invalid wudu is not allowed. This is a ta'lil based on the follower's certainty.
This applies even if the imam's own madhhab does not consider those acts as nullifiers.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a Hanafi who knows his Shafi'i imam got cupped and did not renew wudu. According to this lesson, the Hanafi should not follow that imam. If he is unaware, the prayer is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النوافل
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم کسی طرح مناسب نہیں۔ ودلت المسألة على جواز الاقتداء اس عبارت سے یہ بیان کرنا مقصود ہے کہ یہ مسئلہ دو باتوں پر دلالت کرتا ہے اول یہ کہ منفی المذہب کا شافعی المذہب کی اقتداء کرنا جائز ہے۔ اسی طرح مالکی اور حنبلی کی اقتداء کرنا بھی جائز ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ مقتدی قنوت وتر میں اپنے امام کی متابعت کرے گا۔ کیونکہ اختلاف قنوت فجر میں متابعت کرنے کے سلسلہ میں ہے نہ کہ قنوت وتر میں۔ پس جہاں قنوت مسنون بلکہ واجب ہے وہاں مقتدی خاموش نہ رہے گا بلکہ قنوت پڑھے گا۔
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اگر حنفی المسلک مقتدی کو اپنے شافعی المسلک امام کی طرف سے یقینی طور پر کوئی ایسی بات معلوم ہو جائے کہ احناف کے مذہب کے مطابق اس کی نماز فاسد ہو جاتی ہے تو اس حنفی کے لئے اس کی اقتداء کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ مثلا شافعی المسلک امام نے ونوکیا پھر فصد وغیرہ لگوائی یا غیر سبیلین سے خروج نجاست پایا گیا۔ اور وضو کا اعادہ نہیں کیا تو حنفی کے لئے اس کی اقتداء کرنا جائز نہیں ہو گا کیونکہ یہ چیز میں شوافع کے نزدیک اگر چہ ناقض وضو نہیں لیکن احناف کے نزدیک ناقض ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ حنفی المذہب مقتدی کے گمان کے مطابق اس کا امام محدث ہے اور محدث کے پیچھے اقتداء کرنا جائز نہیں۔
دعائے قنوت میں اختفار مختار ہے فرمایا کہ قنوت میں اخفا مختار ہے دعاء قنوت پڑھنے والا خواہ مقتدی ہو خواہ منفرد ہو، کیونکہ قنوت ایک دعا ہے اور دعا میں اخفاء اولی ہے۔ بعض حضرات کا خیال یہ ہے کہ قنوت بالحجر پڑھے۔ کیونکہ قنوت قرآن کے مشابہ ہے یہی ہ ہے کہ اللهم انا نستعینک کے بارے میں صحابہ نے اختلاف کیا ہے کہ آیا یہ قرآن ہے یا قرآن نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ حضرت ابن مسعود کا قول یہ ہے کہ قنوت قرآن کی سورت ہے اور حضرت ابی بن کعب کہتے ہیں کہ یہ قرآن نہیں ہے عامتہ العلماء بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں لیکن احتیاط کا تقاضا یہی ہے کہ حائضہ ، نفساء اور جنبی اس کی قرآت سے اجتناب کریں۔ (کفایہ) لوان صاحب کفایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ سب سے طویل دعا قنوت وہ ہے جو حضرت عمرؓ سے مروی ہے اللهم اغفر لنا وللمؤمنين والمؤمنات والمسلمين والمسلمات و الف بين قلوبهم و اصلح ذات بينهم وانصرهم على عدوک و عدوهم اللهم العن كفرة اهل الكتاب الذين يصدون عن سبیلک و یکذبون رسلك و يقاتلون اوليانك اللهم خالف بین کلمتهم و زلزل اقدامهم و انزل بهم بأسك الذى لا يرد عن القوم المجرمين بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم اللهم انا نستعینك و نستغفرک و نؤمن بک و نتوکل علیک و نثنی علیک الخیر و نشکرک ولا نکفرک و نخلع و نترك من يفجرک ، بسم الله الرحمن الحيم اللهم ایاک نعبد و لک نصلی و نسجد و الیک نسعی و نحفد و نرجو رحمتک و نخشی عذابک ان عذابك بالكفار ملحق -
بعض روایات میں اللهم انا نستعینک سے آغاز کیا گیا ہے۔ جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
Chapter of Supererogatory Prayers. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume Two is not appropriate in some way. The expression 'Wa dallat al-mas'alah 'ala jawaz al-iqtida' means to explain that this issue indicates two things: first, that a follower of a different madhhab is allowed to follow a Shafi'i imam. Similarly, following a Maliki and Hanbali is also allowed. Second, that the follower will follow his imam in the qunut of witr. Because the disagreement is regarding following in the qunut of Fajr, not the qunut of Witr. So where qunut is sunnah, rather wajib, the follower will not remain silent but will recite qunut. The author of Hidayah says that if the Hanafi follower comes to know with certainty from his Shafi'i imam some action that according to the Hanafi school invalidates his prayer, then for that Hanafi it is not permissible to follow him. For example, the Shafi'i imam performed ritual washing (wudu), then got cupping or applied, or excretion of impurity from other than the two passages was found, and he did not repeat the wudu, then for the Hanafi it is not permissible to follow him, because these things, although not invalidators of wudu according to the Shafi'is, are invalidators according to the Hanafis. Because according to the assumption of the Hanafi follower, his imam is in a state of minor ritual impurity, and following one in impurity is not allowed. In the supplication of qunut, concealment is chosen. He said that in qunut, concealment is chosen, whether the reciter of the qunut supplication is a follower or an individual, because qunut is a supplication, and in supplication concealment is more virtuous. Some people think that qunut should be recited aloud. Because qunut resembles the Qur'an, and there is disagreement among the Companions about the phrase 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuka', whether it is Qur'an or not. Thus, Ibn Mas'ud's statement is that qunut is a surah of the Qur'an, and Ubayy ibn Ka'b says it is not Qur'an, and the majority of scholars also hold this view, but the requirement of caution is that menstruating women, women in postnatal bleeding, and those in a state of major impurity should avoid reciting it. (Kifayah) The author of Kifayah wrote that the longest qunut supplication is the one narrated from Umar, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Allahumma ighfir lana wa lil-mu'minina wa al-mu'minat wa al-muslimina wa al-muslimat, wa allif bayna qulubihim, wa aslih dhata baynihim, wa ansurhum 'ala 'aduwwika wa 'aduwwihim. Allahumma al'an kafarat ahl al-kitab alladhina yasudduna 'an sabilika wa yukadhdhibuna rusulaka wa yuqatiluna awliyaka. Allahumma khallif bayna kalimatihim wa zalzil aqdamahum wa anzil bihim ba'saka alladhi la yuraddu 'an al-qawm al-mujrimin. Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim. Allahumma inna nasta'inuka wa nastaghfiruka wa nu'minu bika wa natawakkalu 'alayka wa nuthni 'alayka al-khayr wa nashkuruka wa la nakfuruka wa nakhla'u wa natruku man yafjuruka. Bismillah al-Rahman al-Haim. Allahumma iyyaka na'budu wa laka nusalli wa nasjudu wa ilayka nas'a wa nahfidu wa narju rahmataka wa nakhsha 'adhabaka inna 'adhabaka bil-kuffari mulhiq. - In some narrations, it begins with 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuka'. Jamil Ahmad 'ufiya 'anhu.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Ashraf al-Hidayah on the chapter of supererogatory prayers (nawafil). It addresses two distinct rulings. First, it discusses the permissibility of a Hanafi follower (muqtadi) praying behind a non-Hanafi imam (e.g., Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali). The text states that the very inclusion of this issue indicates that such following is generally allowed. However, a crucial condition is added: if the follower knows with certainty that the imam has done something that, according to the Hanafi school, invalidates wudu (e.g., cupping, bleeding, or impurity exiting from other than the two passages), then following is not permissible. This is because the Hanafi considers the imam to be in a state of minor impurity (hadath) in such cases, even if the imam's own madhhab does not consider those acts as nullifiers. The second ruling concerns the qunut in witr prayer. The commentator clarifies that the follower should recite the qunut along with the imam because qunut in witr is sunnah and even wajib according to Hanafis. The preferred method is to recite it quietly (ikhfa'), as it is a supplication and concealment is more appropriate. There is a difference among Companions whether the wording of qunut is Quranic, but the majority view is that it is not, hence menstruating women etc. should avoid reciting it. The text also provides a lengthy qunut supplication reportedly from Umar.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following an imam in congregational prayer.
محدث (muhdath): Person in a state of minor ritual impurity.
فصد (fasd): Cupping or bloodletting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following makes it impermissible for a Hanafi to follow a Shafi'i imam?
A) The imam is Shafi'i
B) The Hanafi follower is certain that the imam did something that Hanafis consider a nullifier of wudu
C) The imam recites qunut aloud in Fajr
D) The imam is Maliki

Key Takeaway
Following a non-Hanafi imam is permissible unless the Hanafi follower is certain that the imam has invalidated his wudu by Hanafi criteria.

Qunut in Witr: Ruling and Method
Commentary on qunut in witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qunut in witr and explain the preferred method of recitation.

Core Idea
Qunut in witr is wajib and should be recited quietly, as it is a supplication.

This lesson focuses on the second ruling from the passage: the qunut in witr prayer. The commentary clarifies that the follower must recite qunut along with the imam in witr because it is sunnah mu'akkadah and even wajib according to the Hanafi school. The preferred method is to recite it quietly (ikhfa'), and the text provides a lengthy prayer transmitted by Umar. Understanding this ruling helps Hanafis perform witr correctly in congregation, especially behind non-Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that qunut in witr is sunnah and even wajib. Identify that the Hanafi school holds qunut in witr as wajib.
2
Understand the follower's obligation
The commentator says that the follower will recite qunut in witr along with the imam, and not remain silent. This is because the disagreement about qunut is only for Fajr, not for witr.
3
Learn the preferred method: quiet recitation
The text asserts that concealment (ikhfa') in qunut is preferred (mukhtar). The reasoning is that qunut is a du'a', and in supplication, silence or quietness is more virtuous. Some hold it should be recited loudly, but the commentator favors quiet.
4
Recognize the textual status of the qunut supplication
There is a disagreement among Companions whether the words of qunut (Allahumma inna nasta'inuka) are Quranic or not. The majority say it is not Quran, hence menstruating women, etc., should avoid reciting it. This affects its permissibility for those in states of impurity.

Source Text

باب النوافل
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم کسی طرح مناسب نہیں۔ ودلت المسألة على جواز الاقتداء اس عبارت سے یہ بیان کرنا مقصود ہے کہ یہ مسئلہ دو باتوں پر دلالت کرتا ہے اول یہ کہ منفی المذہب کا شافعی المذہب کی اقتداء کرنا جائز ہے۔ اسی طرح مالکی اور حنبلی کی اقتداء کرنا بھی جائز ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ مقتدی قنوت وتر میں اپنے امام کی متابعت کرے گا۔ کیونکہ اختلاف قنوت فجر میں متابعت کرنے کے سلسلہ میں ہے نہ کہ قنوت وتر میں۔ پس جہاں قنوت مسنون بلکہ واجب ہے وہاں مقتدی خاموش نہ رہے گا بلکہ قنوت پڑھے گا۔

Thus, Ibn Mas'ud's statement is that qunut is a surah of the Qur'an, and Ubayy ibn Ka'b says it is not Qur'an, and the majority of scholars also hold this view, but the requirement of caution is that menstruating women, women in postnatal bleeding, and those in a state of major impurity should avoid reciting it. (Kifayah) The author of Kifayah wrote that the longest qunut supplication is the one narrated from Umar, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Allahumma ighfir lana wa lil-mu'minina wa al-mu'minat wa al-muslimina wa al-muslimat, wa allif bayna qulubihim, wa aslih dhata baynihim, wa ansurhum 'ala 'aduwwika wa 'aduwwihim. Allahumma al'an kafarat ahl al-kitab alladhina yasudduna 'an sabilika wa yukadhdhibuna rusulaka wa yuqatiluna awliyaka. Allahumma khallif bayna kalimatihim wa zalzil aqdamahum wa anzil bihim ba'saka alladhi la yuraddu 'an al-qawm al-mujrimin. Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim. Allahumma inna nasta'inuka wa nastaghfiruka wa nu'minu bika wa natawakkalu 'alayka wa nuthni 'alayka al-khayr wa nashkuruka wa la nakfuruka wa nakhla'u wa natruku man yafjuruka. Bismillah al-Rahman al-Haim. Allahumma iyyaka na'budu wa laka nusalli wa nasjudu wa ilayka nas'a wa nahfidu wa narju rahmataka wa nakhsha 'adhabaka inna 'adhabaka bil-kuffari mulhiq. - In some narrations, it begins with 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuka'. Jamil Ahmad 'ufiya 'anhu.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Ashraf al-Hidayah on the chapter of supererogatory prayers (nawafil). It addresses two distinct rulings. First, it discusses the permissibility of a Hanafi follower (muqtadi) praying behind a non-Hanafi imam (e.g., Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali). The text states that the very inclusion of this issue indicates that such following is generally allowed. However, a crucial condition is added: if the follower knows with certainty that the imam has done something that, according to the Hanafi school, invalidates wudu (e.g., cupping, bleeding, or impurity exiting from other than the two passages), then following is not permissible. This is because the Hanafi considers the imam to be in a state of minor impurity (hadath) in such cases, even if the imam's own madhhab does not consider those acts as nullifiers. The second ruling concerns the qunut in witr prayer. The commentator clarifies that the follower should recite the qunut along with the imam because qunut in witr is sunnah and even wajib according to Hanafis. The preferred method is to recite it quietly (ikhfa'), as it is a supplication and concealment is more appropriate. There is a difference among Companions whether the wording of qunut is Quranic, but the majority view is that it is not, hence menstruating women etc. should avoid reciting it. The text also provides a lengthy qunut supplication reportedly from Umar.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunut): A specific supplication recited in witr prayer.
اخفاء (ikhfa'): Quiet or low recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the preferred method of reciting qunut in witr?
A) Aloud (jahr)
B) Quiet (ikhfa')
C) It depends on whether one is an imam or follower
D) It must be recited only by the imam

Key Takeaway
Qunut in witr is wajib and should be recited quietly, as it is a supplication.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Emphasized Sunnah Prayers: Number and Proof
Listing and proof of sunnah rak'ahs with classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the twelve emphasized sunnah rak'ahs, identify their proof from the hadith, and distinguish them from non-emphasized sunnah prayers according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The Prophet's promise of a house in Paradise for persevering in twelve daily rak'ahs establishes the emphasized sunnah.

In this lesson, we dive into the chapter on supererogatory prayers (nawafil) from the Hanafi classic Ashraf al-Hidayah. You will learn precisely which sunnah prayers are considered emphasized (mu'akkadah) and which are non-emphasized (ghayr mu'akkadah), along with the primary hadith evidence used by the Hanafi school. The passage also addresses differences of opinion within the school and with the Shafi'i madhhab regarding the number of rak'ahs before certain prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the list of sunnah prayers
Locate in the passage the specific rak'ahs mentioned for each of the five daily prayers. Note that some have both before and after prayers.
The list includes 2 before Fajr, 4 before Zuhr, 2 after Zuhr, 4 before Asr (or 2 optionally), 2 after Maghrib, 4 before Isha (or 2 optionally), and 4 after Isha (or 2 optionally).
2
Classify the prayers into emphasized and non-emphasized
The passage explains that the twelve rak'ahs mentioned in the hadith are the emphasized sunnah (mu'akkadah): 2 before Fajr, 4 before Zuhr, 2 after Zuhr, 2 after Maghrib, and 2 after Isha. The additional prayers (4 before Asr, 4 before Isha) are non-emphasized (ghayr mu'akkadah).
The classification is based on the Prophet's consistent practice.
3
Examine the primary proof (dalil)
Read the hadith: 'Whoever perseveres in twelve rak'ahs in the day and night, Allah will build for him a house in Paradise.' Understand how this hadith is interpreted to specify the twelve rak'ahs listed.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala).
4
Analyze the differences in reports and the Hanafi resolution
Note that for Asr and Isha, there are conflicting reports: some mention 4, others 2. The Hanafi school gives a choice but prefers 4, especially according to Abu Hanifa.
Imam Muhammad considered the 4 before Asr as 'hasan' (good) but not as strong as the twelve.
5
Distinguish from the Shafi'i position
The passage mentions that Shafi'is differ on the sunnah before Zuhr: they pray 2+2 with separate salam, while Hanafis pray 4 with one salam. Understand the practical difference.
This is a known ikhtilaf in fiqh.

Chapter of Supererogatory Prayers. Translation: (This) chapter is about the explanation of supererogatory prayers. Explanation: Previously the discussion was about obligatory and necessary prayers. Under this chapter, the description of sunnah and nafil prayers is given. The meaning of nafil (is that which is additional to the obligatory). Since sunnah is also included, only nawafil is mentioned in the title. Chapter of Nawafil 12A. Description of sunnah and nafil: number of rak'ahs of emphasized and non-emphasized sunnah. The sunnah: two rak'ahs before Fajr, four before Zuhr and two after it, four before Asr and if he wishes two, two after Maghrib, four before Isha and four after it, and if he wishes two. The basis for this is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever perseveres in twelve rak'ahs in the day and night, Allah will build for him a house in Paradise.' And he interpreted it according to what is mentioned in the book, except that he did not mention the four before Asr, so for this reason he called it good in the original and gave a choice due to the difference of reports, and the better is four. And he did not mention the four before Isha, so for this reason it is recommended due to lack of continuous practice. And he mentioned two rak'ahs after Isha, and in other reports four are mentioned, so a choice is given, however four is better, especially according to Abu Hanifa based on what is known of his madhhab. And the four before Zuhr with one salam according to us, thus said the Messenger of Allah, and there is disagreement of Shafi'i in this. Translation: The sunnah prayers: two rak'ahs before Fajr, four rak'ahs before Zuhr and two rak'ahs after it, four rak'ahs before Asr, and if he wishes two, two after Maghrib, and four before Isha, and if he wishes two. And the basis for these prayers being sunnah is that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever perseveres in twelve rak'ahs in the day and night, Allah will build for him a house in Paradise.' And the Prophet, peace be upon him, interpreted the twelve rak'ahs according to what is mentioned in the book, except that he did not mention the four before Asr. For this reason, Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut considered these four rak'ahs as good, and a choice is given due to the difference of reports, and the better is to pray four. And the four before Isha are not mentioned, so for this reason these rak'ahs are recommended because constant practice was not found. And in the mentioned hadith, two rak'ahs after Isha are mentioned, and in another hadith four are mentioned, so a choice is given, but praying four is better, especially according to Imam Abu Hanifa based on what is known of his madhhab. And according to us, the four before Zuhr are with one salam, as the Messenger of Allah said, and in this there is disagreement of Shafi'i. Explanation: The author of Hidayah, although under this chapter he will mention both sunnah and nafil, but due to the importance and nobility of sunnah, he gave precedence to it. Then sunnah are of two types: emphasized and non-emphasized. Emphasized sunnah are those which the Prophet consistently performed, sometimes with occasional omission. And non-emphasized sunnah are those which the Prophet of Allah, peace be upon him, did not consistently perform. The emphasized sunnah are twelve rak'ahs in this manner: two before Fajr, four before Zuhr, two after Zuhr, two after Maghrib, and two after Isha. Besides these, the non-emphasized sunnah are. The author of Quduri mentioned both emphasized and non-emphasized in this manner: before Fajr two rak'ahs, before Zuhr four...
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the chapter on supererogatory prayers (nawafil) from the commentary Ashraf al-Hidayah. It provides a comprehensive list of the sunnah prayers associated with the five daily obligatory prayers, along with their proofs. The author distinguishes between emphasized sunnah (mu'akkadah) and non-emphasized sunnah (ghayr mu'akkadah). The primary evidence is the hadith that whoever perseveres in twelve rak'ahs daily will have a house built in Paradise. The twelve rak'ahs are: 2 before Fajr, 4 before Zuhr, 2 after Zuhr, 2 after Maghrib, and 2 after Isha. These are the emphasized sunnah. Additional prayers, such as 4 before Asr and 4 before Isha, are considered recommended (mustahabb) but not emphasized. The text notes differences in reports: for Asr, some narrations mention 4 rak'ahs, others 2, so a choice is given; for after Isha, 2 are mentioned in one hadith and 4 in another, with 4 being better especially according to Abu Hanifa. The passage also specifies that the 4 rak'ahs before Zuhr are performed with one salam (tashahhud after the second rak'ah then continue), which differs from the Shafi'i school who pray them as two separate pairs. The commentator emphasizes that sunnah prayers are superior to nafil because of the Prophet's consistent practice.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): Emphasized sunnah: prayers that the Prophet consistently performed, sometimes leaving them occasionally.
سنة غير مؤكدة (sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah): Non-emphasized sunnah: recommended prayers that the Prophet did not consistently perform.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayers beyond the obligatory and sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 10
B) 12
C) 20
D) 16

Key Takeaway
The twelve emphasized sunnah rak'ahs are the daily optional prayers that the Prophet consistently performed, and their reward is a house in Paradise.

The Emphasized Sunnah Prayers: Number and Proof
States the number of sunnan mu'akkadah and ghayr mu'kkadah with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of sunnah mu'akkadah rak'at according to the Hanafi school and cite the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Twelve rak'at of sunnah mu'akkadah secure a house in Paradise; the additional four before Asr and Isha are optional.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah enumerates the sunnah prayers that the Prophet (peace be upon him) regularly performed. It provides the hadith of Umm Habibah as the foundational proof, while also noting the ikhtilaf regarding the four rak'at before Asr and Isha. By studying this passage, you will learn which prayers are emphasized and why, and you will understand the basis for the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core list of twelve rak'at from the hadith
Find the twelve sunnah rak'at that the Prophet mentioned: two before Fajr, four before Zuhr, two after Zuhr, two after Maghrib, two after Isha.
These are the mu'akkadah.
2
Note the additional optional rak'at before Asr and Isha
The text adds four before Asr and four before Isha (or two), but they are not part of the twelve. They are subject to choice and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
Imam Muhammad considers them hasan and mustahabb; Abu Hanifa considers them mu'akkadah.
3
Understand the hadith proof and its implications
The hadith promises a house in Paradise for persistence on twelve rak'at. The category of sunnah mu'akkadah is derived from the Prophet's consistency.
The phrase 'ثابر على' indicates persistence.
