Preferred Rak'ahs in Nafl: Hanafi vs Sahibayn vs Shafi'i
Compares the preferred number of rak'ahs in nafl prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the preferred number of rak'ahs in nafl prayers and evaluate the proofs of the Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
For nafl prayers, four rak'ahs per taslimah is most virtuous: continuity increases reward.

When performing voluntary (nafl) prayers, is it better to pray two rak'ahs per taslimah or four? The Hanafi school, following Imam Abu Hanifa, holds that four is afdal in both day and night, while the Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi'i differ. This lesson examines the evidence and reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the schools involved
The dispute is about the most virtuous (afdal) number of rak'ahs per taslimah in nafl prayers. The three positions are: Imam Abu Hanifa (4 rak'ahs day and night), the Sahibayn (2 at night, 4 by day), and Imam al-Shafi'i (2 always).
Note that this is about preference, not permissibility.
2
State the Hanafi position and its dalil
Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence includes the hadith that the Prophet prayed 4 rak'ahs after Isha with one taslimah and consistently prayed 4 for Duha. Also, rational argument: continuity through the opening takbir increases effort (mashaqqah), so greater reward.
The rational argument is based on the principle that acts with greater effort are more virtuous.
3
State the opposing positions and their dalil
The Sahibayn use qiyas with tarawih (2 rak'ahs per taslimah) because tarawih is unanimously performed in pairs. Imam al-Shafi'i cites the hadith 'Salat al-layl wa al-nahar mathna mathna' meaning two rak'ahs each.
The Sahibayn's qiyas is valid but is answered by distinguishing between congregational and individual acts.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to each objection
To the Sahibayn: Tarawih is congregational, so ease is considered; nafl is not congregational. To Shafi'i: 'Mathna' means even numbers (pairs), not necessarily two; four and eight are also even.
The Hanafi response to the hadith is a reinterpretation based on linguistic analysis.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical consequence: one who prays 4 rak'ahs per taslimah follows Abu Hanifa; one who prays 2 follows Shafi'i or Sahibayn. Also affects vows: if one vows to pray the afdal way (4 with one taslimah), 4 with two taslimahs does not fulfill the vow. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
This illustrates how preference affects legal obligations like vows.

دوسرے نوافل بھی دو دو رکعت کر کے ادا کرنا افضل ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل تراویح پر قیاس ہے یعنی تراویح کی نماز بالاتفاق دو دو رکعت کر کے ادا کرنا افضل ہے۔ پس اسی طرح رات میں
امام اعظم کی دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس کو ابوداؤد نے ام المومنین حضرت عائشہ سے روایت کیا کہ عشاء کے بعد حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم چار رکعت پڑھتے تھے یعنی ایک سلام کے ساتھ اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم چاشت کی چار رکعت پر مواظبت فرماتے تھے۔ ان دونوں حدیثوں سے معلوم ہوا کہ دن اور رات دونوں میں چار چار رکعت پڑھنا افضل ہے۔ عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک سلام کے ساتھ چار رکعت ادا کرنے میں از راہ تحرمہ دوام ہے پس درمیان میں فارغ نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے زیادہ مشقت ہوگی اور جس عبادت میں مشقت زیادہ ہو وہ افضل ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے ایک سلام کے ساتھ چار رکعت ادا کرنا افضل ہوگا بہ نسبت دور کعت ادا کرنے کے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے ایک سلام کے ساتھ چار رکعت ادا کرنے کی نذر کی پھر اس نے دوسلام کے چار . رکعت ادا کی تو اس کی یہ نذرا دانہ ہوگی کیونکہ نذر کی تھی افضل طریقہ پر چار رکعت ادا کرنے کی اور ادا کیا مفضول طریقہ پر اور قاعدہ ہے کہ جائے گی کیونکہ مفضول افضل کے ساتھ ادا ہو جاتا ہے۔ افضل اور اعلیٰ مفضول اور ادنیٰ سے ادا نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اور گردو سلام کے ساتھ پڑھنے کی نذر کی تو ایک سلام کے ساتھ پڑھنے سے نذر پوری ہو والتراويح تؤدى بجماعة یہ عبارت صاحبین کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ بلاشبہ تراویح کی نماز دودو رکعت کے ساتھ ادا کرنا افضل ہے لیکن تروایح کی نماز جماعت سے ادا کی جاتی ہے اور جماعتی کاموں میں عام لوگوں کی رعایت کے پیش نظر سہولت اور آسانی کو لوظ رکھنے کا حکم دیا گیا ہے جیسے فرمایا گیا کہ امام کو چاہئے کہ وہ ہلکی پھلکی نماز پڑھائے ۔ ظاہر ہے کہ اس امر میں عام مقتدیوں کی رعایت کی گئی ہے پس چونکہ تراویح کی نماز با جماعت ادا کی جاتی ہے اس لئے عام لوگوں کی رعایت کے پیش نظر دو دو رکعت پڑھنے کا حکم کیا گیا۔ کیونکہ دو دو رکعت ادا کرنے میں آسانی ہے۔ یہ نسبت چار چار رکعت ادا کرنے کے اور اگر تنہا تراویح کی نماز پڑھے تو چار چار رکعت افضل ہیں بشرطیکہ طاقت ہو۔ اور نوافل چونکہ باجماعت ادا نہیں کئے جاتے اس لئے نوافل میں یہ رعایت ملحوظ نہیں ہوگی ۔ و معنی مارواہ شفعا لا وترا سے امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ حدیث صلوة الليل والنهار مثنی مثنی کا جواب ہے۔ حاصل جواب یہ ہے کہ رات اور دن کی نماز جفت ہے نہ کہ طاق، یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا منشاء دود و ک عدد بیان کرنا نہیں ہے بلکہ منشاء رسول کا یہ ہے کہ نوافل طاق رکعتوں کے ساتھ ادا نہ کئے جائیں بلکہ جفت یعنی جوڑ جوڑ ادا کئے ہیں خواہ دو رکعت ایک سلام کے ساتھ ہوں یا چار یا آٹھ۔
واللہ اعلم
Explanation: So far the discussion was of sunnah prayers. In the following lines, mention is made of nafl prayers. Scholars have differed regarding the quantity of night and day nafl prayers in terms of permissibility and preference. Summary: Imam Abu Hanifa said that in day nafl, it is permissible to pray up to four rak'ahs with one taslimah, and beyond that is makruh. And at night, praying eight rak'ahs with one taslimah is permissible without dislike, but praying more than that is makruh. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, eight rak'ahs are not mentioned, rather six are mentioned: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir that at night one can pray six rak'ahs with one taslimah. The author of Al-Hidayah said that the evidence that more than eight rak'ahs at night with one taslimah is makruh is that the Prophet never exceeded eight. If exceeding eight were not makruh, the Prophet would have done it once or twice to show its permissibility. But he never prayed more than eight rak'ahs with one taslimah at night. Therefore, praying more than eight with one taslimah is makruh. But an objector may say that there is a sunnah of praying more than eight at night. It is narrated that he (peace be upon him) used to pray five, seven, nine, eleven, and thirteen rak'ahs at night. Our response is: In five rak'ahs, two are nafl of night prayer and three are witr. In seven, four are night nafl and three are witr. In nine, six are night nafl and three are witr. In eleven, eight are night nafl and three are witr. In thirteen, eight are night nafl, three are witr, and two are sunnah. The Prophet would pray all these with one taslimah, then he would explain the details as mentioned above. After this detail, there is no room for objection. (Fath al-Qadir). Al-Quduri's statement 'wa qala la yazidu bi al-layli 'ala rak'atayni bi taslimah' apparently suggests that according to the Sahibayn, exceeding two rak'ahs at night with one taslimah is not permissible. But that is not the case; rather, the meaning is that according to the Sahibayn, exceeding two rak'ahs is not preferable (afdal). And 'wa qala Abu Hanifah in salla thaman rak'aat' is to avoid the statement of Imam al-Shafi'i, because Imam al-Shafi'i said that one should not exceed four rak'ahs with one taslimah, and if one does exceed four, it becomes makruh. The phrase 'wa al-afdal fi al-layl' discusses preference. He says: According to the Sahibayn, the best at night is to pray two rak'ahs with a taslimah, and during the day to pray four rak'ahs. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the best both at night and during the day is to pray two rak'ahs. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the best in both is to pray four rak'ahs. Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is the hadith of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them): 'Salat al-layl wa al-nahar mathna mathna', meaning the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that night and day (voluntary) prayer is two rak'ahs each. Other nafl prayers are also best performed in sets of two. The Sahibayn's evidence is analogy (qiyas) with tarawih: tarawih by consensus is best performed in sets of two rak'ahs. So similarly at night. Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence is the hadith narrated by Abu Dawud from Umm al-Mu'minin Aisha that after Isha the Prophet used to pray four rak'ahs with one taslimah, and he consistently performed four rak'ahs for Duha. From these two hadiths, it is known that praying four rak'ahs is better both at night and during the day. The rational argument is that praying four rak'ahs with one taslimah has continuity through the takbir al-tahrimah, so it involves more effort (mashaqqah) because there is no break, and the act with greater effort is more virtuous. Therefore, praying four rak'ahs with one taslimah is more virtuous than praying two. For this reason, if someone vows to pray four rak'ahs with one taslimah and then prays four rak'ahs with two taslimahs, his vow is not fulfilled because he vowed to pray in the preferred way but prayed in the less preferred way. The rule is that the less preferred can be fulfilled by the preferred, but the preferred cannot be fulfilled by the less preferred. If someone vows to pray with two taslimahs, then praying with one taslimah fulfills the vow. The phrase 'wa al-tarawih tu'adda bi jama'ah' is a response to the qiyas of the Sahibayn. The gist of the response is that undoubtedly tarawih is best performed in sets of two rak'ahs, but tarawih is performed in congregation, and in congregational matters, ease and facility are considered for the general people, as it is commanded that the imam should lighten the prayer. Clearly, in this matter, consideration is given to the general congregation. Therefore, because tarawih is performed in congregation, the command is to pray two rak'ahs for facility. This is compared to praying four rak'ahs. If one prays tarawih alone, then four rak'ahs are better provided he has the strength. Since nafl prayers are not performed in congregation, this consideration does not apply. The phrase 'wa ma'na ma rawahu shifa'an la witran' is a response to the hadith presented by Imam al-Shafi'i: 'Salat al-layl wa al-nahar mathna mathna'. The gist of the response is that the prayers of night and day are in pairs (even), not odd. That is, the intention of the Prophet (peace be upon him) is not to specify the number two, but to indicate that nafl prayers should not be performed in odd numbers, but in even numbers, whether two, four, or eight rak'ahs with one taslimah. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the most virtuous (afdal) number of rak'ahs per taslimah in nafl prayers. The author first clarifies that the earlier discussion was about sunnah prayers, and now he turns to nafl. He summarizes the positions: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it is permissible to pray up to four rak'ahs during the day and up to eight at night with one taslimah, and beyond that is makruh. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) restrict permissibility to two at night and four during the day, not in terms of permissibility but preference. Imam al-Quduri's phrase 'wa qala la yazidu ...' is interpreted as referring to preference, not permissibility. Then the author discusses the preferred (afdal) number: Imam Abu Hanifa says four rak'ahs are best in both day and night; the Sahibayn say two at night and four by day; Imam al-Shafi'i says two in both. Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence includes the hadith from Aisha that the Prophet prayed four rak'ahs after Isha with one taslimah and consistently prayed four for Duha. The rational argument is that more rak'ahs with one taslimah involve greater continuity (due to the single opening takbir), hence more effort and more reward. The Sahibayn's evidence is analogy with tarawih, which is unanimously best in sets of two. The author responds that the tarawih analogy is weak because tarawih is congregational, where ease is required; nafl prayers are not congregational, so the analogy does not apply. Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is the hadith 'Salat al-layl wa al-nahar mathna mathna'. The author interprets this hadith to mean that nafl should be in even numbers, not necessarily two, so four or eight are also acceptable. The passage also discusses the ruling on vows: if one vows to pray the afdal way (four with one taslimah), praying four with two taslimahs does not fulfill the vow, but vice versa. This concludes the discussion of preference. The passage ends with 'And Allah knows best'.

Key Terms
أفضل (afḍal): The most virtuous or preferred method of performing an act, not obligatory.
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning using a revealed case to derive a ruling for a new case.
تفضيل (tafḍīl): Preference; the act of considering one option more virtuous than another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 4 rak'ahs
C) 6 rak'ahs
D) 8 rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that praying four rak'ahs per taslimah in nafl is most virtuous due to prophetic practice and the principle that greater effort (mashaqqah) yields higher reward.

Salah — Prayer

Preferred Number of Rak'ats for Nafl Prayers: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Dispute on whether two or four rakat are better for nafl prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa holds that four rak'ats with one salam is superior for nafl prayers and evaluate the opposing proofs from Shafi'i and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Hardship increases reward: four rak'ats with one salam is more continuous and therefore superior.

When performing supererogatory prayers, is it better to pray two rak'ats at a time or four? This lesson examines the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Shafi'i, as well as an intra-Hanafi difference with the Sahibayn. We will analyze the textual and rational proofs each side presents and understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) for a Hanafi's daily practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the relied-upon view of Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the preferred number of rak'ats for nafl prayers, both day and night.
The mufta bihi is four rak'ats with one salam.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam Shafi'i holds two rak'ats with one salam is superior, and that the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) also hold this view by analogy with tarawih.
The Sahibayn agree with Shafi'i on the ruling but differ in their proof (qiyas).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadith of Ibn 'Umar ("Prayer of night and day is two by two") used by Shafi'i, and the analogy with tarawih used by the Sahibayn.
Shafi'i interprets 'mathna' literally as two rak'ats; Sahibayn see tarawih as a precedent for all nafl.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand how Abu Hanifa refutes both proofs: the hadith means 'even numbers', not exactly two, and tarawih is special due to congregation.
The hadith of 'A'isha (four after 'Isha') and rational argument of greater hardship support Abu Hanifa.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: a Hanafi will pray four rak'ats with one salam, while a Shafi'i will pray two rak'ats and repeat for a total of four.
This difference matters in daily worship and vow fulfillment.

واللہ اعلم
Chapter of Supererogatory Prayers. ... also read, and in the day four four rak'ats. According to Imam Shafi'i, in both night and day, praying two two rak'ats is better. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, in both, praying four four rak'ats is better. Imam Shafi'i's proof is the hadith of Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him): 'The prayer of the night and the day is two by two.' That is, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that the (supererogatory) prayer of night and day is two rak'ats each. Other supererogatory prayers are also better performed as two rak'ats each. The proof of the two companions (Sahibayn) is analogy with tarawih: the prayer of tarawih, by consensus, is better performed as two rak'ats each. So similarly in the night. The proof of the Great Imam (Abu Hanifa) is the hadith narrated by Abu Dawud from the Mother of the Believers, 'A'isha, that after 'Isha' the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray four rak'ats with one salam, and he consistently observed the forenoon prayer of four rak'ats. From these two hadiths it is understood that praying four rak'ats in both day and night is better. The rational proof is that in performing four rak'ats with one salam, there is continuity in the state of consecration (tahrimah), so there is greater hardship due to not finishing in between, and that worship which has more hardship is superior. Therefore, performing four rak'ats with one salam is better than performing two rak'ats. This is why if someone vowed to perform four rak'ats with one salam, then performed four rak'ats with two salams, his vow would not be fulfilled because he vowed to perform it in the better way but performed it in the inferior way. The rule is that the inferior can be fulfilled by the superior, but the superior cannot be fulfilled by the inferior. And if he vowed to pray with two salams, performing with one salam would fulfill his vow. 'And tarawih is performed in congregation' – this statement is the answer to the analogy of the two companions. The gist of the answer is that undoubtedly tarawih is better performed as two rak'ats each, but tarawih is performed in congregation, and in congregational matters, consideration is given to the common people, so ease and facility are commanded, as it is said that the imam should lead a light prayer. Obviously, regard is given to the general followers. So since tarawih is performed in congregation, for the sake of general people, it is commanded to pray two rak'ats each because praying two rak'ats is easier compared to praying four. And if one prays tarawih individually, then four rak'ats are better, provided he has ability. And supererogatory prayers are not performed in congregation, so this consideration does not apply to them. And the meaning of his narration 'in pairs, not odd' is the answer to the hadith presented by Imam Shafi'i, 'Prayer of night and day is two by two.' The gist of the answer is that the prayer of night and day is even, not odd. That is, the intent of the Prophet (peace be upon him) is not to specify the number two, but rather that supererogatory prayers should not be performed with odd rak'ats, but with even rak'ats – whether two with one salam, or four, or eight. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i school regarding the preferred number of rak'ats for supererogatory (nafl) prayers. Imam Shafi'i holds that two rak'ats with one salam is superior, citing the hadith 'Prayer of night and day is two by two.' His proof is that each pair is a separate prayer. Within the Hanafi school, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) also hold that two rak'ats is superior, based on analogy with tarawih, which is unanimously performed in pairs. However, the relied-upon Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa) is that four rak'ats with one salam is superior. His proofs are: (1) The hadith of 'A'isha that the Prophet used to pray four rak'ats after 'Isha' with one salam and consistently observed four rak'ats for forenoon prayer. (2) A rational argument: continuous devotion in four rak'ats involves greater hardship, and greater hardship means greater reward. The text then addresses two objections. First, the analogy of the Sahibayn with tarawih: tarawih is performed in congregation, so ease is prioritized. For individual nafl prayers, this consideration does not apply. Second, the hadith of Ibn 'Umar is interpreted to mean that prayers should be performed in even numbers, not necessarily exactly two. Four or eight are also even. The discussion shows how the Hanafi school uses both textual evidence and rational reasoning (istihsan) to establish the preferred practice. The reliance is on the position of Imam Abu Hanifa, which is the mufta bihi view.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer, offered voluntarily beyond the obligatory prayers.
مثنى (mathnā): In the context of the hadith, meaning 'two by two' or in pairs, indicating even numbers.
تراويح (tarāwīḥ): Supererogatory prayers performed in congregation during Ramadan after 'Isha'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is four rak'ats with one salam superior to two rak'ats?
A) Because the Prophet only prayed four rak'ats and never two.
B) Because it involves greater hardship due to continuous devotion, and hardship increases reward.
C) Because the hadith 'two by two' was abrogated.
D) Because the Sahibayn agreed with him.

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa's relied-upon position is that four rak'ats with one salam is superior for nafl prayers, based on prophetic practice and rational reasoning of increased hardship.

Obligation of Quran Recitation in Fard Prayers: Hanafi Position and Proofs
Hanafi ruling with proof on recitation in fard prayer, including inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation in fard prayer, cite the Quranic verse and Hanafi usul principle, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i and Maliki views.

Core Idea
Hanafi: recitation is wajib only in the first two rak'ats of fard prayer, not in all.

This passage from Ashraf ul Hadaya presents the Hanafi ruling that recitation (qira'ah) is wajib in the first two rak'ats of fard prayer, contrasting it with the views of Imam Shafi'i (all rak'ats) and Imam Malik (three rak'ats). The Hanafi proof is based on the Quranic verse 'faqra'u ma tayassara' and the usul principle that a command does not imply repetition. Understanding this ruling requires you to grasp the distinction between fard and wajib in Hanafi usul, and to see how the Hanafi school responds to the proof of the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its hukm level
State that recitation is wajib in the first two rak'ats, and note that it is not fard in all.
The hukm level is wajib, not fard, due to zanni evidence.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil and usul principle
Cite the Quranic verse (73:20) and the principle that an order (amr) does not require repetition.
The verse is qat'i in thubut but zanni in dalala regarding number of rak'ats.
3
Follow the Hanafi inference for the second rak'ah
Explain how the obligation is extended to the second rak'ah by qiyas due to similarity.
The first two rak'ats share characteristics; the last two differ.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i proof and Hanafi response
Identify the Shafi'i hadith and explain the Hanafi response that 'prayer' defaults to a complete two-rak'ah prayer in custom.
The word 'salat' in the hadith is interpreted to mean a full prayer, which is two rak'ats 'urfan.

فصل في القراءة

قرآت کا بیان فرائض میں قرآت کا حکم ... امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر و دلائل

والقراءة فى الفرض واجبة فى الركعتين وقال الشافعى فى الركعات كلها لقوله عليه السلام لا صلاة بقراءة وكل ركعة صلاة وقال مالك فى ثلاث ركعات اقامة للأكثر مقام الكل تيسيرا ولنا قوله تعالى : فَاقْرَءُ وُا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرآن والأمر بالفعل لا يقتضى التكرار وإنما أوجبنا في الثانية استدلالا بالأولى لأنهما تتشاكلان من كل وجه فأما الأخريان تفارقانهما في حق السقوط بالسفر وصفة القراءة وقدرها فلا تلحقان بهما والصلاة فيما روى مذكورة تصريحا فتصرف الى الكاملة وهى الركعتان عرفا كمن حلف لا يصلى صلاة بخلاف ما اذا حلف لا يصلى

ترجمہ فصل قرآت کے بیان میں ہے، فرض نماز میں دورکعتوں میں قرآت کرنا واجب ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ تمام رکھتوں میں واجب ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ بغیر قرآت کے نماز نہیں ہے۔ اور ہر رکعت نماز ہے۔ اور امام مالک نے کہا کہ تین رکعتوں میں لیے (فرض) ہے کیونکہ آسانی کے پیش نظر اکثر کل کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے۔
اور ہماری دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَاقْرَءُ وُا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ ہے اور کسی فعل (کام) کا امر تکرار کا تقاضہ نہیں کرتا۔ اور دور و رکعت میں ہم نے واجب کیا پہلی رکعت سے استدلال کرتے ہوئے۔ کیونکہ دونوں رکعتیں من کل وجہ ہم شکل ہیں۔ رہیں بعد کی دور رکھیں تو وہ اولین سے سفر کی وجہ سے ساقط ہونے میں اور قرآت کی صفت میں اور قرآت کی مقدار میں مفارقت رکھتی ہیں لہذا اخر بین اولین کے ساتھ لاحق نہ ہوں گی۔ اور امام شافعی کی روایت کردہ حدیث میں لفظ صلوۃ صراحت مذکور ہے اس لئے صلوٰۃ کا ملہ کی طرف پھیرا جائے گا اور وہ عرف میں دور کھتیں ہے ہیں۔ جیسے کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ کوئی نماز نہیں پڑھے گا۔ اس کے برخلاف جب لا یصلی کہ کر قسم کھائی۔
تشریح صاحب ہدایہ نماز مفروضہ، واجبات اور نوافل کے بیان سے فارغ ہو کر اب اس فصل میں مسئلہ قرآت کو ذکر فرمائیں گے
چنانچہ رباعی فرض نماز میں مسئلہ قرآت کے اندر پانچ قول ہیں۔

4)
علماء احناف کے نزدیک دورکعتوں میں قرآت فرض ہے۔
امام شافعی کے نزدیک تمام رکعتوں میں فرض ہے۔
و امام مالک نے کہا کہ تین رکعتوں میں فرض ہے۔ حسن بصری ایک رکعت میں فرضیت قرآت کے قائل ہیں۔ ابوبکر اہم نماز میں سنیت قرآت کے قائل ہیں۔
(۴)
ابوبکر نے قرآت کو باقی دوسرے اذکار پر قیاس کیا ہے۔ یعنی جس طرح نماز کے اندر رکوع اور سجدہ کی تسبیحات اور ثناء وغیر ہ مسنون
ہیں اسی طرح قرآت قرآن بھی مسنون ہے۔
Section on Recitation. Statement concerning recitation, the ruling of recitation in obligatory prayers... The viewpoint and proofs of Imam Shafi'i. And recitation in obligatory prayer is obligatory (wajib) in two rak'ats. And al-Shafi'i said: in all rak'ats, because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'There is no prayer without recitation, and every rak'ah is a prayer.' And Malik said: in three rak'ats, establishing the majority in place of the whole for ease. And our proof is the saying of the Exalted: 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' (Qur'an 73:20). And a command to an action does not require repetition. And we made it obligatory in the second (rak'ah) by inference from the first, because they resemble each other in every respect. As for the last two (rak'ats), they differ from the first two in that they may be dropped during travel, and in the manner of recitation and its quantity, so they are not attached to them. And in the hadith narrated by him, the word 'prayer' (salat) is explicitly mentioned, so it is directed to the complete (prayer), which is two rak'ats by custom, like one who swears that he will not pray a prayer, unlike when he swears that he will not pray. Commentary: The author of Al-Hidayah, after finishing the discussion of obligatory prayers, duties, and supererogatory prayers, now in this section mentions the issue of recitation. So, in the four-rak'ah obligatory prayer, there are five opinions regarding recitation: (1) According to Hanafi scholars, recitation is obligatory (fard) in two rak'ats. (2) Imam Shafi'i holds it is fard in all rak'ats. (3) Imam Malik said it is fard in three rak'ats. (4) Hasan al-Basri held it is fard in one rak'ah. (5) Abu Bakr held that recitation is sunnah in prayer. Abu Bakr analogized recitation to other remembrances (adhkar); just as in prayer the glorifications of bowing and prostration and the praise (thana') are sunnah, so too is recitation of the Quran sunnah.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, presenting the Hanafi position on the obligation of Quran recitation in fard prayers. The Hanafi school holds that recitation (qira'ah) is wajib only in the first two rak'ats of a four-rak'ah fard prayer, not in the last two. The text contrasts this with the views of Imam Shafi'i (wajib in every rak'ah), Imam Malik (wajib in three), Hasan al-Basri (wajib in one), and Abu Bakr (sunnah, not wajib). The Hanafi proof is the Quranic verse 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Qur'an' (So recite what is easy of the Quran). The command (amr) to recite does not imply repetition, so it is sufficient in some rak'ats. The obligation is established for the first two rak'ats by analogy: they are similar in all respects (both are recited aloud in Fajr and first two of Maghrib/Isha, and silently in Zuhr/Asr). The last two rak'ats differ because recitation is dropped during travel, the manner (aloud vs. silent) differs, and the quantity (Fatihah vs. nothing) differs. Regarding the Shafi'i proof (hadith 'no prayer without recitation'), the Hanafi response is that 'prayer' (salat) in that hadith refers to a complete prayer, which by custom is two rak'ats (e.g., Fajr). Just as if someone swears not to pray a prayer, it is understood as a complete two-rak'ah prayer. Thus, the hadith requires recitation in two rak'ats, not all. The passage also refutes Abu Bakr's view that recitation is sunnah by analogy with other dhikr; the Hanafi position maintains it is wajib based on stronger evidence. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that recitation is wajib in the first two rak'ats, and omitting it intentionally or forgetfully requires a prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah sahw) or repetition if deliberate.

Key Terms
قراءة (qirā'ah): Recitation of the Quran during the standing portion (qiyam) of prayer. In this context, the recitation of Surah al-Fatihah (and optionally another surah).
فرض (farḍ): A legally obligatory act that is established by definitive evidence (qat'i). If omitted, the prayer is invalid.
واجب (wājib): A legally obligatory act that is established by zanni evidence. Omission deliberately invalidates the prayer; if forgetful, sajdah sahw suffices.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in how many rak'ats of a four-rak'ah fard prayer is recitation of the Quran wajib?
A) In all four rak'ats
B) In the first two rak'ats only
C) In the first rak'ah only
D) In three rak'ats

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, recitation of the Quran in fard prayer is wajib only in the first two rak'ats, based on the Quranic command not implying repetition and the distinct characteristics of the last two rak'ats.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Obligation of Qira'ah: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on qira'ah in fard salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qira'ah in fard salah, explain the Hanafi proof from the Quranic command and the principle 'al-amr la yaqtadi al-takrar', and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith 'la salata illa bi qira'ah'.

Core Idea
A command does not obligate repetition; recitation is wajib in two rak'ahs, not four.

This passage presents a core inter-madhhab dispute: in how many rak'ahs of the four-rak'ah fard prayer is Quran recitation (qira'ah) obligatory? The Hanafi school holds it is wajib only in the first two. Imam al-Shafi'i argues it is wajib in all four. The dispute hinges on how we interpret the Quranic command and the prophetic hadith. We'll walk through the Hanafi proof, the Shafi'i objection, and the Hanafi response to understand the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: recitation (qira'ah) is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard prayer. Note that 'wajib' (not fard) reflects the probabilistic (zanni) nature of the evidence.
The distinction between fard and wajib is a Hanafi usul concept; other schools may not differentiate.
2
Identify the opponent's position and proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds recitation is wajib in all rak'ahs. His primary proof is the hadith 'La salata illa bi qira'ah' (No prayer without recitation) and 'kullu rak'atin salatun' (Every rak'ah is a prayer). Understand how this entails recitation in every rak'ah.
The Shafi'i school relies on the general command and the definition of 'salat' as each rak'ah.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Quranic proof
The Hanafi school cites the verse 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Qur'an' (al-Muzzammil 73:20). The operative term is the imperative 'iqra'u'. Apply the Hanafi usul principle: a command (amr) indicates obligation but does not necessitate repetition (takrar). Thus the verse obligates recitation only once, i.e., in one rak'ah. The second rak'ah is included by qiyas (analogy) due to resemblance.
The principle 'al-amr la yaqtadi al-takrar' is a key Hanafi usul rule.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i hadith
The Hanafi response interprets 'salat' in the hadith as 'al-salatu al-kamilah' (the complete prayer), which customarily means two rak'ahs. Evidence from oaths: if someone swears 'la usalli salatan', breaking the oath requires two rak'ahs; if he swears 'la usalli', one rak'ah suffices. Thus the hadith only obligates recitation in two rak'ahs.
The Hanafi interpretation uses 'urf (custom) and linguistic analysis to limit the general term.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In practice, a Hanafi prays reciting only in the first two rak'ahs of a fard prayer (and remains silent or makes dhikr in the last two), while a Shafi'i recites in all rak'ahs. This difference affects every fard prayer performed by followers of each school.
The thamarah shows why this dispute matters in daily worship.

سوال : یہاں ایک سوال ہوگا وہ یہ کہ پہلی اور دوسری رکعت میں مشابہت نہیں ہے بلکہ مفارقت ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ پہلی رکعت میں ثناء، نوز اور بسملہ ہے اور دوسری میں یہ چیزیں نہیں ہیں۔
ناب یہ چیزیں امر زائد ہیں۔ اعتبار فقط ارکان کا ہے اور اصل ارکان میں دونوں رکعتیں یکساں ہیں۔ رہیں آخر کی دورکعتیں سو وہ گیا اور کعتوں سے مختلف ہیں اور یہ فرق چند باتوں میں ہے۔
سفر کی وجہ سے آخر کی دورکعتیں ساقط ہوتی ہیں پہلی دو ساقط نہیں ہوتیں۔
اول کی دورکعتوں میں بالجبر قرآت ہوتی ہے اور آخیر کی دورکعتوں میں بالسر۔
اول کی دورکعتوں میں فاتحہ کے ساتھ عورت کا ملانا بھی واجب ہے اور آخر کی دو میں فاتحہ کے ساتھ سورت کا ضم نہیں ہوتا۔
پس جب اس قدر تفاوت ہے تو آخر کی دورکعتوں کو اول کی دو کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
والصلواة فيما بروی سے امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ حدیث لا صلوۃ الا بقراءة کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں صریحی لفظ صلوۃ سے مراد صلوۃ کاملہ ہے اور عرف میں صلوۃ کا ملہ کا اطلاق دورکعتوں پر ہوتا ہے پس حدیث سے دو انوں میں قرآت کا ثبوت ہوگا نہ کہ ہر رکعت میں۔
رہی یہ بات کہ صریحی لفظ صلوۃ سے عرف میں دورکعت مراد ہوتی ہیں، کیسے معلوم ہوا تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے ان الفاظ کے ہاتھ تم کھائی کہ لا یصلى صلوۃ یعنی لفظ صلوۃ صراحہ ذکر کیا تو دورکعت پڑھنے سے حانث ہوگا۔ اور اگر فقط لا یصلی کہا اور کا لوہا نہیں کہا تو ایک رکعت پڑھنے سے بھی حانث ہو جائے گا۔
Recitation in the obligatory (prayer) is obligatory in two rak'ahs. Al-Shafi'i said: in all rak'ahs, because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'No prayer without recitation, and every rak'ah is a prayer.' Malik said: in three rak'ahs, making the majority stand in place of all for ease. Our proof is the saying of Allah Most High: 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' (al-Muzzammil 73:20). The command for an action does not necessitate repetition. We only made it obligatory in the second rak'ah by inference from the first, because they resemble each other in every respect. As for the last two, they differ from the first two in terms of dropping (the obligation) in travel, the manner of recitation, and the amount of recitation, so they are not attached to them. And 'prayer' (al-salāh) mentioned in the hadith is mentioned explicitly, so it is directed to the complete prayer, and customarily that is two rak'ahs, as in the case of one who swears 'I will not pray a prayer (salāh)'—unlike if he swears 'I will not pray (yusallī)'. Translation: The chapter on recitation. In obligatory prayer, recitation in two rak'ahs is obligatory. Imam Shafi'i said it is obligatory in all rak'ahs because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no prayer without recitation, and every rak'ah is a prayer.' Imam Malik said it is obligatory in three rak'ahs for ease, because the majority is made to stand in place of the whole. Our proof is the verse 'So recite what is easy of the Quran.' The command for an action does not necessitate repetition. We made it obligatory in the second rak'ah by inference from the first, because the two rak'ahs resemble each other in every respect. As for the last two, they differ from the first two in being dropped during travel, in the manner (loud vs. quiet) of recitation, and in the amount of recitation, so they are not attached to the first two. In the hadith narrated by Imam Shafi'i, the word 'salāh' is mentioned explicitly, so 'salāh' is directed to the complete one, and customarily that is two rak'ahs—like if someone swore 'I will not pray a prayer (salāh),' unlike if he swore 'I will not pray (yusallī).' Commentary: The author of al-Hidayah, having finished the discussion of obligatory, necessary, and supererogatory acts of prayer, now mentions the issue of recitation. Thus, on the issue of recitation in the four-rak'ah obligatory prayer, there are five statements: (1) According to the Hanafi scholars, recitation is obligatory in two rak'ahs. (2) Imam Shafi'i holds it obligatory in all rak'ahs. (3) Imam Malik said it is obligatory in three rak'ahs. (4) Hasan al-Basri held that recitation is obligatory in one rak'ah. (5) Abu Bakr (al-Asamm) held that recitation in prayer is sunnah. Abu Bakr analogized recitation to other dhikr (remembrances) in prayer, i.e., just as the tasbīḥ of bowing and prostration and the thanā' (opening praise) are sunnah, similarly recitation of the Quran is sunnah. Hasan al-Basri's proof is that in 'So recite what is easy of the Quran', the word 'iqra'ū' is a command form, and a command does not necessitate repetition, so recitation is obligatory in one rak'ah only. Imam Malik's proof is the hadith 'No prayer without recitation', and every rak'ah is a prayer, so no rak'ah is without recitation, but since three rak'ahs are the majority, and for ease the majority is made to stand in place of the whole, he made recitation obligatory in three rak'ahs in place of four. Imam Shafi'i's proof is also this hadith, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said there is no prayer without recitation, and every rak'ah is a prayer, so recitation becomes obligatory in every rak'ah. The proof that every rak'ah is a prayer is: if someone swears 'I will not pray,' then prays one rak'ah, he breaks his oath—so praying one rak'ah causing a broken oath is proof that one rak'ah is a prayer, otherwise he would not have broken his oath. The Hanafi proof is the verse 'So recite what is easy of the Quran', that 'iqra'ū' is a command form, and a command does not necessitate repetition, so the obligation of recitation in one rak'ah is established by the explicit text (i‘ārat al-naṣṣ). Since the second rak'ah resembles the first in every way, by indication of the text (dalālat al-naṣṣ) recitation is made obligatory in the second rak'ah as well. Summary: The obligation of recitation in the first rak'ah is proven by the explicit text, and in the second rak'ah by the indication of the text. Objection: There is no resemblance between the first and second rak'ah, rather there is difference, because in the first rak'ah there is thanā', ta‘awwudh, and basmalah, not in the second. Answer: These are additional matters; consideration is only of the pillars, and in the essential pillars the two rak'ahs are alike. As for the last two rak'ahs, they are different from the first two in several ways: (1) The last two are dropped during travel, while the first two are not. (2) In the first two, recitation is loud (jahr), in the last two quiet (sirr). (3) In the first two, adding a surah to al-Fatihah is obligatory, while in the last two, a surah is not added. Given this much difference, the last two rak'ahs are not attached to the first two. And al-salātu fīmā ruwiya is a response to the hadith 'No prayer without recitation' presented by Shafi'i. The response is that in the hadith, the explicit word 'salāh' means the complete prayer, and customarily 'complete prayer' is applied to two rak'ahs—so the hadith proves recitation in two rak'ahs, not in every rak'ah. As for how it is known that customarily 'salāh' means two rak'ahs, the answer is: If someone swears using the words 'lā yuṣallī ṣalāh' (i.e., mentioning the word 'ṣalāh' explicitly), he breaks the oath by praying two rak'ahs. But if he merely says 'lā yuṣallī' (without the word 'ṣalāh'), he breaks the oath even by praying one rak'ah.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the obligation of Qira'ah (Quran recitation) in obligatory prayer. The Hanafi position is that recitation is wajib in only the first two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard prayer. The Shafi'i school requires it in all rak'ahs, the Maliki in three, Hasan al-Basri in one, and Abu Bakr al-Asamm considers it sunnah. The Hanafi proof is primarily the Quranic verse 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Qur'an' (So recite what is easy of the Quran). The Hanafi usul principle: a command (amr) does not necessitate repetition (takrar). So the verse only obligates recitation once, i.e., in one rak'ah. The second rak'ah is included by qiyas (analogy) because it resembles the first in all essential pillars. The third and fourth rak'ahs are excluded because they differ in three aspects: they can be dropped during travel (qasr), recitation is quiet (sirr) instead of loud (jahr), and no additional surah is added after Fatihah. The Shafi'i hadith 'la salata illa bi qira'ah' is interpreted by Hanafis to mean a complete prayer (salat kamilah), which customarily refers to two rak'ahs, not each individual rak'ah. This is supported by oath examples: if one swears 'la usalli salatan', he breaks the oath only by praying two rak'ahs, but if he swears 'la usalli', one rak'ah suffices to break the oath. Thus the hadith does not prove recitation in every rak'ah.

Key Terms
قراءة (qira'ah): Recitation of the Quran during the standing portion of the prayer, specifically Surah al-Fatihah and optionally an additional surah.
الصلوة الكاملة (al-salatu al-kamilah): The complete prayer, which in the context of the hadith is customarily understood as two rak'ahs.
الأمر لا يقتضى التكرار (al-amr la yaqtadi al-takrar): A fundamental usul principle in the Hanafi school: a command form in the Quran or Sunnah that is not repeated or qualified indicates obligation only once, not repetitively.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in how many rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard prayer is recitation (qira'ah) wajib?
A) One rak'ah
B) Two rak'ahs
C) Three rak'ahs
D) All four rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, based on the Quranic command and the principle that a command does not necessitate repetition, holds that recitation is wajib only in the first two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Recitation in the First Two Rak'ahs: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i/Maliki
Hanafi vs. Shafi'i/Maliki on recitation in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on recitation in fard prayer and evaluate the Shafi'i and Maliki counter-arguments using ibarat al-nass and dalalat al-nass.

Core Idea
In fard prayer, recitation is wajib only in the first two rak'ahs; the last two are optional because a command does not imply repetition.

This passage presents a classic intra-Islamic legal dispute: is recitation of the Quran obligatory in every rak'ah of fard prayer, or only in the first two? The Hanafi school argues for the latter, while Hasan al-Basri, Imam Malik, and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that recitation is required in all rak'ahs. By analyzing the proofs and the Hanafi response, we will see how the Hanafis use textual interpretation (ibarat al-nass and dalalat al-nass) and customary understanding to defend their position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school says about recitation in the first two versus last two rak'ahs of fard prayer.
Recitation is wajib in the first two, optional in the last two.
2
Identify the opposing schools and their proofs
List the schools that disagree (Hasan al-Basri, Malik, Shafi'i) and state their main evidence from the Quran or hadith.
Hasan uses the same Quranic verse; Malik and Shafi'i use the hadith 'لا صلوۃ الا بقرائة'.
3
Follow the Hanafi response to the Quranic command
Explain how the Hanafis use 'amr does not imply repetition' and then extend to the second rak'ah via dalalat al-nass.
Ibarat al-nass establishes recitation in one rak'ah; similarity extends it to the second.
4
Analyse the Hanafi reinterpretation of the hadith
Show how the Hanafis argue that 'salat' in the hadith means a complete prayer (two rak'ahs), not each rak'ah, using the oath analogy.
In custom, swearing by 'salat' requires two rak'ahs to break the oath.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Identify what actually changes in practice between the Hanafi ruling and the opposing ruling.
Hanafis: recitation in last two is optional; omission no sajdah. Shafi'is: fard in every rak'ah; omission invalidates.

Source Text

حسن بصری کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ فَاقْرَؤُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرآن میں اقرؤا امر کا صیغہ ہے اور امر تکرار کا تقاضہ نہیں کرتا۔ اس لئے ایک ہی رکعت میں قرآت کرنا فرض ہو گا۔ امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا لا صلوۃ الا بقرائة اور ہر رکعت صلوۃ ہے۔ لہذا کوئی رکعت بغیر قراءت کے نہیں یا مگر چونکہ تین رکعت اکثر ہیں اور آسانی کے پیش نظر اکثر کو کل کے قائم مقام کر دیا جاتا ہے اس لئے تین رکعات کو چار کے قائم مقام زاردے کر تین میں قرآت فرض کی گئی۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل بھی یہی حدیث ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ بغیر قرآت کے نماز نہیں ہوتی اور ہر رکعت نماز ہے لہذا ہر رت میں قرآت کرنا فرض ہو گا۔ ہر رکعت کے نماز ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ میں نماز نہیں پڑھوں گا۔ پھر اس نے یک رکعت پڑھی تو حانث ہو جائے گا پس ایک رکعت پڑھنے سے حانث ہو جانا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ ایک رکعت نماز ہے ورنہ حانث احناف کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَاقْرَؤُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآن بایں طور کہ اقرؤا امر کا صیغہ ہے اور امر تکرار کا تقاضہ نہیں کرتا کی ایک رکعت میں فرضیت قرآت عبارت النص سے ثابت ہوگئی اور چونکہ رکعت ثانیہ من کل وجہ رکعت اولی کے مشابہ ہے اس لئے دلالة النص سے رکعت ثانیہ میں بھی قرآت کو واجب کیا گیا۔ حاصل یہ کہ پہلی رکعت میں قرآت کا وجوب عبارت النص سے ثابت ہوا اور دوسری رکعت میں دلالت النص سے ثابت ہوا۔ سوال : یہاں ایک سوال ہوگا وہ یہ کہ پہلی اور دوسری رکعت میں مشابہت نہیں ہے بلکہ مفارقت ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ پہلی رکعت میں ثناء، نوز اور بسملہ ہے اور دوسری میں یہ چیزیں نہیں ہیں۔ ناب یہ چیزیں امر زائد ہیں۔ اعتبار فقط ارکان کا ہے اور اصل ارکان میں دونوں رکعتیں یکساں ہیں۔ رہیں آخر کی دورکعتیں سو وہ گیا اور کعتوں سے مختلف ہیں اور یہ فرق چند باتوں میں ہے۔ سفر کی وجہ سے آخر کی دورکعتیں ساقط ہوتی ہیں پہلی دو ساقط نہیں ہوتیں۔ اول کی دورکعتوں میں بالجبر قرآت ہوتی ہے اور آخیر کی دورکعتوں میں بالسر۔ اول کی دورکعتوں میں فاتحہ کے ساتھ سورت کا ملانا بھی واجب ہے اور آخر کی دو میں فاتحہ کے ساتھ سورت کا ضم نہیں ہوتا۔ پس جب اس قدر تفاوت ہے تو آخر کی دورکعتوں کو اول کی دو کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ والصلواة فيما بروی سے امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ حدیث لا صلوۃ الا بقراءة کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں صریحی لفظ صلوۃ سے مراد صلوٰۃ کاملہ ہے اور عرف میں صلوۃ کاملہ کا اطلاق دورکعتوں پر ہوتا ہے پس حدیث سے دو رکعتوں میں قرآت کا ثبوت ہوگا نہ کہ ہر رکعت میں ۔ رہی یہ بات کہ صریحی لفظ صلوۃ سے عرف میں دورکعت مراد ہوتی ہیں، کیسے معلوم ہوا تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے ان الفاظ کے ساتھ قسم کھائی کہ لا یصلى صلوۃ یعنی لفظ صلوۃ صراحہ ذکر کیا تو دورکعت پڑھنے سے حانث ہوگا۔ اور اگر فقط لا یصلی کہا اور کلمہ نہیں کہا تو ایک رکعت پڑھنے سے بھی حانث ہو جائے گا۔
The proof of Hasan al-Basri is that in 'فَاقْرَؤُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرآن' the word 'اقرؤوا' is a command form, and a command does not require repetition. Therefore, recitation in just one rak'ah becomes fard. The proof of Imam Malik is that the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم said 'لا صلوۃ الا بقرائة' and every rak'ah is a prayer. Thus no rak'ah is without recitation, but since three rak'ahs are more numerous and for ease the majority is placed in place of the whole, so three rak'ahs are made representative of four and recitation in three is made fard. The proof of Imam Shafi'i is also this hadith, because the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم said that there is no prayer without recitation, and every rak'ah is a prayer, so recitation in every rak'ah becomes fard. The proof that every rak'ah is a prayer is that if someone swears 'I will not pray', then prays one rak'ah, he becomes a breaker of oath. So becoming a breaker by praying one rak'ah is evidence that one rak'ah is a prayer, otherwise he would not break [his oath]. The proof of the Hanafis is the saying of Allah تعالى 'فَاقْرَؤُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآن' in this manner: 'اقرؤوا' is a command form, and a command does not require repetition, so the obligation of recitation in one rak'ah is established by ibarat al-nass (explicit text). And since the second rak'ah is similar to the first in every aspect, so by dalalat al-nass (implication of the text) recitation is made wajib in the second rak'ah as well. The conclusion is that the obligation of recitation in the first rak'ah is established by ibarat al-nass, and in the second rak'ah by dalalat al-nass. Question: Here a question arises: there is not similarity between the first and second rak'ah but rather difference, in that in the first rak'ah there is thana', na'uz [؟] and basmalah, while in the second these things are not present. Answer: These things are extra; consideration is only of the pillars, and in the fundamental pillars both rak'ahs are equal. As for the last two rak'ahs, they are different from the first two in several ways: due to travel the last two rak'ahs are dropped while the first two are not; in the first two rak'ahs recitation is aloud, in the last two silently; in the first two, joining a surah with Fatihah is wajib, in the last two a surah is not joined with Fatihah. So when there is such disparity, the last two rak'ahs cannot be annexed to the first two. And 'والصلاة فيما بروي' is a response to Imam Shafi'i's hadith 'لا صلوۃ الا بقراءة'. The gist of the answer is that by the explicit word 'salat' in the hadith is meant the complete prayer, and in customary usage 'complete prayer' is applied to two rak'ahs; thus the hadith proves recitation in two rak'ahs, not in every rak'ah. As for how it is known that the explicit word 'salat' means two rak'ahs in custom, the response is that if someone swears with these words 'لا یصلى صلوۃ' mentioning the word 'salat' explicitly, then he breaks his oath by praying two rak'ahs; but if he just says 'لا يصلّي' without saying the word, then he breaks his oath by even one rak'ah.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether recitation of the Quran in fard prayer is obligatory in every rak'ah or only in the first two. The Hanafi position is that recitation is wajib in the first two rak'ahs, and in the last two it is optional (mukhayyar). The opposing schools (followers of Hasan al-Basri, Imam Malik, and Imam Shafi'i) argue that recitation is fard in every rak'ah, but with different reasoning. The text presents the proofs of each side and the Hanafi response. The Hanafis rely on the Quranic verse 'فاقرؤوا ما تيسر من القرآن' (73:20) which is a command, and commands do not imply repetition. Thus the obligation is fulfilled by recitation in one rak'ah. But since the second rak'ah is essentially similar in its pillars, by implied textual indication (dalalat al-nass) recitation is wajib in the second rak'ah as well. The last two rak'ahs are different in several ways: they are dropped in travel, recited silently, and surah is not joined with Fatihah. Therefore the analogy does not extend to them. The Hanafis also reinterpret the hadith 'لا صلوۃ الا بقرائة' to mean that the complete prayer (salat kamilah) requires recitation, and in custom 'prayer' refers to two rak'ahs, not one. The oath analogy supports this: if someone swears using the word 'salat', breaking the oath requires two rak'ahs, but without the word, one rak'ah suffices. This establishes that the word 'salat' is normally used for two rak'ahs. Thus the Hanafi ruling is well-founded on textual evidence (ibarat al-nass and dalalat al-nass) and customary understanding.

Key Terms
عبارة النص (ibarat al-nass): The explicit meaning of a text; the plain, literal indication of a textual statement without need for inference.
دلالة النص (dalalat al-nass): The implicit indication of a text; a meaning that is necessarily implied but not explicitly stated.
صلوٰۃ کاملہ (salat kamilah): A complete prayer; in Hanafi usage, a complete unit of prayer that fulfills the obligations and is not deficient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response to Imam Shafi'i's hadith 'لا صلوۃ الا بقرائة', what proves that the word 'salat' in custom refers to two rak'ahs?
A) The Quranic verse 'فاقرؤوا' implies two rak'ahs.
B) If someone swears 'لا یصلى صلوۃ', he only breaks the oath by praying two rak'ahs, not one.
C) The Prophet ﷺ always prayed two rak'ahs in fard prayers.
D) The companions agreed on this.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the command to recite in prayer is fulfilled in the first two rak'ahs; the last two rak'ahs are optional due to textual interpretation and customary understanding.

intermediate

Recitation is Wajib in All Rak'ahs of Nafil and Witr
Hanafi ruling with reasoning for recitation in nafil and witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation in nafil and witr prayers and explain the reasoning behind it.

Core Idea
Every rak'ah of nafil and witr requires recitation; nafil pairs are independent prayers.

In Hanafi fiqh, the obligation of recitation differs between fard and non-fard prayers. This lesson examines a key ruling: that in nafil (supererogatory) and witr prayers, recitation of the Quran is wajib in every single rak'ah. The reasoning behind this ruling reveals the unique structure of nafil prayers and the precautionary approach for witr. By understanding this, you will avoid the common mistake of thinking recitation is optional in the later rak'ahs of these prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the ruling: recitation is wajib in all rak'ahs of nafil and witr. Note the hukm level: wajib (not fard).
In Hanafi, wajib means omission requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw) but does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Understand the reasoning for nafil
Analyze the talil: each pair (shaf') of nafil is a separate prayer. Therefore, standing for the third rak'ah is like a new takbir tahrimah, making recitation required in that rak'ah as well.
This implies that if you pray four rak'ahs of nafil with one salam, the third rak'ah behaves like a new prayer start: you must recite the opening supplication (thana') again.
3
Understand the reasoning for witr
The text states witr is for caution (ihtiyat). In Hanafi, witr is wajib, and its structure is similar to maghrib but with recitation in all three rak'ahs as a precaution.
Some schools consider witr as two rak'ahs plus one, but Hanafis treat it as a single three-rak'ah prayer with recitation wajib in all.
4
Apply the consequence of omission
If one intentionally omits recitation in a rak'ah of nafil or witr, the prayer is still valid but requires sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) because a wajib was missed.
This distinguishes wajib from rukn: omitting a rukn would invalidate the prayer entirely.

Source Text

و القراءة واجبة في جميع ركعات النفل و فى جميع ركعات الوتر اما النفل فلان كل شفع منه صلواة عن حدة والقيام الى الثالثة كتحريمة مبتدأة و لهذا لايجب بالتحريمة الاولى الأركعتان في المشهورة اصحابنا ولهذا قالوا يستفتح في الثالثة اى يقول سبحانك اللهم واما الوتر فللاحتياط ترجمہ اور نفل کی تمام رکعتوں میں قرآت واجب ہے اور وتر کی تمام رکعتوں میں بہر حال نفل تو اس لئے کہ نفل کی ہر دورکعت علیحد ہے اور تیسری رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہونا نئے سرے سے تحریمہ کے مانند ہے اسی وجہ سے ہمارے اصحاب کے قول مشہور کے مطابق پہلی تحریمہ سے فقط دورکعت واجب ہوں گی۔ اور اسی وجہ سے مشائخ نے کہا کہ تیسری رکعت میں سبحانك اللهم و بحمدک پڑھے۔ اور رہا وتر تو احتیاط کی وجہ سے ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ قرآت نفل اور وتر کی تمام رکعتوں میں واجب ہے نفل کی تمام رکعتوں میں قرآت اس لئے واجب ہے کہ نفل کی ہر رکعت علیحدہ نماز ہے۔ چنانچہ پہلی تحریمہ سے دوہی رکعت واجب ہوں گی اگر چہ دو رکعت سے زیادہ کی نیت کی ہو۔ علماء احناف کا باز
And recitation is wajib in all rak'ahs of nafil and in all rak'ahs of witr. As for nafil, because each pair of it is a separate prayer, and standing up for the third rak'ah is like a new takbir tahrimah. Hence, by the first tahrimah only two rak'ahs are obligatory according to the well-known (mashhurah) [view] of our companions. And for this reason they said: he should recite the opening supplication (subhanaka Allahumma) in the third rak'ah. As for witr, it is for caution (ihtiyat). Translation: And recitation is wajib in all rak'ahs of nafil and in all rak'ahs of witr. As for nafil, because each pair of nafil is a separate prayer, and standing for the third rak'ah is like a new takbir tahrimah. For this reason, according to the well-known view of our associates, only two rak'ahs are obligatory by the first tahrimah. And for this reason the scholars said that he should recite 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika' in the third rak'ah. As for witr, it is due to precaution. Explanation: The issue: recitation is wajib in all rak'ahs of nafil and witr. In nafil, it is wajib because each rak'ah of nafil is a separate prayer. Thus, by the first tahrimah, only two rak'ahs become obligatory, even if one intends more than two. (End of the text from the scholars of the Hanafis.)
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling that in nafil (supererogatory) and witr prayers, recitation of the Quran is wajib in every rak'ah. The reason for nafil is that each pair of nafil (two rak'ahs) is considered an independent prayer. Thus, when performing four rak'ahs of nafil with one salam, the third rak'ah is like the start of a new prayer with a new takbir tahrimah, so the worshipper must recite the opening supplication (thanā') and recite Fatihah in every rak'ah. For witr, recitation is wajib in all three rak'ahs out of caution (ihtiyat), since witr is a confirmed sunnah and its structure is like maghrib but with slight differences. The commentary notes that in nafil, by the first tahrimah only two rak'ahs are obligatory (i.e., the minimum obligation is two rak'ahs for each intention), and if one prays more than two, each additional rak'ah requires a separate intention or is considered a separate unit. This is a key distinction from fard prayers, where recitation is not wajib in every rak'ah.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Voluntary supererogatory prayer; any prayer beyond the obligatory (fard) and sunnah mu'akkadah.
وتر (witr): An odd-numbered prayer (usually three rak'ahs) performed after Isha, considered wajib in Hanafi school, sunnah mu'akkadah in others.
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The initial takbir (Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer, also called takbir al-iftitah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is recitation wajib in all rak'ahs of nafil according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the Prophet ﷺ ordered it specifically for nafil.
B) Because each pair of nafil is a separate prayer, so each rak'ah requires recitation.
C) Because nafil is longer in duration.
D) Because the Quran says so explicitly.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, recitation in nafil and witr prayers is wajib in every rak'ah due to the independent nature of each pair of nafil and the precautionary approach for witr.

Recitation in the Last Two Rak'ahs: Optional but Preferred
Ruling on optional recitation in the last two rak'ahs of fard prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation in the last two rak'ahs of obligatory prayer and explain the evidence from the Prophet's consistent practice.

Core Idea
In the last two rak'ahs, recitation is optional (not wajib), but reciting Surah al-Fatiha is preferred.

The prayer consists of multiple rak'ahs with distinct rulings. While recitation in the first two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard prayer is wajib, the last two rak'ahs grant the worshipper flexibility. This lesson examines the Hanafi position that recitation is optional—silence, tasbih, or recitation are all valid—and clarifies why the Prophet's practice makes recitation meritorious but not obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on recitation (qira'ah) in the last two rak'ahs (al-akhirayn) of Zuhr, Asr, and Isha. Determine the hukm level: is it fard, wajib, sunnah, or mubah?
Hanafi usul distinguishes between fard (qat'i) and wajib (zanni).
2
Locate the primary dalil
The passage cites the Prophet's continuous practice (muwazaba) as evidence. Identify whether this is a proof for obligation (wujub) or recommendation (nadb).
The Arabic phrase 'لانه عليه السلام داوم على ذلك' indicates he persisted in reciting.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the Prophet's perseverance (muwazaba) shows preference, not obligation. The Hanafi rule: muwazaba indicates mustahabb unless there is a qarinah (context) raising it to wajib, but here silence and tasbih are also permitted.
Additional support: sajda al-sahw is not required for omission.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Hasan ibn Ziyad narrates from Abu Hanifa that recitation or remembrance (dhikr) is obligatory; omitting it incurs sin and requires sajda al-sahw. Contrast this with the Zahir al-Riwayah position.
This difference shows how different narrations within the madhhab can lead to different rulings.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Al-Hidayah and al-`Inayah prefer the Zahir al-Riwayah view. Al-`Inayah analogizes the worshipper's qiyam in the last two rak'ahs to that of a muqtadi (follower), where silence is the norm. Thus the mufta bihi is the optional view.
The tarjih authority comes from later Hanafi masters who weighed the narrations.

Source Text

باب النوافل وهو مخير في الاخريين معناه ان شاء سكت وان شاء قرأ وان شاء سبح كذا روى عن ابي حنيفة و المأثور عن على وابن مسعود وعائشة الا ان الافضل ان يقرأ لأنه عليه السلام داوم على ذلك ولها يجب السهو بتركها في ظاهر الرواية

ترجمہ اور مصلی کو اخیرین میں اختیار ہے۔ اس کی مراد یہ ہے کہ جی چاہے خاموش رہے اور جی چاہے تو پڑھے اور اگر چاہے؟ پڑھے۔ [پہنی؟] امام ابوحنیفہ سے مروی ہے اور یہی علی ، ابن مسعود اور عائشہ سے منقول ہے۔ مگر افضل قرآت کرنا ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور اس پر مداومت کی ہے اور اسی وجہ سے ترک قرآت سے (اخیرین میں ) ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق سجدہ سہو واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ آخر کی دورکعتوں میں مصلی کو اختیار ہے، سورۃ فاتحہ کی قرآت کرے یا تین تسبیحات کی منہ خاموش کھڑا ہے یا تین تسبیح پڑھے امام ابو حنیفہ سے یہی مروی ہے یعنی ظاہر الروایہ یہی ہے۔ اور یہ تسبیح کرنا حضرت علی ، ابن مسعود حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالی عنہم اجمعین سے بھی منقول ہے مگر آخیرین میں سورہ فاتحہ کی قرآت کرنا افضل ہے کیونکہ حضور نے بھی کی ترک کے ساتھ اس پر مداومت فرمائی ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ آخیرین میں اگر قرآت فاتحہ ترک کر دی گئی تو اس پر سجدہ سہو واجب نہیں ۔ اس سے بھی آخیرین میں قرآت فاتحہ کا افضل ہونا معلوم ہوا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ ظاہر الروایت بھی یہی ہے۔ امام حسن بن زیاد نے امام اعظم سے روایت کی ہے کہ اخربین میں مصلی نے اگر نہ قرآنہ کی اور نہ عمد انہی کی تو گنہگار ہوگا اور کی ان چیزوں کو ترک کر دیا تو سجدہ سہو واجب ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اخربین میں قیام مقصود ہے لہذا اس کو قرآت اور ذکر سے خالی کر نا کرنا گا۔ صاحب عنایہ نے کہا کہ [خاہ رالروایہ؟] اصح ہے۔ کیونکہ قیام کے اندر اصل تو قرآت ہے پس جب قرآت ساقط ہوگئی تو مطلق قیام رہا۔ پس ایسا ہو گیا جیسے مقتدی کا قیام۔ (عنایہ )
Chapter of Supererogatory Prayers. And he has the choice in the last two [rak'ahs]: meaning, if he wishes he remains silent, if he wishes he recites, if he wishes he glorifies. It is narrated from Abu Hanifa, and it is reported from Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Aisha. However, the best is that he recites, because he (peace be upon him) persevered upon that. And according to that, sajda al-sahw is not obligatory for omitting it in the apparent narration. Translation: The worshipper has choice in the last two. Its meaning: if he wishes he remains silent, and if he wishes he recites, and if he wishes he recites? It is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa, and it is likewise from Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Aisha. But it is better to recite, because the Prophet persevered upon it, and for this reason, according to the apparent narration, sajda al-sahw is not obligatory for omitting recitation in the last two. Explanation: Sahib Quduri said: In the last two rak'ahs, the worshipper has choice: either recite Surah al-Fatiha, or three tasbihs while standing silently, or recite three tasbihs. This is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa, meaning this is the apparent narration. And this tasbih is also narrated from Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Aisha. But to recite Surah al-Fatiha in the last two is better, because the Prophet persevered upon it and did not repeatedly leave it. This is why if recitation of Fatiha is omitted in the last two, sajda al-sahw is not obligatory. From this also, it is known that recitation of Fatiha in the last two is better. Sahib al-Hidayah said that the apparent narration is this too. Imam Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Imam A'zam that if the worshipper in the last two did not recite and did not intend those things, he will be sinful, and if he abandoned these things, sajda al-sahw will be obligatory. The proof is that in the last two, qiyam (standing) is intended, so it cannot be left void of recitation and remembrance. Sahib al-`Inayah said: The apparent narration is more correct, because in qiyam, the original is recitation, so when recitation falls, absolute qiyam remains, so it becomes like the qiyam of a follower (muqtadi). (al-`Inayah)
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on nawafil (supererogatory prayers) discusses the ruling on recitation in the last two rak'ahs of obligatory prayers. The author first presents the principle: the worshipper has a choice—he may recite Surah al-Fatiha, remain silent, or glorify Allah (tasbih). This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa as recorded in the Zahir al-Riwayah, and it is also reported from the Companions Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Aisha. However, the preferred act (afdal) is to recite, because the Prophet ﷺ consistently did so. Consequently, if one omits recitation, sajda al-sahw is not obligatory according to the apparent narration. The commentary then elaborates: Quduri confirms the three options. The narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad records a stricter view from Imam Abu Hanifa that requires recitation or remembrance, making omission sinful and requiring sajda al-sahw. Sahib al-`Inayah refutes this, arguing that while qiyam is intended, the default act in qiyam is recitation; but when recitation is dropped (as in the last two rak'ahs), the qiyam itself remains valid like the qiyam of a follower. Thus, the Zahir al-Riwayah position is upheld: recitation is not obligatory but recommended. The lesson's core is that the last two rak'ahs of fard prayer are not equivalent to the first two in the obligation of recitation; rather, they enjoy flexibility with a preference for Fatiha.

Key Terms
الاخريين (al-akhirayn): The last two rak'ahs of the obligatory four-rak'ah prayers (Zuhr, Asr, and Isha).
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The apparent or transmitted narrations from the imams of the madhhab, specifically the six books of Imam Muhammad (al-Mabsut, etc.), which carry the greatest authority.
مداومة (muwazaba): Continuous and consistent practice without abandoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah of the Hanafi school, what are the options for a person praying alone in the last two rak'ahs of an obligatory prayer?
A) He must recite Surah al-Fatiha
B) He may recite, remain silent, or glorify
C) He must recite three tasbihs
D) He must remain silent

Key Takeaway
In the last two rak'ahs of fard prayer, recitation is optional but reciting Surah al-Fatiha is preferred (afdal); omitting it does not require sajda al-sahw.

Recitation in Nafl and Witr: Wajib in Every Rak'ah
Ruling with proof for recitation in nafl and witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on recitation in nafl and witr prayers and explain the Hanafi reasoning for each.

Core Idea
Each two rak'ahs of nafl are a separate prayer, making recitation wajib in every rak'ah.

In fard prayers, recitation is only required in the first two rak'ahs. But for nafl and witr, the Hanafi school holds a different ruling. This lesson examines the text that establishes recitation as wajib in every rak'ah, and unpacks the legal reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Locate the explicit ruling: recitation is obligatory (wajib) in all rak'ahs of nafl and witr. Note that the hukm level is wajib, not fard.
2
Understand the structure of nafl: shaf' as independent prayer
Recognize that nafl prayer is built on pairs (shaf'). Each pair is an independent legal unit. This is the key principle for deriving the ruling.
3
Apply the principle to the third rak'ah
When standing for the third rak'ah, it is treated as a new takbirat al-ihram. Thus, recitation is required for this new unit as well.
4
Recognize the implication for obligation by first takbir
Only two rak'ahs become obligatory by the first takbir. This is why the early scholars recommended opening supplication (thana') in the third rak'ah.
5
For witr: apply caution
Although witr is wajib, it carries characteristics of nafl (e.g., number of rak'ahs, qunut). Therefore, out of caution (ihtiyat), recitation is made wajib in every rak'ah.

Source Text

نوافل میں قرآت کا حکم

و القراءة واجبة في جميع ركعات النفل و فى جميع ركعات الوتر اما النفل فلان كل شفع منه صلواة عن حدة والقيام الى الثالثة كتحريمة مبتدأة و لهذا لايجب بالتحريمة الاولى الأركعتان في المشهورة اصحابنا ولهذا قالوا يستفتح في الثالثة اى يقول سبحانك اللهم واما الوتر فللاحتياط

ترجمہ اور نفل کی تمام رکعتوں میں قرآت واجب ہے اور وتر کی تمام رکعتوں میں بہر حال نفل تو اس لئے کہ نفل کی ہر دورکعت علیحد ہے اور تیسری رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہونا نئے سرے سے تحریمہ کے مانند ہے اسی وجہ سے ہمارے اصحاب کے قول مشہور کے مطابق کی اولی سے فقط دورکعت واجب ہوں گی۔ اور اسی وجہ سے مشائخ نے کہا کہ تیسری رکعت میں سبحانك اللهم و بحمدک پڑھے۔ اور رہا وتر تو احتیاط کی وجہ سے ہے۔

تشریح مسئلہ قرآت نفل اور وتر کی تمام رکعتوں میں واجب ہے نفل کی تمام رکعتوں میں قرآت اس لئے واجب ہے کہ نقل کیا رکعت علیحدہ نماز ہے۔ چنانچہ پہلے تحریمہ سے دوہی رکعت واجب ہوں گی اگر چہ دو رکعت سے زیادہ کی نبیت کی ہو۔ علماء احتفاف باز 

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم مشہور یہی ہے حتی کہ اگر چار کی نیت کی پھر دورکعت پوری کرنے سے پہلے فاسد کر دیا تو شروع کرنے کی وجہ سے اس پر صرف ایک دوگانہ قضاء کرنا واجب ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ اول تحریمہ سے صرف دو رکعت لازم آئیں۔

چونکہ ہر دور کعت علیحدہ نماز ہے اس لئے مشائخ احناف نے کہا کہ تیسری کے لئے کھڑا ہونے پر ثناء پڑھے کیونکہ تیسری رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہونا ئی تحریمہ کے مرتبہ میں ہے اور وتر کی تمام رکعتوں میں قرآت اس لئے واجب ہے کہ نماز میں قرآت لذا تہ رکن مقصود ہے اور وتر کا وجوب حدیث سے ثابت ہوا ہے پس وتر کے نقل ہونے کا احتمال پیدا ہو گیا لہذا احتیاط کی وجہ سے وتر کی تمام رکعتوں میں قربات واجب کی گئی۔ حاصل یہ کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک وتر کی نماز اگر چہ واجب ہے لیکن چونکہ نفل ہونے کے آثار اس پر ظاہر ہیں تو ہم نے احتیاط اس کی ہر رکعت میں مثل سنت و نفل کے قرآت واجب کی ہے۔
Ruling on recitation in nafl prayers. And recitation is obligatory in all rak'ahs of nafl and in all rak'ahs of witr. As for nafl, because each pair of it is a separate prayer, and standing up for the third rak'ah is like a new takbirat al-ihram. For this reason, only two rak'ahs become obligatory by the first takbir according to our renowned companions. And therefore they said: he recites the opening supplication (Subhanaka Allahumma) in the third rak'ah. As for witr, it is out of caution. Translation: And recitation is obligatory in all rak'ahs of nafl and in all rak'ahs of witr. As for nafl, because each two rak'ahs of it are separate, and standing for the third rak'ah is like a new takbirat al-ihram. For this reason, according to our companions' well-known saying, only two rak'ahs are obligatory by the first takbir. And for this reason, the scholars said: he should recite Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika in the third rak'ah. As for witr, it is due to caution. Explanation: The issue: recitation is obligatory in all rak'ahs of nafl and witr. In nafl, recitation is obligatory because each two rak'ahs are a separate prayer. Thus, by the first takbir, only two rak'ahs become obligatory, even if one intended more than two. Ashraf al-Hidaya: this is the well-known view. Even if one intended four and then spoilt after the first two but before completing, only one two-rak'ah set is due to be made up. So it is known that only two rak'ahs become necessary by the first takbir. Since each two rak'ahs are a separate prayer, the Hanafi scholars said that upon standing for the third, one should recite the opening supplication, because standing for the third is like a new takbir. And recitation is obligatory in all rak'ahs of witr because recitation in prayer is the intended pillar, and the obligation of witr is established by hadith, so the possibility of it being nafl remains; therefore, out of caution, recitation is made obligatory in all its rak'ahs. Summary: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, although witr is obligatory, because traces of nafl appear on it, we have obligated recitation in every rak'ah like sunnah and nafl out of caution.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage deals with the obligation of recitation (qira'ah) in nafl (supererogatory) and witr prayers. The author states clearly: recitation is wajib in every rak'ah of nafl and in every rak'ah of witr. The reasoning for nafl is that each pair of rak'ahs (shaf') constitutes an independent prayer unit. Therefore, when one stands for the third rak'ah, it is treated as if beginning a new prayer with a new takbirat al-ihram. Consequently, according to the well-known position of the Hanafi imams, only two rak'ahs are made obligatory by the first takbir. This explains why scholars recommend opening with the thana' (Subhanaka Allahumma) when standing for the third rak'ah of a nafl prayer. For witr, although witr is wajib in the Hanafi school, it carries characteristics of nafl (e.g., the number of rak'ahs, the permissibility of reciting Qunut). Therefore, to be cautious (ihtiyat), recitation is made obligatory in every rak'ah. The commentary elaborates that if one intends four rak'ahs of nafl and spoils the prayer after completing two rak'ahs, only the qada of one two-rak'ah set is obligatory, confirming that the first takbir only obligates two rak'ahs. The overall lesson distinguishes between the structure of fard prayers (where recitation is wajib in the first two rak'ahs only) and nafl/witr prayers (where recitation is wajib in every rak'ah).

Key Terms
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; in nafl prayer, each two rak'ahs form a separate legal unit.
تحریمة (tahrimah): The initial takbir (Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer; also used to mean the entire act of entering into prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is recitation obligatory in every rak'ah of nafl prayer?
A) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) always recited in every rak'ah of nafl
B) Because each pair of rak'ahs is a separate prayer unit
C) Because nafl is like fard in requiring recitation in all rak'ahs
D) Because the obligation of witr is established by hadith

Key Takeaway
Recitation is wajib in every rak'ah of nafl and witr prayers; the Hanafi school bases the nafl ruling on the independent nature of each pair of rak'ahs, and the witr ruling on caution due to its similarity to nafl.

Obligation to Make Up Invalidated Supererogatory Prayer
Ruling on qada for invalidated nafil with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada for an invalidated nafil prayer and explain the difference from the Shafi'i position using the opposing proofs.

Core Idea
Starting a nafil makes it binding — invalidation requires qada.

This lesson examines a key point of ikhtilaf: If a person begins a voluntary (nafil) prayer but then invalidates it, is he obliged to make it up? The Hanafi school says yes, while Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees. The dispute hinges on the binding nature of a voluntarily initiated act of worship. Understanding the usul principles behind each view clarifies the practical differences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school rules: if a nafil prayer is started and then invalidated, qada is wajib. Note that this applies to both prayers and fasts.
The ruling is from the matn of Al-Hidayah.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds no qada is required because the worshipper is a volunteer (mutabarri') and a volunteer is not bound.
Shafi'i evidence is the verse 'No blame on the doers of good' (Surah al-Tawbah: 91).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Analyze the Shafi'i dalil: the volunteer has no prior obligation, and the Quranic verse supports immunity from liability.
The verse is often used by Shafi'is to support the idea that a volunteer is not held to completion.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal: the performed portion becomes an act of worship; nullifying it is prohibited by 'Do not nullify your deeds' (Surah al-Anfal: 46). The Shafi'i verse applies only before initiation.
The Hanafi response distinguishes between pre- and post-initiation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: In the Hanafi school, if a nafil prayer is invalidated, qada is required; in the Shafi'i school, it is not. This affects daily practice, especially for those who start a nafil prayer and accidentally break it.

Chapter on supererogatory prayers: Ruling on making up after invalidating: He said: Whoever starts a supererogatory prayer and then invalidates it, he must make it up. Al-Shafi'i said: Making it up is not required upon him, because he is a volunteer in it, and there is no binding upon a volunteer. Our proof: That which was performed occurred as an act of obedience, so completing it is necessary to preserve it from nullification.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. It opens with the Hanafi ruling: if a person starts a supererogatory (nafil) prayer and then invalidates it, he must make it up (qada). Imam al-Shafi'i disagreed, arguing that a volunteer (mutabarri') is not bound, citing the Quranic verse 'There is no blame on the doers of good.' The Hanafi response: the part performed became an act of worship, so completing it is necessary to avoid nullifying good deeds, citing the verse 'Do not nullify your deeds.' The Shafi'i argument applies only before starting, not after.

Key Terms
نافلة (nafilah): A supererogatory prayer, voluntary act of worship.
متبرع (mutabarri'): One who volunteers an act of worship without prior obligation.
قضاء (qada): Making up a prayer that was invalidated after starting it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The entire prayer must be made up as qada.
D) It is recommended but not wajib to make it up.

Key Takeaway
Initiation of a nafil act of worship transforms it into a binding obligation; invalidation requires qada in the Hanafi school.
