Qada for Invalidated Four-Rak'ah Nafil: Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on qada for four-rak'ah nafil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position and Abu Yusuf's view on qada for a four-rak'ah nafil invalidated after two rak'ahs, and apply the school's tarjih.

Core Idea
In a four-rak'ah nafil, each pair (shaf') is independent; invalidation of the second requires qada of only the second.

This lesson examines an internal Hanafi dispute: if a person starts a four-rak'ah nafil, completes the first two rak'ahs with qa'dah, and then invalidates the last two, how many rak'ahs must be made up? The majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) holds that only the second pair (shaf') is invalidated, so two rak'ahs are required. Abu Yusuf argues that starting a four-rak'ah prayer makes all four wajib, analogizing to a vow. We will analyze the proofs and understand the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exact scenario
The case: a person begins a four-rak'ah nafil, recites in the first two, performs the first sitting (qa'dah), then invalidates the last two rak'ahs. The question: what qada is required?
Key detail: the first two rak'ahs are completed and valid.
2
State the majority position and its proof
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rule that only two rak'ahs (the second shaf') must be made up. Their proof: the first shaf' is complete; standing for the third rak'ah is like a new initiation (tahrimah) that binds only the second shaf'. The validity of the first shaf' does not depend on the second.
The first shaf' is a separate unit once the sitting is performed.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position and his qiyas
Abu Yusuf says all four rak'ahs must be made up. He analogizes starting a four-rak'ah prayer to making a vow (nathr): if one vows four rak'ahs, all four become wajib; similarly, initiating four rak'ahs makes all four binding.
Abu Yusuf's argument is based on qiyas khafi (hidden analogy).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to Abu Yusuf
The majority responds: initiation binds only what is started and what is necessary for its validity. The first shaf' is already valid without the second; the second shaf' alone becomes binding at the moment of standing for the third rak'ah.
This distinguishes the four-rak'ah nafil from a vow where the entire act is stipulated from the outset.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the majority view: qada of two rak'ahs. The practical difference is clear: one must make up either two or four rak'ahs depending on which view is followed.
Tarjih authority: Al-Hidayah presents the majority view as stronger; Zahir al-Riwayah supports it.

بطلان التي
الابها وفي
بطلان الت
If he prayed four (nafil) and recited in the first two and sat, then invalidated the last two, he makes up two rak'ahs because the first shaf' (pair) is completed, and standing for the third is like a new initiation (tahrimah), thus binding. This is if he invalidated after starting the second shaf'. If he invalidated before starting, he does not make up. From Abu Yusuf, he makes up four, analogizing to a vow. The two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say: initiation binds only what is started and what is necessary for its validity; validity of the first shaf' does not depend on the second. Similarly for the sunnah of zuhr (since it is nafil). Some say he makes up four out of caution.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage details an intra-Hanafi dispute about a specific scenario: a person starts a four-rak'ah nafil, completes the first two rak'ahs with recitation and sitting, then invalidates the last two. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) rule that only two rak'ahs (the second shaf') must be made up, because the first shaf' is complete and the standing for the third is like a new initiation. Abu Yusuf analogizes starting the four-rak'ah prayer to a vow (nathr); if one vows four rak'ahs, four become obligatory, so too if one initiates four, all four become binding. The majority respond that initiation binds only what is started (the second shaf') and what is necessary for its validity (which does not include the first shaf'). The passage also notes that if the last two are invalidated before standing for the third, no qada is required for anything. The sunnah of zuhr is mentioned as similar to this nafil ruling. A cautious opinion says make up four because the whole is like one prayer.

Key Terms
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs in a prayer. In a four-rak'ah nafil, the first two are the first shaf' and the last two are the second shaf'.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The inaugural takbir that initiates the prayer or a new pair of rak'ahs.
نذر (nathr): A vow to perform an act of worship, making it wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

intermediate

Making Up Invalidated Rak'ahs in Four-Rak'ah Nafl
Inter-madhhab dispute on qada of invalidated nafl prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on making up invalidated rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah nafl and evaluate Abu Yusuf's counter-argument.

Core Idea
In a four-rak'ah nafl, the first two rak'ahs are an independent unit; only the second pair must be remade if invalidated.

This lesson addresses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: when a person begins a four-rak'ah nafl prayer, completes the first two rak'ahs with recitation and sitting, but then invalidates the last two, how many rak'ahs must be made up? The majority of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) holds that only the second pair need repetition, while Abu Yusuf argues for all four. Understanding the underlying principle—whether the first pair is an independent unit—is key.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling according to Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad: make up only two rak'ahs. This is based on the first pair being complete and the third rak'ah initiating a new unit.
The first pair (shaff) is considered a complete prayer unit once the sitting (qadah) is performed.
2
Identify the opponent's view
State Abu Yusuf's position: make up all four rak'ahs. His evidence is qiyas to a vow (nadhr)—just as vowing four rak'ahs makes all four binding, so does starting a four-rak'ah nafl.
Abu Yusuf treats the entire four-rak'ah sequence as a single prayer, not two independent pairs.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine Abu Yusuf's analogy: starting the prayer with the intention of four rak'ahs creates a commitment to complete all four, similar to a nadhr obligation.
The 'start' (shurū') is seen as a binding act that encompasses the entire intended number.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the majority's rebuttal: the start only makes binding what is started and what is necessary for its validity. The first pair is valid independently; the second pair does not affect its validity. Thus, only the second pair is made binding.
The distinction: unlike the second rak'ah of a fard prayer (which depends on the first), the second pair in nafl does not depend on the first.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a person who invalidates after the first pair makes up two rak'ahs (majority view) or four (Abu Yusuf). The difference also applies to the four-rak'ah sunnah of zuhr.
The majority view is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.

Chapter of Supererogatory Prayers: And if he prays four and recites in the first two and sits, then invalidates the last two, he makes up two rak'ahs because the first pair has been completed, and standing for the third is like a new opening takbeer, thus it makes binding. This is when he invalidates the last two after starting them. And if he invalidates before starting the second pair, he does not make up the last two. And from Abu Yusuf that he makes up four, considering the start like a vow. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) the start makes binding what he started and what is necessary for its validity, and the validity of the first pair does not depend on the second, unlike the second rak'ah. And upon this is the sunnah of zuhr because it is nafl. And it is said he makes up four out of precaution because it is like one prayer. Translation: And if he starts with the intention of four rak'ahs (nafl prayer) and recites in the first two and sits, then invalidates the last two, then he makes up only two rak'ahs because the first pair is complete and standing for the third is like an opening takbeer, so that makes only two rak'ahs binding. This ruling is when he invalidates after starting the second pair. And if he invalidates before starting the second pair, he will not make up the last two. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that he makes up four, analogizing the start to a vow. And the evidence of the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the start makes binding what he started and what is necessary for its validity, and the validity of the first pair does not depend on the second, unlike the second rak'ah. And upon this difference is the sunnah of zuhr because it is nafl. And some scholars said he makes up four out of precaution because it is like one prayer. Explanation: The scenario is that a person started nafl prayer with the intention of four rak'ahs, and recited in the first two and sat after two rak'ahs, then invalidated the second pair, so only the second pair's qada' is obligatory. The condition of sitting after two rak'ahs is mentioned because if he did not sit after two and invalidated the last two, then by consensus four rak'ahs qada' are obligatory. The conclusion is that if after standing for the third rak'ah he invalidates the second pair, then qada' of the second pair is obligatory.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the chapter on supererogatory prayers (nawafil) regarding a person who begins a four-rak'ah nafl prayer, completes the first two rak'ahs with recitation and sitting for tashahhud, then invalidates the last two rak'ahs. The ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad is that only two rak'ahs must be made up, because the first pair (shaff) is considered a complete unit. Standing for the third rak'ah is analogous to a new opening takbeer (tahrimah), and thus it only makes the second pair binding. If the invalidation occurs before standing for the third, nothing is required as the second pair was not started. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that all four rak'ahs must be made up, drawing an analogy to a vow (nadhr): just as vowing four rak'ahs makes all four obligatory, starting a four-rak'ah nafl also makes all four binding. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) respond that the start only makes binding what is started and what is necessary for its validity; the validity of the first pair does not depend on the second pair, unlike the second rak'ah's dependence on the first. This dispute extends to the four rak'ahs of sunnah before zuhr, since that is also nafl. Some later scholars (mashayikh) recommend making up four rak'ahs out of precaution, considering the four as a single prayer.

Key Terms
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; in nafl, each two rak'ahs can constitute a separate unit.
تحریمہ (taḥrīmah): The opening takbeer that initiates prayer and makes prohibitions binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Four rak'ahs
B) Two rak'ahs
C) None
D) It depends on the intention

Key Takeaway
In a four-rak'ah nafl, if the first two rak'ahs are completed with sitting, only the second pair (two rak'ahs) must be made up if invalidated after starting it.

Omission of Recitation in All Rak'ahs of 4-Rak'ah Nafl
Ruling on how many rak'ahs to repeat when no recitation occurs in any rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on the repetition required when recitation is omitted in a four-rak'ah nafl, and explain the underlying principles regarding the tahrimah.

Core Idea
Omission of recitation affects the validity of the tahrimah; the number of rak'ahs to repeat depends on whether the tahrimah is invalidated or just the performance.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute over how many rak'ahs must be repeated when a person prays four rak'ahs of nafl without any recitation. The key is whether the opening takbeer (tahrimah) is invalidated or merely the performance. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold one view, while Abu Yusuf offers a different analysis.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: repeat two rak'ahs.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
2
Identify the opposing view
Abu Yusuf holds that four rak'ahs must be repeated.
His view is based on a different classification of recitation.
3
Follow Abu Yusuf's reasoning
He considers recitation an additional pillar (rukn za'id); its omission invalidates the performance (ada') but not the tahrimah.
Thus the prayer is not fully void; only the performance is flawed.
4
Analyse the majority's response
Abu Hanifa distinguishes omitting in both first two rak'ahs (invalidates tahrimah) vs. one (does not). Muhammad holds that omission in either invalidates.
Each pair of nafl is a separate prayer for Abu Hanifa.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: two vs. four rak'ahs must be made up.
The mufta bihi is the majority view (two rak'ahs).

And if he prays four and does not recite anything in them, he repeats two rak'ahs. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And according to Abu Yusuf, he makes up four. And this issue has eight aspects. The principle is that according to Muhammad, omission of recitation in the first two or in one of them necessitates invalidation of the tahrimah because it is contracted for actions. And according to Abu Yusuf, omission of recitation in the first pair does not necessitate invalidation of the tahrimah, only invalidates the performance because recitation is an additional pillar. Do you not see that prayer exists without it, except that performance is valid only with it, and invalidation of performance does not exceed its omission, so it does not invalidate the tahrimah. Commentary
This passage discusses a person who prays four rak'ahs of nafl and omits recitation entirely in all rak'ahs. According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, he must repeat two rak'ahs, while Imam Abu Yusuf says four. The underlying principle involves the status of the opening takbeer (tahrimah). For Muhammad, omitting recitation in either the first two or even in one of them invalidates the tahrimah because it is contracted for the actions of prayer. For Abu Yusuf, recitation is an additional pillar; prayer can exist without it but performance is valid only with it; omission merely invalidates the performance (ada') without affecting the tahrimah. For Abu Hanifa, omission in both first two invalidates the tahrimah, but omission in only one does not, because each pair of nafl is a separate prayer; the invalidation of one pair does not affect the other. The text indicates that the issue has eight aspects (likely referring to different scenarios). The Urdu commentary (which is incomplete in the OCR) would elaborate further.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The opening takbeer that makes prayer binding and prohibits worldly actions.
ركن زائد (rukn za'id): An additional pillar; recitation is considered a pillar that is not essential for the existence of prayer but for its validity.

Principles of the Three Imams on Recitation Omission in Nafl
Lists eight scenarios of recitation omission and explains the usul of the three imams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principles of each of the three Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the effect of omitting recitation in the first two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah nafl prayer, and apply these principles to at least two of the eight scenarios to determine whether the tahrima is nullified or only the ada is corrupted.

Core Idea
Omitting recitation in the first shaf' of a nafl prayer triggers a three-way intra-Hanafi dispute over whether the tahrima itself is invalidated or just the performance.

In this passage, al-Marghinani presents three distinct principles from the founders of the Hanafi school. The disagreement hinges on whether the tahrima (opening takbir) is contracted for valid actions only, and whether the omission of recitation in the first two rak'ahs (the first shaf') strikes at the essence of the prayer's validity. Understanding this dispute illuminates how Hanafi usul al-fiqh allows for multiple valid interpretations within a single madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
The dispute is about the legal effect of omitting recitation in the first two rak'ahs (first shaf') of a four-rak'ah nafl prayer. Does it nullify the tahrima (opening takbir) entirely, or only corrupt the performance (ada) while leaving the tahrima intact?
Note that the tahrima is the 'ihram' of prayer; its nullification means the prayer never validly began.
2
State Imam Muhammad's principle and its basis
Imam Muhammad: Omitting recitation in either both or one of the first two rak'ahs invalidates the tahrima. Basis: The tahrima is contracted for valid actions; if the actions become void due to missing an integral (recitation), the tahrima cannot stand. 'تھریمہ منعقد کیا جاتا ہے افعال کے لئے اور افعال ترک قرآت کی وجہ فاسد ہو جاتے ہیں'.
This is the most stringent view.
3
State Imam Abu Yusuf's principle and its basis
Imam Abu Yusuf: Omitting recitation in the first shaf' corrupts the performance (ada) but does not nullify the tahrima. Basis: Recitation is a rukn whose absence can be compensated (e.g., a mute person prays without recitation). Corruption of ada is less severe than complete abandonment; if abandonment (by hadath) does not nullify tahrima, a fortiori corruption does not. 'فساد ادا ترک ادا سے پر نہیں'.
This is the most lenient view; the prayer remains valid in its essence but must be repeated.
4
State Imam Abu Hanifa's principle and its basis
Imam Abu Hanifa: Omitting recitation in both rak'ahs of the first shaf' nullifies the tahrima, but omitting it in only one rak'ah does not. Basis for two rak'ahs: Each shaf' is an independent prayer, so omitting recitation in a whole shaf' empties it of an essential, voiding the tahrima. Basis for one rak'ah: Qiyas would demand nullification (as in Fajr), but since Hasan al-Basri held that one rak'ah suffices, the school acts on precaution: the prayer is corrupted but the tahrima remains for the requirement of the second shaf'.
This is a middle position that balances qiyas and ikhtilaf.
5
Apply each principle to two scenarios
Scenario 2 (omission in first shaf' only): Abu Yusuf → tahrima remains, ada corrupt. Muhammad → tahrima void, entire prayer invalid. Abu Hanifa → tahrima void (since both rak'ahs omitted). Scenario 3 (omission in one rak'ah of first shaf'): Abu Yusuf → tahrima remains. Muhammad → tahrima void. Abu Hanifa → tahrima remains (since only one rak'ah omitted).
The eight scenarios are given for further application.

Source Text

باب النوافل
رکعت ثانیہ اور ثالثہ میں ترک کی۔ (۱۶) رکعت ثانیہ اور رکعت رابعہ میں ترک کی۔ صنف نے پہلی صورت کو بیان نہیں کیا کیونکہ مقصود اقتسام فساد کو بیان کرنا ہے اور پہلی صورت میں چونکہ تمام رکعتوں میں قرآت کی گئی اس لئے وہ اقسام فساد میں سے نہیں ہوگی۔ اور چونکہ سات صورتیں اتحاد حکم کی وجہ سے انہیں آٹھ میں متداخل ہو گئیں اس لئے اب کل آٹھ صورتیں باقی رہیں جن کے بارے میں فاضل مصنف نے فرمایا و هذه المسئلة على ثمانية اوجه --
صاحب ہدایہ کے پیش نظر آٹھ صورتوں میں سے یہ آٹھ ہیں:-
(۱) چاروں میں قرآت کو ترک کر دیا گیا ہو۔
(۲) شفع اول میں ترک کیا گیا ہو۔
(۳) شفع اول کی کسی ایک رکعت میں ترک کیا گیا ہو۔
(۴) شفع ثانی میں ترک کر دیا گیا ہو۔
(۵) شفع ثانی کی کسی ایک رکعت میں ترک کیا گیا ہو۔
(۶) شفع اول کی کسی ایک رکعت میں اور شفع ثانی کی کسی ایک رکعت میں ترک کیا گیا ہو۔
(۷) شفع ثانی کی دونوں رکعتوں اور شفع اول کی کسی ایک رکعت میں ترک کیا گیا ہو۔
(۸) شفع اول کی دونوں رکعتوں اور شفع ثانی کی کسی ایک رکعت میں ترک کیا گیا ہو۔ (الکفایة)
چونکہ اس مسئلہ کی تخریج ائمہ ثلاثہ کے علیحدہ علیحدہ اصول پر مبنی ہے اس لئے صاحب ہدایہ نے اولاً اصول کو ذکر فرمایا ہے۔ چنانچہ کہا کہ محمد کی اصل اور بنیادی بات یہ ہے کہ پہلی دو رکعتوں میں قرآت چھوڑنا یا ان دونوں میں سے کسی ایک میں چھوڑنا تحریمہ کو باطل کر دیتا ہے۔ کیونکہ تحریمہ منعقد کیا جاتا ہے افعال کے لئے اور افعال ترک قرآت کی وجہ فاسد ہو جاتے ہیں۔ لہذا وہ تحریمہ جو افعال کے لئے منعقد کیا جاتا ہے وہ بھی فاسد ہو جائے گا۔ امام ابو یوسف کی اصل یہ ہے کہ شفع اول میں قرآت چھوڑنا تحریمہ کو باطل نہیں کرتا بلکہ ادا کو فاسد کر دیتا ہے کیونکہ قرآت ایک رکن ہے۔ چنانچہ آپ غور کیجئے کہ بغیر قرآت کے بھی نماز پائی جاتی ہے جیسے گونگے کے حق میں نماز بلا قرآت ہے۔ البتہ بغیر قرآت کے ادا نہیں ہوتی۔ بہرحال شفع اول میں قرآت کا ترک کرنا فساد ادا کا موجب ہے بطلان تحریمہ کا موجب نہیں ہے اور فساد ادا ترک ادا سے پر نہیں یعنی ادا کو اگر ترک کر دیا مثلاً حدث ہو گیا اور وضو کے لئے گیا تو اس صورت میں اس نے ادا چھوڑ دی مگر تحریمہ باطل نہیں ہوا پس بذریعہ ترک ادا تحریمہ باطل نہیں ہوتا تو فساد ادا سے بدرجہ اولی تحریمہ باطل نہیں ہوگا۔
امام ابوحنیفہ کی اصل یہ ہے کہ اول کی دو رکعتوں میں قرآت چھوڑنا تحریمہ باطل کر دیتا ہے اور ایک رکعت میں چھوڑنا تحریمہ باطل نہیں کرتا۔ پہلی بات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ نفل کا ہر شفع علیحدہ مستقل نماز ہے پس اس میں قرآت چھوڑنا نماز کو قرآت سے خالی کرنا ہے اور قرآت سے خالی ہونے کی صورت میں نماز اس طرح فاسد ہو جاتی ہے کہ اس کی قضاء واجب ہوگی اور تحریمہ باطل ہو جائے گا۔ دوسری بات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک رکعت میں قرآت چھوڑنے کی وجہ سے قیاس کا تقاضہ تو یہی ہے کہ مثل اول کے تحریمہ باطل ہو اور نماز فاسد ہو جائے جیسے کہ فجر کی ایک رکعت میں قرآت چھوڑنے سے نماز فاسد ہو جاتی ہے مگر ایک رکعت میں ترک قرآت کی بنا پر نماز کا فاسد ہونا مختلف فیہ ہے۔ کیونکہ حسن بصری کا مذہب ہے کہ ایک رکعت میں قرآت کرنا کافی ہے اگر دو میں سے ایک میں قرآت کی اور ایک میں نہیں کی تو نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی۔ پس احتیاط پر عمل کرتے ہوئے ہم نے کہا کہ ایک رکعت میں ترک قرآت سے نماز تو فاسد ہو جائے گی اور قضاء واجب ہوگی لیکن شفع ثانی کے لزوم کے حق میں تحریمہ باقی رہے گا۔
Chapter of Voluntary Prayers. [The author] mentioned omission in the second and third rak'ah, and (16) omission in the second and fourth rak'ah. The author did not mention the first form because the purpose is to explain the division of corruption (ifsad), and in the first form, since recitation occurred in all rak'ahs, it is not from the types of corruption. And since the seven forms became interwoven into eight due to the unity of ruling, now eight forms remain, about which the eminent author said: 'This issue has eight aspects.' According to the author of Hidayah, these eight are: (1) Recitation omitted in all four. (2) Omitted in the first shaf'. (3) Omitted in one rak'ah of the first shaf'. (4) Omitted in the second shaf'. (5) Omitted in one rak'ah of the second shaf'. (6) Omitted in one rak'ah of the first shaf' and one rak'ah of the second shaf'. (7) Omitted in both rak'ahs of the second shaf' and one rak'ah of the first shaf'. (8) Omitted in both rak'ahs of the first shaf' and one rak'ah of the second shaf'. (Al-Kifayah) Since the derivation of this issue is based on the separate principles of the three imams, the author of Hidayah first mentions the principles. Thus he said: The principle of Muhammad is that omitting recitation in the first two rak'ahs or in one of them invalidates the tahrima, because the tahrima is contracted for actions, and the actions become void due to omission of recitation. Therefore the tahrima contracted for actions also becomes void. Imam Abu Yusuf's principle is that omitting recitation in the first shaf' does not invalidate the tahrima but rather corrupts the ada (performance), because recitation is a rukn. Consider that prayer is still valid without recitation, as for a mute person, prayer is without recitation. However, without recitation, ada is not achieved. In any case, omitting recitation in the first shaf' causes corruption of ada, not nullification of tahrima. And corruption of ada is less than abandoning ada; if one abandons ada, e.g., by hadath and goes for wudu', then the ada is abandoned but the tahrima is not nullified. So by abandoning ada, the tahrima is not nullified; a fortiori, by corruption of ada, the tahrima is not nullified. Imam Abu Hanifa's principle is that omitting recitation in the first two rak'ahs invalidates the tahrima, but omitting it in one rak'ah does not invalidate the tahrima. His proof for the first part is that each shaf' of nafl is a separate independent prayer; thus omitting recitation in it empties the prayer from recitation, and when empty from recitation, the prayer becomes void such that its qada' is obligatory, and the tahrima becomes void. His proof for the second part is that due to omitting recitation in one rak'ah, qiyas requires that, similar to the first, the tahrima should become void and the prayer corrupt, like the corruption of Fajr prayer by omitting recitation in one rak'ah. However, the corruption of prayer due to omitting recitation in one rak'ah is disputed, because Hasan al-Basri's school is that recitation in one rak'ah is sufficient; if one recites in one of the two and not in the other, the prayer is not invalid. Therefore, acting on precaution, we say that omitting recitation in one rak'ah will corrupt the prayer and qada' becomes obligatory, but the tahrima will remain for the requirement of the second shaf'.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of omitting recitation in voluntary prayers. The author first lists eight possible scenarios of omission in a four-rak'ah nafl prayer. Then he explains the fundamental principles of the three major Hanafi imams concerning omission in the first two rak'ahs. Imam Muhammad's principle: omitting recitation in either both or one of the first two rak'ahs invalidates the tahrima (opening takbir) because the tahrima is contracted for the actions, and if the actions are void due to missing an integral, the tahrima is also void. Imam Abu Yusuf distinguishes between the tahrima and the performance (ada): omission corrupts the performance but does not affect the tahrima, as recitation is a rukn whose absence can be compensated (like for a mute) and corruption of ada is less severe than complete abandonment. Imam Abu Hanifa differentiates between omitting recitation in two rak'ahs (invalidates tahrima) and in one rak'ah (does not invalidate tahrima). His reasoning: each shaf' (pair) is an independent prayer, so omitting recitation in a whole shaf' nullifies the tahrima, but omitting it in one rak'ah is disputed among scholars; he adopts a cautious middle position. These principles form the basis for the specific rulings that follow.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (tahrima): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that establishes the state of ihram for prayer; its nullification means the prayer never properly began.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs in nafl prayer; each shaf' is considered an independent unit in the context of recitation obligations.
ادا (ada): The performance of the prayer in a valid manner; corruption of ada means the prayer is performed defectively but the state of ihram remains.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, what is the effect of omitting recitation in the first two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah nafl prayer?
A) The tahrima is invalidated and the prayer must be restarted.
B) The tahrima remains valid but the prayer is corrupt, requiring qada' of all four rak'ahs.
C) The tahrima remains valid and the prayer is valid; no qada' needed.
D) The tahrima is invalidated only if both rak'ahs are omitted.

Key Takeaway
The three Hanafi imams differ on whether omitting recitation in the first shaf' of a nafl prayer nullifies the tahrima or only corrupts the performance, based on distinct usul regarding the nature of the tahrima and the role of recitation.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Qada' for Omitting Recitation in Nafl Prayer
Applies the three imams' principles to the case of omitting recitation in all four rak'ahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding the obligation of qada' when recitation is omitted in all four rak'ahs of a nafl prayer, and explain the underlying principle of tahrima voidance.

Core Idea
The number of rak'ahs to repeat depends on whether the tahrima is voided by omitting recitation in the first two rak'ahs.

This passage from Al-Hidayah applies the principles of the three Hanafi imams to a specific scenario: a worshipper omits recitation entirely in a four-rak'ah nafl prayer. The difference in ruling hinges on a fundamental question—does the omission invalidate the very beginning of the prayer (tahrima) or not? Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace rulings back to their usul roots.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
Recognize that the subject is a nafl prayer of four rak'ahs where recitation is omitted in every rak'ah. The dispute concerns the obligation of qada' (repetition).
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
According to them, omitting recitation in the first two rak'ahs (first shaf') voids the tahrima. Consequently, the second shaf' is invalid; effectively only two rak'ahs were initiated and corrupted, so qada' of two rak'ahs is wajib.
3
State the position of Abu Yusuf
According to him, the tahrima remains valid despite omission in the first shaf'. Thus all four rak'ahs are validly begun but become corrupt due to omission of recitation, requiring qada' of all four rak'ahs.
4
Identify the underlying principle
The key difference is whether the omission of a wajib (recitation) in the first two rak'ahs voids the initial takbir (tahrima). This is a principle-level dispute within the Hanafi school.
This is not a dispute about the obligation of recitation itself, but about its effect on the validity of the prayer's beginning.
5
Note the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf is the number of rak'ahs to be repeated: 2 vs 4. This affects the worshipper's obligation and the imam's guidance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ جب ہر ایک کی بیان کردہ اصل ثابت ہو چکی تو مسئلہ متن کی توضیح اس طرح ہوگی کہ جب مصلی نے چاروں رکعتوں میں قرآت نہیں کی تو طرفین کے نزدیک شفع اول میں ترک قرآت کی وجہ سے تحریمہ باطل ہوگیا اور جب تحریمہ باطل تو شفع ثانی کا شروع کرنا درست نہیں ہوا۔ پس گویا اس نے دو ہی رکعت کے لئے تحریمہ باندھا تھا اور انہیں کو فاسد کر دیا۔ تو اس کی قضاء واجب ہوگی اور چونکہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تحریمہ باطل نہیں ہوا لہذا شفع ثانی کو شروع کرنا بھی صحیح ہوا لیکن ترک قرآت کی وجہ سے چاروں رکعتیں فاسد ہو گئیں۔ اس لئے چاروں کی قضاء واجب ہوگی۔ واللہ اعلم
The author of Hidayah said: When each one's stated principle is established, the explanation of the text's issue is as follows: When the praying person did not recite in any of the four rak'ahs, then according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), due to omitting recitation in the first shaf', the tahrima became void, and when the tahrima is void, beginning the second shaf' is not valid. So it is as if he contracted the tahrima for only two rak'ahs and corrupted those two. Therefore, qada' of those two is obligatory. And since according to Imam Abu Yusuf the tahrima did not become void, beginning the second shaf' was valid, but due to omitting recitation, all four rak'ahs became corrupt. Therefore, qada' of all four is obligatory. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This is an application of the three imams' principles to a specific case: the worshipper omits recitation in all four rak'ahs of a nafl prayer. According to Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Hanifa (the 'two'), omitting recitation in the first two rak'ahs invalidates the tahrima. Consequently, the initial takbir becomes void, and the subsequent second shaf' is not a valid continuation. Effectively, only two rak'ahs were intended (though corrupted), so only two rak'ahs need to be repeated (qada'). According to Imam Abu Yusuf, the tahrima remains valid despite omission in the first shaf'; thus the second shaf' is properly begun. However, since all four rak'ahs lack recitation, the entire prayer is corrupt, requiring qada' of all four rak'ahs. This demonstrates how the difference in principles leads to differing qada' obligations.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): The compensatory repetition of a prayer that was performed corruptly or missed.
تحریمہ (tahrima): The initial takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) that commences the prayer; considered a pillar in Hanafi fiqh.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; in a four-rak'ah prayer, the first two rak'ahs form the first shaf' and the last two form the second shaf'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person omits recitation in all four rak'ahs of a nafl prayer, how many rak'ahs must he repeat according to Imam Abu Yusuf?
A) Two rak'ahs
B) Four rak'ahs
C) Eight rak'ahs
D) None, the prayer is valid

Key Takeaway
The qada' obligation for a corrupted nafl prayer depends on whether the tahrima is considered void, leading to a difference of 2 vs 4 rak'ahs.

Ruling on Recitation in Nafl: Qada' of Last Two Only When Sitting Performed
Ruling with reasoning and conditional nuance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when recitation is omitted in the last two rak'ahs of nafl and distinguish the consequence when the first sitting is present or absent.

Core Idea
Omitting recitation in the last two rak'ahs corrupts only the second shaf'; the first remains valid if the sitting was performed.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in nafl prayer: when recitation is only performed in the first two rak'ahs. The Hanafi school holds that only the last two rak'ahs require repetition (qada'), but this depends on whether the first sitting was performed. We will explore the reasoning and the conditional ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Consider a four-rak'ah nafl prayer where the worshipper recited (Fatiha + surah) in the first two rak'ahs but omitted all recitation in the last two.
2
State the default ruling
By Hanafi consensus (ijma'), only the last two rak'ahs (the second shaf') require qada'. The first shaf' remains valid.
The text states 'بالاجماع' (by consensus) among the three imams.
3
Analyze the reasoning
The tahrima (prohibition of worldly acts) was not invalidated because recitation in the first shaf' was correct. Thus the beginning of the second shaf' was valid. Corruption of the second shaf' due to omitted recitation does not affect the first shaf'.
4
Introduce the conditional factor
This ruling applies only if the worshipper performed the first sitting (qa'dah) after the second rak'ah. The sitting is wajib in a four-rak'ah prayer.
The text adds 'وہ خیال رہے کہ یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جبکہ شفع اول پر قعدہ کیا ہو'.
5
Determine the alternative ruling
If the sitting was omitted, both shaf' are corrupt: the second due to omitted recitation, the first due to omitted wajib sitting. In that case, qada' of all four rak'ahs is required.
The text: 'اگر قعدہ نہیں کیا تو چار کی قضاء واجب ہوگی'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قرأ في الاوليين لا غير فعليه قضاء الاخريين بالاجماع لان التحريمة لم تبطل فصح الشروع في الثاني ثم فساده بترك القراءة لا يوجب فساد الشفع الأول.
ترجمہ: اور اگر اس نے فقط اولین میں قرآت کی تو اس پر بالاجماع اخرین کی قضاء واجب ہے کیونکہ تحریمہ باطل نہیں ہوا تو شفع ثانی کا شروع کرنا صحیح ہوا۔ پھر ترک قرآت کی وجہ سے شفع ثانی کا فساد شفع اول کے فساد کو واجب نہیں کرتا۔
تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر نفل کی پہلی دو رکعتوں میں قرآت کی اور آخر کی دو میں قرآت نہیں کی تو بالاجماع اس پر آخر کی دو کی قضاء کرنا واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ شفع اول میں قرآت کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے تحریمہ باطل نہیں ہوا پس جب تحریمہ باطل نہیں ہوا تو شفع ثانی کا شروع کرنا بھی صحیح ہوا۔ قضاء بھی فقط شفع ثانی ہی کی واجب ہوگی نہ کہ شفع اول کی۔ لیکن ترک قرآت کی وجہ سے شفع ثانی کا فاسد ہونا شفع اول کے فساد کو متلازم نہیں۔ پس جب شفع ثانی ہی فاسد ہوا ہے تو اس کی قضاء واجب ہوگی، شفع اول کی نہیں۔ اور یہ خیال رہے کہ یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جبکہ شفع اول پر قعدہ کیا ہو۔ چنانچہ اگر قعدہ نہیں کیا تو چار کی قضاء واجب ہوگی: شفع ثانی کی ترک قرآت کی وجہ سے اور شفع اول کی قعدہ اخیرہ کے ترک کی وجہ سے۔
And if he recited only in the first two (rak'ahs), then upon him is qada' of the last two by consensus, because the tahrima did not become void, so beginning the second (shaf') was valid. Then its corruption due to omission of recitation does not necessitate the corruption of the first shaf'. Translation: And if he recited only in the first two, then by consensus qada' of the last two is obligatory upon him, because the tahrima did not become void, so beginning the second shaf' was valid. Then the corruption of the second shaf' due to omission of recitation does not make the corruption of the first shaf' necessary. Elaboration: The issue is that if a person recited in the first two rak'ahs of a nafl prayer and did not recite in the last two, then by consensus qada' of the last two is obligatory. Because due to recitation in the first shaf', the tahrima did not become void; thus the beginning of the second shaf' was also valid. Qada' is only obligatory for the second shaf', not the first. But the corruption of the second shaf' due to omission of recitation is not necessarily connected to corruption of the first shaf'. So since only the second shaf' is corrupt, its qada' is obligatory, not the first. And note that this ruling applies when he performed the sitting (qa'dah) at the end of the first shaf'. If he did not sit, then qada' of all four is obligatory: the second shaf' due to omission of recitation, and the first shaf' due to omission of the final sitting.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where the worshipper recites in the first two rak'ahs but omits recitation in the last two. The text states there is consensus (ijma') that only the last two require qada'. The reasoning: since recitation was performed in the first shaf', the tahrima remains intact; thus the second shaf' was validly started. The omission of recitation corrupts the second shaf' alone, without affecting the first shaf'. Consequently, only the last two rak'ahs need to be repeated. However, the author adds a crucial condition: if the worshipper did not perform the sitting (qa'dah) after the first two rak'ahs (which is wajib in a four-rak'ah prayer), then both shaf' are corrupted: the second due to omitted recitation and the first due to omitted sitting. In that case, qada' of all four rak'ahs becomes obligatory.

Key Terms
قعدہ (qa'dah): The sitting after the second rak'ah (for tashahhud) in a four-rak'ah prayer; its omission affects the validity of the first shaf'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person recites in the first two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah nafl but not in the last two, and performed the sitting after the first two?
A) The entire prayer is valid; no qada' required.
B) Qada' of all four rak'ahs is required.
C) Qada' of only the last two rak'ahs is required.
D) The prayer is invalid and must be restarted completely.

Key Takeaway
In a four-rak'ah nafl prayer, omitting recitation in the last two rak'ahs only corrupts the second shaf'; the first shaf' remains valid if the sitting was performed, but if the sitting is also omitted, the entire prayer becomes corrupt.

Recitation Only in Last Two Rak'ahs of Nafl: Agreed Ruling, Different Reasoning
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the legal basis for qada' of first two rak'ahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi difference in takhrij for the ruling on qada' when recitation is omitted in the first two rak'ahs of a nafl prayer.

Core Idea
All Hanafi imams agree on qada' of first two rak'ahs, but differ on whether tahrima is void or just ada is missing.

In Hanafi fiqh, sometimes a single ruling is unanimously accepted, yet the juristic reasoning (takhrij) differs among the founding imams. This lesson examines such a case: a person prays four rak'ahs of nafl but only recites in the last two. The obligation to repeat the first two is agreed upon, but the legal basis for that obligation reveals a deeper principle about the role of recitation in the structure of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Agreed Ruling
State that all three Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree that qada' of the first two rak'ahs is wajib. This is stated as 'بالاجماع' and 'بالاتفاق'.
The ruling is unanimous, so the debate is not about the outcome but about the reasoning.
2
Contrast the Two Positions
Explain that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that omitting recitation in the first shaf' invalidates the tahrima (declaration of prayer), so the prayer never properly began. Abu Yusuf argues that the tahrima remains valid, but the first two rak'ahs were not performed (ada) correctly.
The key difference is whether the omission affects the validity of the inception or the performance.
3
Analyze the Consequence
Note that while the practical outcome is the same (qada' of two rak'ahs), the underlying principles affect other cases. For example, if the worshipper stands up for the second shaf' without reciting in the first, the two would rule the entire prayer void, while Abu Yusuf would still consider the second shaf' valid.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) may emerge in variant scenarios.
4
Apply the Takhrij
Consider a variant: if a person recites only in the first two rak'ahs and omits recitation in the last two, the ruling would be qada' of the last two. The same takhrij applies.
This shows the consistency of the principle across different patterns of omission.

و لو قرأ في الاخريين لا غير فعليه قضاء الاوليين بالاجماع لان عندهما لم يصح الشروع في الشفع الاول.
ترجمہ: اور اگر اس نے فقط اخرین میں قرآت کی تو اس پر بالاجماع اولین کی قضاء واجب ہوگی کیونکہ طرفین کے نزدیک شفع اول میں شروع ہونا صحیح نہیں ہوا۔ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اگرچہ صحیح ہے لیکن اس نے آخر کی دو رکعتوں کو ادا کیا۔
تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مصلی نے اگر آخر کی دو رکعتوں میں قرآت کی اور اول کی دو میں قرآت کو چھوڑ دیا تو بالاتفاق پہلی دو کی قضاء واجب ہے۔ اس مسئلہ کے حکم میں تینوں حضرات متفق ہیں مگر تخریج میں مختلف ہیں۔ چنانچہ طرفین (امام ابوحنیفہ اور امام محمد) نے کہا کہ پہلی دو رکعتوں میں قرآت کے نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے تحریمہ باطل ہو گیا، لہذا شفع اول کا شروع کرنا ہی صحیح نہیں ہوا، اور اس نے جو پچھلی دو پڑھیں وہ شروع ہی سے نفل کے طور پر نہیں تھیں بلکہ اس نے نفلاً نہیں ادا کیا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف نے کہا: ہمارے نزدیک تحریمہ باطل نہیں ہوا، لہذا شفع اول کا شروع کرنا صحیح ہوا، لیکن بغیر قرآت کے ادا نہیں ہوا، پھر اس نے آخر کی دو کو ادا کیا (یعنی ان میں قرآت کی) تو ان کی ادا صحیح ہوئی، لیکن شفع اول کی رکعتیں ادا نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ان کی قضاء واجب ہے۔
And if he recited only in the last two (rak'ahs), then upon him is qada' of the first two by consensus, because according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), beginning the first shaf' was not valid. And according to Abu Yusuf, although it was valid, he performed (ada) the last two rak'ahs. Translation: And if he recited only in the last two, then by consensus qada' of the first two is obligatory upon him, because according to the two, beginning the first shaf' was not valid. And according to Abu Yusuf, although it was valid, he performed the last two rak'ahs. Elaboration: The issue is that if the praying person recited in the last two rak'ahs and omitted recitation in the first two, then by agreement qada' of the first two is obligatory. The three imams agree on the ruling but differ in its derivation. Thus the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) said: Due to absence of recitation in the first two rak'ahs, the tahrima became void, so beginning the first shaf' was not valid, and the last two he prayed were not originally as nafl; he did not perform them as nafl. And Imam Abu Yusuf said: In our view, the tahrima did not become void, so beginning the first shaf' was valid, but without recitation it was not performed (ada); then he performed the last two (with recitation), so their performance was valid, but because the first shaf' rak'ahs were not performed, qada' of them is obligatory.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage covers the case where the worshipper only recites in the last two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah nafl. There is agreement (ittifaq) among the three imams that qada' of the first two rak'ahs is obligatory, but the reasoning differs. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the 'two'), omitting recitation in the first two rak'ahs invalidates the tahrima from the start, so the prayer never properly began; consequently, the last two rak'ahs are not considered part of the same nafl prayer. The worshipper must repeat the first two rak'ahs. According to Abu Yusuf, the tahrima remains valid, so the first two rak'ahs were initiated but not performed correctly due to missing recitation. The last two rak'ahs are validly performed (with recitation), but the obligation to pray four rak'ahs remains unfulfilled because the first two were not properly ada. Thus, the first two must be repeated (qada'). The practical outcome is the same: qada' of two rak'ahs, but the juristic reasoning differs.

Key Terms
تخریج (takhrij): Juristic derivation or reasoning from principles to a specific ruling.
تحریمہ (tahrima): The opening declaration of prayer (takbir al-ihram) that marks the beginning of the state of ihram in salah.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs. In a four-rak'ah prayer, there are two shaf's: the first two and the last two.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a person recites only in the last two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah nafl, what is the agreed-upon ruling among the Hanafi imams?
A) The prayer is valid and no qada' is required.
B) Qada' of the last two rak'ahs is required.
C) Qada' of the first two rak'ahs is required.
D) Qada' of all four rak'ahs is required.

Key Takeaway
Consensus on a ruling does not preclude diversity in legal reasoning; the same outcome can be reached via different principles.

Consensus Rulings on Recitation Omission in Nafl
Explains four consensus cases of recitation omission in four-rak'ah nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four consensus rulings on qadā' for omitted recitation in a four-rak'ah supererogatory prayer and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect on the tahrīmah.

Core Idea
Recitation is wajib in every rak'ah of nafl; omission requires qadā' of the affected shaf‘, with consensus on the ruling despite disagreement on tahrīmah.

In supererogatory prayers, each rak'ah requires recitation (qirā’ah) as a wājib. If a worshipper omits recitation in some rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah nafl (divided into two shaf‘s of two), the Hanafi school agrees on which rak'ahs must be made up, even though they differ on whether the opening takbir (tahrīmah) remains valid. This lesson unpacks the four scenarios and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the prayer structure
A four-rak'ah nafl is composed of two shaf‘s (pairs): the first two rak'ahs (shaf‘ awwal) and the last two (shaf‘ thānī). The tahrīmah initiates the entire prayer.
Hanafi jurisprudence uses this shaf‘ terminology for supererogatory prayers of four rak'ahs.
2
Identify the legal status of recitation
Recitation in every rak'ah of nafl is wājib. Omission does not invalidate the rak'ah completely (it is not a rukn) but requires compensation through qadā' of that rak'ah or the affected shaf‘.
This is unlike obligatory prayers where recitation is fard in two rak'ahs.
3
Analyze the four scenarios
The passage lists four cases based on where recitation is performed: (1) only in first two, (2) only in last two, (3) first two and one of last two, (4) last two and one of first two. In each, the missing recitation triggers qadā' of the shaf‘ where omission occurred.
The consensus (ijmā‘) among the Hanafi imams on these specific qadā' rulings is emphasized.
4
Apply the consensus rule
For each case, determine which shaf‘ is defective due to omission. The healthy shaf‘ with full recitation remains valid; the defective shaf‘ must be repeated. The tahrīmah's status does not alter this practical outcome.
Example: If recitation is only in the first two (case 1), the second shaf‘ is defective → qadā' of last two.
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on tahrīmah
When recitation is entirely omitted from the first shaf‘ (e.g., no recitation in first two rak'ahs), Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the tahrīmah becomes invalid, so the second shaf‘ was never validly begun. Abu Yusuf maintains the tahrīmah remains valid. Despite this, all agree on the same qadā' ruling for the first two scenarios.
This dispute illustrates that ikhtilāf in reasoning does not always lead to difference in final fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بہر جا فاسد ہو جائے گی اور قضاء واجب ہوگی لیکن شفع ثانی کے لزوم کے حق میں تحریمہ باقی رہے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ جب ہر ایک کی بیان کردہ اصل ثابت ہو چکی تو مسئلہ متن کی توضیح اس طرح ہوگی کہ جب مصلی میں یہ شخص چاروں رکعتوں میں قرآت نہیں کی تو طرفین کے نزدیک شفع اول میں ترک قرآت کی وجہ سے تحریمہ باطل ہوگیا اور جب تحریمہ باطل ہوگیا تو شفع ثانی کا شروع کرنا درست نہیں ہوا۔ پس گویا اس نے دو ہی رکعت کے لئے تحریمہ باندھا تھا اور انہیں کو فاسد کر دیا۔ تو اس کی قضاء واجب ہوگی اور چونکہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تحریمہ باطل نہیں ہوا لہذا شفع ثانی کو شروع کرنا بھی صحیح ہوا لیکن ترک قرآت کی وجہ سے چاروں رکعتیں فاسد ہو گئیں۔ اس لئے چاروں کی قضاء واجب ہوگی۔ ولو قرأ في الأوليين لا غير فعليه قضاء الأخريين بالاجماع لان التحريمة لم تبطل فصح الشروع في الشفع الثاني ثم فساده بترك القرأة لا يوجب فساد الشفع الأول. ترجمہ: اور اگر اس نے فقط اولین میں قرآت کی تو اس پر بالاجماع آخرین کی قضاء واجب ہے کیونکہ تحریمہ تو باطل نہیں ہوا لہذا شفع ثانی کا شروع کرنا صحیح ہوا۔ پھر ترک قرآت کی وجہ سے شفع ثانی کا فساد شفع اول کے فساد کو واجب نہیں کرتا۔ ولو قرأ في الأخريين لا غير فعليه قضاء الأوليين بالاجماع لانه لم يصح الشروع في الشفع الثاني. ترجمہ: اور اگر اس نے فقط اخرین میں قرآت کی تو اس پر بالاجماع اولین کی قضاء واجب ہوگی کیونکہ طرفین کے نزدیک شروع ہونا صحیح نہیں ہوا۔ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اگرچہ صحیح ہے لیکن اس نے آخر کی دو رکعتوں کو ادا کیا۔ ولو قرأ في الأوليين وإحدى الأخريين فعليه قضاء الأخريين بالاجماع. ترجمہ: اگر پہلی دو میں اور اخرین کی ایک رکعت میں قرآت کی تو بالاتفاق اس پر اخرین کی قضاء واجب ہوگی۔ ولو قرأ في الأخريين وإحدى الأوليين فعليه قضاء الأوليين بالاجماع. ترجمہ: اور اگر اخرین میں اور اولین میں سے ایک میں قرآت کی تو اس پر بالاجماع اولین کی قضاء واجب ہے۔
If he recited in the first two only, then by consensus he must make up the last two, because the opening takbir did not become invalid, so the commencement of the second shaf‘ was valid; then its invalidation due to omitting recitation does not necessitate invalidation of the first shaf‘. If he recited in the last two only, then by consensus he must make up the first two, because the commencement of the second shaf‘ was not valid. If he recited in the first two and one of the last two, then by consensus he must make up the last two. If he recited in the last two and one of the first two, then by consensus he must make up the first two.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage presents four scenarios from the chapter on supererogatory prayers regarding omission of recitation (qirā’ah) in a four-rak‘ah nafl prayer, arranged as two sets of two (shaf‘ awwal and shaf‘ thānī). The author first explains the underlying principle: if recitation is completely omitted in the first two rak‘ahs, the opening takbir (tahrīmah) becomes invalid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two), but Abu Yusuf holds it remains valid. The four consensus rulings are: (1) reciting only in the first two — make up the last two; (2) reciting only in the last two — make up the first two; (3) reciting in the first two and one of the last two — make up the last two; (4) reciting in the last two and one of the first two — make up the first two. In all these, the tahrīmah is preserved because at least one rak‘ah of the first shaf‘ contains recitation, so the second shaf‘ is validly initiated. The invalidation of the second shaf‘ due to missing recitation does not retroactively invalidate the first shaf‘. The consensus (ijmā‘) refers to agreement among the Hanafi imams on the ruling, though they differ in reasoning.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (taḥrīmah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that initiates the prayer, marking the transition from secular to sacred state.
شفع (shaf‘): A pair of rak'ahs in a supererogatory prayer divided into two sets (shaf‘ awwal and shaf‘ thānī).
قضاء (qaḍā’): The compensatory performance of a prayer or its parts after its prescribed time due to omission or invalidation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a four-rak'ah supererogatory prayer, if a person recites only in the first two rak'ahs, which rak'ahs must he make up according to the Hanafi consensus?
A) The first two rak'ahs
B) The last two rak'ahs
C) All four rak'ahs
D) No qadā' is required

Key Takeaway
In a four-rak'ah nafl, omission of recitation in any rak'ah makes that shaf‘ defective, requiring qadā' of the entire shaf‘, with consensus on four specific patterns; the tahrīmah is only invalidated when recitation is completely absent from the first shaf‘.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Reciting in One of Each Pair
Presents the ikhtilāf among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on qadā' when recitation is in one rak'ah of each pair.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on qadā' when recitation is in one of each pair and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
When recitation is omitted in one rak'ah of each pair, Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf require qadā' of all four; Muhammad requires only the first two.

This passage delves into a nuanced intra-Hanafi disagreement: if a worshipper recites in exactly one rak'ah of the first pair and one of the second pair in a four-rak'ah nafl prayer, how many rak'ahs must be made up? The answer hinges on whether the opening takbir (taḥrīmah) remains valid for the entire prayer or is nullified by the omission in the first pair. Three distinct positions emerge among the Hanafi imams, each with different practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the case is a four-rak'ah supererogatory prayer where recitation (a wajib element) is performed in only one rak'ah of the first pair and one of the second pair.
2
State the three positions
List each view: (1) Abu Hanifa (well-known) and Abu Yusuf: qadā' of all four. (2) Muhammad: qadā' of only the first two. (3) Another narration from Abu Hanifa (reported by Abu Yusuf): qadā' of two rak'ahs.
The third position is disputed in transmission.
3
Understand the key reasoning
The difference turns on whether the taḥrīmah remains valid. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that recitation in one rak'ah of the first pair preserves the taḥrīmah, so the second pair is validly begun. Muhammad holds that omitting recitation in one rak'ah of the first pair invalidates the taḥrīmah entirely, nullifying the second pair.
4
Note the transmission dispute
Abu Yusuf denied the second narration from Abu Hanifa (the one requiring two rak'ahs), affirming that his own direct narration from Abu Hanifa requires four rak'ahs. Muhammad did not retract his view.
This affects authority weight.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The established position for fatwa is that of Abu Hanifa (well-known) and Abu Yusuf: qadā' of all four rak'ahs, as it is the majority view and more precautionary in worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قرأ في إحدى الأوليين وإحدى الأخريين على قول أبي يوسف قضاء الأربع وكذا عند أبي حنيفة لأن التحريمة باقية وعند محمد قضاء الأوليين لأن التحريمة قد ارتفعت عنده وقد أنكر أبو يوسف هذه الرواية عنه وقال رويت لك عن أبي حنيفة أنه يلزمه قضاء ركعتين ومحمد لم يرجع عن روايته عنه. ترجمہ: اور اگر اولین میں سے ایک میں اور آخریین میں سے ایک میں قرآت کی تو ابو یوسف کے نزدیک چار کی قضاء واجب ہے اور یوں ہی ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک۔ کیونکہ تحریمہ باقی ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اولین کی قضاء واجب ہے کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک تحریمہ مرتفع ہو گیا۔ امام ابو یوسف نے امام ابوحنیفہ سے اس روایت کا انکار کیا ہے اور ابویوسف نے کہا کہ میں نے تو ابو حنیفہ سے تم کو یہ روایت کی تھی کہ اس پر دو رکعت کی قضاء لازم ہوگی۔ اور امام محمد نے رجوع نہیں کیا ابویوسف کے ابوحنیفہ سے روایت کرنے سے۔
If he recited in one of the first two and one of the last two, then according to Abu Yusuf, qadā' of all four, and likewise according to Abu Hanifa, because the tahrīmah remains. According to Muhammad, qadā' of the first two, because the tahrīmah has been lifted with him. Abu Yusuf denied this narration from him and said: I narrated to you from Abu Hanifa that he is obligated to make up two rak'ahs, and Muhammad did not retract from his narration from him.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the fifth scenario: when the worshipper recites in exactly one rak'ah of the first pair and one rak'ah of the second pair. Three positions emerge: (1) According to Abu Yusuf and a narration from Abu Hanifa, qadā' of all four rak'ahs is required because the tahrīmah remains valid (since recitation was performed in one rak'ah of the first pair), so both shaf's were validly begun; the invalid rak'ahs (those without recitation) require qadā'. (2) According to Muhammad, only the first two rak'ahs need qadā', because he holds that the tahrīmah is invalidated when any rak'ah of the first pair lacks recitation; hence the first couplet was invalid and the second was never properly started. (3) Abu Yusuf disputes the attribution to Abu Hanifa, claiming he heard directly that Abu Hanifa said only two rak'ahs (not four) must be made up. The practical consequence is a three-way difference in the number of rak'ahs subject to qadā'. The authoritative position in the school is that of Abu Yusuf and the well-known narration from Abu Hanifa (four rak'ahs), as it is more precautionary and supported by the principle that the tahrīmah remains intact.

Key Terms
ترک قرآت (tark al-qirā’ah): Omitting the recitation of a sūrah (or verses) in a rak'ah, which is a wajib element in supererogatory prayers according to Hanafi fiqh.
ارتفاع تحریمہ (irtifā‘ al-taḥrīmah): The lifting or nullification of the opening takbir, meaning the prayer's commencement is invalidated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the first two rak'ahs
B) Only the last two rak'ahs
C) All four rak'ahs
D) No qadā' is required

Key Takeaway
When recitation is omitted in one rak'ah of each pair in a four-rak'ah supererogatory prayer, the mufta bihi view of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) requires qadā' of all four rak'ahs.

Qada for Nafal When Recitation Is Missed in Some Rak'ahs
Rulings on qada of rak'ahs when Quran is recited in some pairs but not others

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the ruling of qada for nafal when recitation is missed in some rak'ahs, distinguishing between the agreed scenarios and the disputed scenario, and explain the Hanafi ikhtilaf based on the status of tahrima.

Core Idea
In nafal prayer, missing recitation in an entire pair necessitates qada; partial missing triggers ikhtilaf on whether tahrima remains intact.

In nafal prayer, recitation is wajib in every rak'ah. When a person prays four rak'ahs (as two pairs) but fails to recite in one or more rak'ahs, the ruling on qada (making up the deficient part) varies. This passage from Al-Hidayah presents three scenarios: two by consensus and one where Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad differ. Understanding the role of the tahrima (the initial takbir) is key to following the ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage describes three ways recitation can be distributed across four rak'ahs of nafal (prayed as two pairs). List each scenario clearly.
Scenario A: recitation in first two and one of last two. Scenario B: recitation in last two and one of first two. Scenario C: recitation in one of first two and one of last two.
2
Understand the consensus on full pairs
Scenarios A and B are ruled by consensus (ijma). In each, the pair where recitation was missed entirely requires qada. Explain why the entire pair is deficient.
In A, the last two are deficient; in B, the first two are deficient. The other pair is complete because both its rak'ahs had recitation.
3
Analyze the disputed scenario (C) and the role of tahrima
In scenario C, each pair has one rak'ah with recitation and one without. The ikhtilaf hinges on whether the tahrima (prohibition of worldly actions) remains in effect for the second pair. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that tahrima remains, so both pairs are partially deficient, requiring qada of all four. Muhammad holds that missing recitation in a rak'ah of the first pair lifts the tahrima, invalidating the start of the second pair, so only the first pair needs qada.
The tahrima is a rukn; its invalidation nullifies the prayer's continuity.
4
Compare the proofs and the narration dispute
Abu Yusuf claimed he heard Abu Hanifa say qada of two rak'ahs, but Muhammad did not retract his own narration that Abu Hanifa said qada of four. Understand that this is a dispute over the exact transmission, not just the ruling.
This shows how riwayah (transmission) affects the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قرأ فى الأوليين واحدى الاخريين فعليه قضاء الاخريين بالاجماع ولو قرأ في الاخريين و احدى الاوليين فعليه قضاء الاوليين بالاجماع و لو قرأ فى احدى الاوليين واحدى الاخريين على قول ابي يوسف قضاء الاربع وكذا عند ابي حنيفة لأن التحريمة باقية وعند محمد قضاء الاوليين لان التحريمة قد ارتفعت عنده وقد انكر ابويوسف هذه الرواية عنه و قال رويت لك عن ابي حنيفة انه يلزمه قضاء ركعتين و محمد لم يرجع عن رواية عنه
If one recited in the first two and one of the last two, then upon him is qada of the last two by consensus. If one recited in the last two and one of the first two, then upon him is qada of the first two by consensus. If one recited in one of the first two and one of the last two: according to Abu Yusuf, qada of four; similarly according to Abu Hanifa because the tahrima remains; according to Muhammad, qada of the first two because the tahrima is lifted in his view. Abu Yusuf denied this narration from him and said: I narrated to you from Abu Hanifa that two rak'ahs of qada are obligatory upon him. Muhammad did not retract from the narration about him (i.e., from his own view).
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage presents three scenarios regarding qada (making up) of missed recitation in nafal prayer. The first two scenarios are agreed upon: if recitation is done in the first two rak'ahs and one of the last two, qada of the last two is wajib by consensus; similarly, if recited in the last two and one of the first two, qada of the first two is wajib. The third scenario is disputed: if recitation is in one rak'ah of the first pair and one rak'ah of the last pair, Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa rule qada of all four rak'ahs because the tahrima (prohibition of speaking) remains intact, so both pairs are valid but each has a missed wajib. Muhammad argues that missing recitation in a rak'ah of the first pair lifts the tahrima, invalidating the second pair's start, so only the first pair requires qada. Abu Yusuf claimed he heard Abu Hanifa say qada of two rak'ahs, but Muhammad insists on his own memory of the narration.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (tahrima): The initial takbir that begins the prayer and prohibits worldly actions; its validity is tied to the prayer's structure.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed wajib element of prayer; here it means repeating the deficient rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the third scenario (recitation in one of the first two and one of the last two), what is the ruling according to Imam Muhammad?
A) Qada of all four rak'ahs
B) Qada of the last two rak'ahs only
C) Qada of the first two rak'ahs only
D) No qada required

Key Takeaway
When recitation is missed in a nafal prayer of two pairs, if a complete pair is deficient, that pair requires qada by consensus; if the deficiency is split, the ruling depends on whether the tahrima remains — the Hanafi ikhtilaf on this point is preserved in the madhhab.
